Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
Intention in Hajj: The Exception to the General Rule
Explains the exception to the rule of intention for Hajj and Ibn al-Humam's deduction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on intention in Hajj, distinguishing when absolute intention suffices and when explicit intention of fard is required, and identify the underlying qawida and its istithna.

Core Idea
Hajj is valid with absolute intention, but if one intended nafl, the fard is not fulfilled.

In this lesson, we explore a unique Hanafi exception to the rule that acts common to fard and nafl require explicit intention of fard. The jurists held that Hajj is valid with absolute intention because the hardship it entails implies one must be performing it for fard. Ibn al-Humam refined this by demonstrating that if the person actually intended nafl, the Hajj does not discharge the obligation. This distinction hinges on the interplay between apparent circumstances (zahir) and internal reality (haqiqah).

Guided Path
1
State the general qawida
Recall the rule: An act suitable for both fard and nafl is not valid for fard without intending fard. Write down the qawida in Arabic and English.
The qawida is 'ما يصلح للفرض والنفل لا يصح إلا بنية الفرض'.
2
Identify the exception for Hajj
Note that Hajj is an exception: it is valid with absolute intention. The rationale is that no one undertakes such hardship for nafl. This exception is based on istihsan.
The exception is not a violation of the qawida but a recognition that the apparent circumstance (zahir) indicates fard intention.
3
Analyze Ibn al-Humam's deduction
Ibn al-Humam deduces that if a person internally intended nafl (not fard), the Hajj does not fulfill the fard. This is because the interpretation based on zahir is overridden by the explicit internal intention.
The deduction is consistent: absolute intention is interpreted as fard, but if the actual intention is otherwise, the internal reality prevails.
4
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider a person who has the obligatory Hajj due, enters ihram with absolute intention, but in his heart intends nafl. Determine the ruling using the two layers: external ruling (valid with absolute intention) vs. internal condition (intention of fard required).
The ruling: The Hajj is performed but counts as nafl; the fard remains unfulfilled.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Compare the Hanafi view with the Shafi'i view (which requires explicit intention of fard). Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) in fatwa.
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) due to istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْحَج فَقَدَّمْنَا أَنَّهُ يَصِحُ بِمُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ، وَلكِنْ عَلَلُوْهُ بِمَا يَقْتَضِي أَنَّهُ نَوَىٰ فِي نَفْسِ الْأمْرِ الْفَرْضِيَّةَ، قَالُوا : لأنَّهُ لَا يَتَحَمَّلُ الْمَشَاقَ الْكَثِيرَة إِلَّا لأجل الْفَرْضِ، فَاسْتَنْبَطَ مِنْهُ المُحَقِّقُ إبْنُ الْهُمَام أَنَّهُ لَوْ كَانَ الْوَاقِعُ مِنْهُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَنْوِ الْفَرْضَ لَمْ يَجُزُهُ؛ لِأَنَّ صَرْفَهُ إِلَى الْفَرْضِ حَمْلاً لَهُ عَلَيْهِ عَمَلاً بالظاهر ، وَهُوَ حَسَنٌ جِدًّا فَلَا بُدَّ فِيْهِ مِنْ نِيَّةِ الْفَرْضِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ نَوَى النَّفْلَ فِيْهِ، وَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةُ الإِسْلَامِ كَانَ نَفْلاً.
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال حج تو ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ وہ مطلق نیست سے بیچ ہو جاتا ہے لیکن فقہاء نے علت بیان کی ہے جو اس بات کو متقاضی ہے کہ فی نفس الامر میں اس نے فرضیت کی نیت کی ہے فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ اتنی زیادہ مشکلات فرض ہی کی وجہ سے برداشت کر سکتا ہے، تو اس سے محقق ابن ہمام نے مستنبط کیا ہے کہ اگر اس کی طرف سے واقعہ ایسا ہے کہ اس نے فرض کی نیت نہیں کی ہے تو جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس (مطلق نیت) کو فرض کی طرف پھیرنا (مطلق نیت) کو اس (فرض) پر محمول کرتے ہوئے (متعین ہے) ظاہر پر عمل کرتے ہوئے اور یہ بہت عمدہ ہے لہذا اس (حج) میں فرض کی نیت ضروری ہے اس لئے کہ اگر اس نے اس (حج) میں نفل کی نیت کی حالانکہ اس کے ذمہ حج فرض تھا تو وہ نفل ہوگا ۔ قدمنا الله ينصح بمطلق النبية اس میں قدمنا سے نشاب بمطلق النية نظراً إلى المعيارية كى طرف اشارہ ہے، صرف و حملا لہ میں ضمیر کا مرجع مطلق نیت ہے اور علیہ میں ضمیر کا مرجع الفرض ہے۔ اگر چہ حج مطلق نیت سے صحیح ہو جاتا ہے لیکن فی نفسہ اس میں بھی فرضیت کی نیت شرط ہے کیونکہ مطلق نیت سے صحیح ہونے کی علت فقہاء نے یہ ذکر کی ہے کہ اتنی بڑی مصیبتیں اور مشقتیں کوئی فرض کی ادائیگی کے لئے ہی برداشت کر سکتا ہے گو یا فقہاء نے ظاہر کو نفس الامر میں پائی جانے والی نیت کے درجہ میں رکھا ہے جیسا کہ اگلے مسئلہ میں مزید اس کی وضاحت ہوگی ۔ لو اطلق نية الحج بان احرم بحجه ولم يعين فرضاً ولا نفلاً صح احرامه للحج صرفه الى القرض استحساناً على المذهب . رقية جديد ص : ۸۰) اوپر ذکر کیا گیا کہ فی نفسہ حج میں بھی نیت شرط ہے لیکن فقہاء نے ظاہر کو اس کے قائم مقام رکھا ہے اس لئے علامہ ابن ہمام نے یہ مسئلہ مستنبط کیا ہے کہ اگر کسی پر حج فرض تھا اور اس نے حج کیا لیکن اس کی نیت نفل حج کرنے کی تھی تو فی الجملہ اس کی نیت کا اعتبار ہوگا اور حج فرض ادا نہ ہوگا۔
As for Hajj, we have previously stated that it is valid with absolute intention, but they have given a rationale that necessitates that he intended fardiyyah in the internal reality. They said: Because he would not bear such great hardships except for the sake of the fard. So from this, the verifying scholar Ibn al-Humam deduced that if the reality from him was that he did not intend fard, it would not be valid for him; because turning it to the fard (by interpreting the absolute intention) as acting upon the apparent (that he must have intended fard) is very good. Therefore, intention of fard is necessary in it; because if he intended nafl in it while he had the Hajjat al-Islam upon him, it would be nafl. Translation: And in any case, we have previously stated that Hajj is valid with absolute intention, but the jurists have stated a rationale that requires that internally he intended fard. The jurists say: He would not bear such great hardships except for the sake of fard. So from this, al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam deduced that if the reality from him was that he did not intend fard, it would not be valid; because turning this absolute intention to the fard (by interpreting the absolute intention) upon the apparent (that he intended fard) is very good. Therefore, intention of fard is necessary in it; because if he intended nafl in it while he had the obligatory Hajj upon him, it would be nafl. We previously indicated that Hajj is valid with absolute intention, with reference to the customary practice. The pronoun in 'hamlan lahu' refers to the absolute intention, and in 'alayhi' refers to the fard. Although Hajj is valid with absolute intention, in itself the intention of fard is a condition because the reason for its validity with absolute intention is that the jurists have stated that no one would bear such great difficulties except for the performance of fard. It is as if the jurists have placed the apparent in the position of the intention found in the internal reality, as will be further clarified in the next issue. 'If one makes an absolute intention of Hajj, i.e., he enters ihram with Hajj without specifying fard or nafl, his ihram is valid for Hajj and it is turned to the fard by istihsan according to the madhhab' (Raqiyya Jadid, p. 80). It was stated above that in itself, intention is also a condition in Hajj, but the jurists have placed the apparent in its place. Therefore, Allamah Ibn al-Humam deduced this issue: If someone had the obligatory Hajj upon him and he performed Hajj but his intention was to perform nafl Hajj, then definitely his intention will be considered and the fard Hajj will not be fulfilled.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a qawida application regarding intention in Hajj. The general rule is that for acts common to fard and nafl, intention of fard is required. However, for Hajj, there is a nuanced ruling: it is valid with absolute intention (without specifying fard or nafl). The jurists rationalize this by saying that a person would not undertake such severe hardships except for the fard. Therefore, Ibn al-Humam deduced that if a person actually intended nafl (not fard), the Hajj would not discharge the obligation – it would be counted as nafl. So even though the ruling is that absolute intention suffices, the underlying reality is that the person must have intended fard. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the absolute intention is interpreted as fard due to the apparent circumstances. This shows a delicate balance between zahir (apparent) and haqiqah (reality) in Hanafi usul. The quotation from Raqiyya Jadid confirms that the madhhab turns the absolute intention to fard by istihsan. Thus, while the external ruling is lenient, the internal condition of intention of fard remains.

Key Terms
مُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ (mutlaq al-niyyah): Absolute or general intention, without specifying whether the act is fard or nafl.
ظَاهِر (zahir): The apparent or external circumstances that indicate the person must have intended fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Humam, if a person has the obligatory Hajj upon him and he performs Hajj with absolute intention but internally intended nafl, what is the ruling?
A) The fard Hajj is fulfilled because absolute intention suffices.
B) The fard Hajj is not fulfilled; it is counted as nafl.
C) The Hajj is invalid.
D) He must repeat the Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is exceptional: absolute intention suffices, but if one intends nafl internally, the fard remains unfulfilled.

Intention of Fard for Kaffarat and Qada Fasts
States that for kaffarat and qada fasts, intention of fard is required from the night

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'ما يصلح للفرض والنفل لا يصح إلا بنية الفرض' to identify when a specific intention of fard is required for obligatory fasts.

Core Idea
An act that can be both fard and nafl requires intention of fard to be valid for the obligation.

In this lesson, we examine a key qawida about intention in fasting. The Hanafi school distinguishes between Ramadan fasts and other obligatory fasts (qada and kaffarah). While Ramadan fasts are automatically valid with the general intention of the month, qada and kaffarah fasts require explicit intention of fard from the night. This rule ensures that the obligation is clearly separated from optional acts, protecting the worshipper's intention.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Identify the Arabic text of the qawida and understand its plain meaning: 'An act suitable for both fard and nafl is not valid (for the fard) without intending fard.'
The maxim applies when the same time or action could be used for either obligation or supererogation.
2
Identify its scope
Understand that this qawida primarily governs the fiqh chapter of fasting (sawm), but analogous principles apply elsewhere. Note the dabt (restriction): Ramadan fasts are an exception.
The scope is limited to acts that are not inherently fixed as fard by the lawgiver.
3
Work through the furuat
Apply the qawida to the cases mentioned: kaffarah and qada fasts. Both require intention of fard from the night because the daytime is suitable for nafl fasts.
The ruling is that without specifying fard, the fast defaults to nafl.
4
Identify the istithna
Recognise that Ramadan fasts are an exception: they do not require intention of fard from the night because the obligation is divinely appointed and certain. The governing qawida for the exception is 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك'.
This exception is based on the strength of the obligation and the certainty of the time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَابُدَّ مِنْ نِيَّةِ الْفَرْضِ فِى الْكَفَّارَاتِ، وَلِذَا قَالُوا إِنَّ صَوْمَ الْكَفَّارَةِ وَقَضَاءَ رَمَضَانَ يَحْتَاجُ إلَى تَبْيْتِ النِّيَّةِ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ لِأَنَّ الْوَقْتَ صَالِحٌ لِصَوْمِ النَّفْلِ.
ترجمه : اور کفارات میں فرض کی نیت ضروری ہے اسی وجہ سے فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ کفارہ اور قضاء رمضان کے روزے میں رات سے نیت کی ضرورت ہے اس لئے کہ وقت نفل روزہ کا بھی احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ تشریح: قضا اور کفارہ کے روزوں میں رات سے نیت ضروری ہے تا کہ دیگر روزوں میں اور ان میں امتیاز ہو سکے مگر رمضان کے روزوں میں یہ اس لئے شرط نہیں ہے کہ وہ من جانب اللہ متعین ہونے کی وجہ سے اس سے متلی
And intention of fard is necessary in the kaffarat (expiation fasts). For this reason, they said: The fast of kaffarah and qada of Ramadan require the intention from the night, because the time is suitable for voluntary fasting. Translation: And in kaffarat, intention of fard is necessary. For this reason, the jurists say that in the fast of kaffarah and qada of Ramadan, intention from the night is required, because the time also has the possibility of voluntary fasting. Explanation: In qada and kaffarah fasts, intention from the night is necessary so that distinction can be made between them and other fasts. However, in the fasts of Ramadan, this is not a condition because they are determined by Allah (thus no need for specific intention).
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage applies the same qawida to kaffarat (expiation fasts) and qada of Ramadan fasts. The rule is that when the time (day) is suitable for both obligatory and voluntary fasting, one must specify intention from the night to distinguish which type is intended. Unlike Ramadan fasts, which are fard by default and the intention for the month itself suffices, these fasts require explicit intention from the night. The reasoning is that the time can host voluntary fasts, so without specifying, it is unclear which obligation is being fulfilled. This is a clear example of the general maxim: an act that can be both fard and nafl requires intention of fard.

Key Terms
تَبْيِتِ النِّيَّةِ (tabyit al-niyyah): Making the intention from the night (i.e., before dawn) for the next day's fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do kaffarah and qada fasts require intention from the night?
A) Because they are optional.
B) Because the time is also suitable for voluntary fasting, so specification is needed.
C) Because they are more difficult than Ramadan fasts.
D) Because the moon sighting is uncertain.

Key Takeaway
For qada and kaffarah fasts, intention of fard from the night is required because the time could otherwise be used for voluntary fasting; Ramadan fasts are exempt.

Intention of Obligation Not Required for Conditions
Expansion of the rule that shurut do not require niyyat al-fardiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that conditions (shurut) do not require intention of obligation (niyyat al-fardiyyah) and apply it to distinguish between acts that require tahsil vs husul.

Core Idea
For conditions of worship, only their occurrence matters, not the intention of obligation.

In Hanafi fiqh, not all acts require the same level of intention. While the ultimate acts of worship (maqsudah) often require niyyat al-fardiyyah, the means (wasail) and conditions (shurut) do not. This passage from the sharh expands the principle that for shurut, what matters is husul (occurrence), not tahsil (procuring with intention). Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary burden in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Find the statement 'إنما يراعي حصولها لا تحصيلها' (Only their occurrence is considered, not their procurement). This is the core principle governing conditions.
This applies to all shurut of worship.
2
Understand the rationale
Recognize that shurut are means (wasail), not ends. The intended act of worship is the end; the condition is a prerequisite. Since the condition's benefit is attained by its mere existence, intention specifying its obligation is not needed.
Ends vs means distinction is key in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply to wudu and ghusl
Both wudu and ghusl are conditions for prayer. The text states that intention is not required for them because their 'occurrence' suffices. The command is fulfilled regardless of whether one intended obligation.
This includes tayammum similarly.
4
Extend to other shurut
The text generalizes: all conditions (shurut) follow this rule. Examples: khutbah for Jumu'ah, funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) which is always obligatory, and even a child's prayer where obligation is not required.
Note: funeral prayer is never repeated as nafl, so no need to specify fardiyyah.
5
Recognize the furuat
The passage then discusses borderline cases: child's prayer (no fardiyyah because not obligatory for him), fard al-ayn vs fard kifayah (explicit intention apparently not required). These are furuat derived from the principle.
The author (Ibn Nujaym) notes he hasn't seen explicit rulings, but the principle suggests non-requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہیں اور نفل میں اس لئے شرط نہیں ہے کہ شارع علیہ السلام سے قبل نیت کے بغیر نفل روزہ رکھنا ثابت ہے۔ والقضاء والنذر المطلق والكفارات لا تصح الا بنية معينة من الليل.
(الدر المنتقى مع مجمع الانهر ج ۱، ص : ۳۰۷)
وَامَّا الْوُضُوْءُ وَالْغُسْلُ فَلَا دَخَلَ لَهُمَا فِى هَذَا الْمَبْحَثِ لِعَدَمِ إشْتِرَاطِ النِّيَّةِ فِيهِمَا ، وَأَمَّا التيمم فَلَاتُشْتَرَطُ لَهُ نِيَّةُ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ؛ لأنَّهُ مِنَ الْوَسَائِلِ، وَقَدَّمْنَا أَنَّ نِيَّةَ رَفْعِ الْحَدَثِ كَافِيَةٌ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال وضو اور غسل تو ان دونوں کا اس بحث سے کوئی تعلق نہیں ہے ان دونوں میں نیت کے شرط نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور بہر حال تیم تو اس کے لئے فرضیت کی نیت ضروری نہیں اس لئے کہ وہ وسائل میں سے ہے اور ہم نے پہلے بیان کر دیا کہ رفع حدث کی نیت کافی ہے۔
تشریح وضو اور غسل کا تعین نیت سے کچھ لینا دینا نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کا حصول ضروری ہے تحصیل ضروری نہیں ہے لہذا وضو اور غسل کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے۔
لان الماموربه ليس الا غسلا و مسحاً ربما تفيد هذه العبارة ان الوضوء الماموربه لا تشترط له النية قال الحموي و التحقيق ان الوضوء الماموربه ينادى بغير نية لان المامور به حصوله لا تحصيله (حاشیة الطحطاوي قديم ص: ۴۱) تیم میں بھی فرضیت کی نیت شرط نہیں ہے کیونکہ تیم وسائل میں سے ہے لہذا رفع حدث کی نیت اس میں کافی ہے۔ و أما التيمم فلا تشترط له نية الفرضة لانه من الوسائل وقدمنا ان نية رفع الحدث كافية (مراقی الفلاح على شرح نور الايضاح ص : ٦١ (قديم)
وَعَلى هذا الشُّرُوْطُ كُلُّهَا لَا تُشْتَرَطُ لَهَا نِيَّةُ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ لِقَوْلِهِمْ إِنَّمَا يُرَاعِي حُصُوْلُهَا لاَ تَحْصِيْلُهَا، وَكَذَا الْخُطْبَةُ لَا تُشْتَرَطُ لَهَا نِيَّةُ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ وَ إِنْ شَرَطْنَا لَهَا النِّيَّةَ لِأَنَّهَا لَا يُتَنَفَّلُ بِهَا، وَلِذَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ تَكُونَ صَلَاةُ الْجَنَازَةِ كَذلِكَ، لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَكُوْنَ إِلَّا قَرْضاً كَمَا صَرَّحُوْا بِهِ، وَلِذَا لَا تُعَادُ نَفْلًا، وَلَمْ أرَ حُكْمَ صَلَاةِ الصَّبِيِّ فِي نِيَّةِ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ، وَ يَنْبَغِي أَنَ لا تُشْتَرَطَ لِكَوْنِهَا غَيْرَ قَرْضٍ فِي حَقِّهِ، لكنْ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُنْوِى صَلَاةَ كَذَا، الَّتِي فَرَضَهَا اللهُ تَعَالَى عَلَى الْمُكَلَّفِ فِي هَذَا الْوَقْتِ، وَلَمْ أرَ  َأيْضاً حُكْمَ نِيَّةِ فَرْضِ الْعَيْنِ فِي فَرْضِ الْعَيْنِ، وَفَرْضِ الْكِفَايَةِ فِيهِ، وَالظَّاهِرُ عَدَمُ الاشْتِرَاط.
ترجمہ: اور اس پر جملہ شرطیں محمول میں کہ ان کے لئے فرضیت کی نیت شرط نہیں ہے بقول فقہاء کہ ان کا حصول ہے تحصیل مقصود نہیں اور ایسے ہی خطبہ اس کے لئے فرضیت کی نیت شرط نہیں ہے اگر چہ ہم نے اس کے لئے نیت کو شرط قرار دیا ہے اس لئے کہ وہ فرض ہوتی ہے جیسا کہ فقہاء نے صراحت کی اور اسی وجہ سے نقل نہیں ہوتی اور فرضیت کی نیت میں بچہ کی نماز کا حکم میں نے نہیں دیکھا اور مناسب ہے کہ شرط نہ ہو کیونکہ وہ اس کے حق میں فرض نہیں ہے لیکن مناسب ہے کہ نیت کرے اس نماز کی جس کو اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس وقت میں مکلف پر فرض کیا ہے اور میں نے فرض عین کی نیت کا حکم فرض عین میں اور فرض کفایہ کی نیت کا حکم فرض کفایہ میں بھی نہیں دیکھا اور ظاہر شرط نہ ہونا ہے۔ تشریح جو چیزیں عبادات کے لئے شرط ہیں بذات خود مقصود نہیں جیسے وضو غسل وغیرہ ان کو انجام دیتے وقت فرضیت کی نیت شرط نہیں ہے تحصیل یعنی وجود میں لانے کے لئے نیت فرضیت کی ضرورت ہے اور ان شرائط کا صرف حصول یعنی وجود میں آنا کافی ہے جن کے لئے فرضیت نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہوتی چونکہ یہ وسائل ہیں اور وسائل میں نیت ہی شرط نہیں چہ جائے کہ نیت فرضیت شرط ہو۔ قال الحموي و التحقيق ان الوضوء المامور به يتأدى بغير نية لان المامور به حصوله لا تحصيله كسائر الشروط (مراقی الفلاح على شرح نور الايضاح ص: ۴۱ قديم
وكذا الخطبة: خطبہ بذات خود واجب ہے اس لئے اس میں فرضیت کی نیت کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے البتہ عبادت مقصورہ میں سے ہونے کی وجہ سے نفس نیت ضروری ہے۔
ولذا ينبغي ان تكون صلاة الجنازة : عبادت مختلف اوصاف کے ساتھ متصف نہ ہو بلکہ اس کی ایک ہی صفت متعین ہو تو اس عبادت میں فرضیت کی نیت کی ضرورت ہی نہیں اگر کوئی شخص نماز جنازہ پڑھے تو اس کے اوپر اس میں بھی فرضیت کی نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے کیونکہ نیت تمیز کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور یہاں تمیز کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ نماز جنازہ ہمیشہ فرض ہی ہوتی ہے نفل کبھی نہیں ہوتی یہی وجہ ہے کہ نماز جنازہ بصورت نفل نہیں لوٹائی جاتی ہے، بلکہ اگر فاسد ہو جائے تو از سرنو ہی ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس کی فرضیت خود ہی متعین ہے نیت تعین کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے۔ ولم ار حکم صلاة الصبی: اس جگہ یہ مسئلہ مذکور ہے کہ بچہ نماز کی نیت کیسے کرے؟ علامہ ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ بچہ نماز کی نیت کیسے کرے، اس سلسلہ میں مجھے کوئی صریح حکم تو نہیں ملا لیکن مناسب یہ ہے کہ بچہ کے حق میں فرضیت کی نیت شرط نہیں ہونی چاہئے کیونکہ بچہ کے حق میں نماز فرض نہیں ہے، ہاں وہ اس طرح نیت کرے کہ اس وقت اللہ نے مکلف بندوں پر جو نماز فرض کی ہے میں وہ نماز پڑھ رہا ہوں ۔
. ولم ار حكم نية فرض العین: فرائض میں فرض عین اور فرض کفایہ کی نیت کرنا بھی ضروری ہے یا نہیں علامہ ابن نجیم المصری فرماتے ہیں کہ اس سلسلہ میں بھی مجھے کوئی حکم صراحت نہیں ملا لیکن ظاہراً یہی بات معلوم ہوتی ہے کہ فرض عین میں فرض عین کی اور فرض کفایہ میں فرض کفایہ کی صراحت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ میں
And for supererogatory, it is not required because it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) kept supererogatory fast without prior intention. And make-up fasts, absolute vows, and expiations are not valid except with a specific intention from the night. (al-Durr al-Muntaqa with Majma' al-Anhur, vol. 1, p. 307) As for wudu and ghusl, they have no connection to this discussion due to the absence of the condition of intention in them. And as for tayammum, the intention of obligation is not required for it because it is among the means, and we have stated that the intention to remove impurity is sufficient. Translation: ... Explanation: Wudu and ghusl have nothing to do with specifying intention because their occurrence is necessary, not their procuring; therefore intention is not a condition for wudu and ghusl. ... And based on this, all conditions are not required to have the intention of obligation, according to their statement: 'Only their occurrence is considered, not their procuring.' Similarly, the sermon does not require the intention of obligation, even if we require intention for it, because it cannot be performed as supererogatory. Hence, the funeral prayer should be similar, because it is only obligatory as they explicitly stated, and therefore it is not repeated as supererogatory. I have not seen the ruling of a child's prayer regarding the intention of obligation, and it should not be required because it is not obligatory for him. But he should intend the prayer that Allah has obligated upon the responsible person at this time. I also have not seen the ruling of the intention of fard al-ayn in fard al-ayn, and fard kifayah in it, and the apparent is non-requirement. ... Commentary: ... And likewise the sermon: ... Hence, the funeral prayer should be: ... And I have not seen the ruling of the child's prayer: ... And I have not seen the ruling of the intention of fard al-ayn: ...
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage discusses the rule that for conditions (shurut) of worship, the intention of obligation (niyyat al-fardiyyah) is not required. It begins by referencing the ruling on fasting: voluntary fasts do not require prior intention, while obligatory fasts require a specific intention from the night. Then it moves to wudu and ghusl: these are conditions for prayer, but they are not intended as acts of worship in themselves; their mere occurrence (husul) is sufficient, not their procurement (tahsil). Therefore, intention is not required for them. Tayammum is similar because it is a means (wasilah); the intention to remove ritual impurity suffices. The text generalizes: all conditions (shurut) do not require intent of obligation, because only their occurrence matters, not their procurement. The sermon (khutbah) also does not require intent of obligation, though intention is still required because it is a specific act. The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is always obligatory, never supererogatory, so there is no need to specify obligation in intention. For a child's prayer, since it is not obligatory for him, intention of obligation is not required, but he should intend the obligatory prayer of that time. Finally, for fard al-ayn and fard kifayah, explicit intention of their category is apparently not required. The text cites authorities like al-Hamawi and Ibn Nujaym.

Key Terms
نية الفرضية (niyyat al-fardiyyah): Intention that an act is obligatory (fard) — required for some acts but not for conditions.
شرط (shart): Condition that is not the ultimate goal but a prerequisite for validity of worship.
حصول (husul): Occurrence or existence of the condition, as opposed to its procurement (tahsil).
تحصيل (tahsil): Procuring or bringing about intentionally; not required for conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, is the intention of obligation (niyyat al-fardiyyah) required for performing wudu?
A) Yes, it is required because wudu is an act of worship.
B) No, it is not required because wudu is a condition (shart) and its mere occurrence suffices.
C) Yes, it is required only for obligatory acts.
D) No, intention is never required for any act.

Key Takeaway
Conditions of worship require only occurrence, not intention of obligation — a key Hanafi principle for ease.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
6 min
Intention of Obligation Not Required for Means (Wasail)
Explaining that intention of obligatoriness is not required for wudu, ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that intention of faradiyyah is not required for preparatory acts (wasail) and distinguish between means and ends in worship.

Core Idea
For means, only occurrence matters, not intention of obligation.

This passage explains a foundational principle: acts that are conditions for worship, like wudu and ghusl, do not require the intention that they are obligatory. The reason is that they are means (wasail), not ends. For means, only their actual occurrence (husul) is required, not the intention of acquisition (tahsil). This lesson will help you understand and apply this important distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qawida
State the maxim in Arabic and English: 'لا تشترط نية الفرضية في وسائل العبادات' - 'Intention of obligatoriness is not required in means of worship.' Recognize that this is a sub-maxim (dabt) restricting the general rule that intention is required for acts of worship.
The qawida applies specifically to preparatory acts, not to the acts themselves (ghayat).
2
Understand the Rationale
Distinguish between husul (occurrence) and tahsil (acquisition). For means, the Shariah only commands the occurrence of the act, not the intention of fulfilling a command. This is based on the nature of means: they are not the goal, so the intention of obligation is not relevant.
The passage cites al-Hamawi: 'the commanded thing is its occurrence, not its acquisition.'
3
Examine the Furu' (Applications)
Apply the maxim to wudu, ghusl, and other conditions like tayammum. In each case, the intention of faradiyyah is not required. However, for the actual prayer (salat), which is an end, intention of obligation is required.
Other schools may differ; this is the Hanafi position.
4
Recognize the Scope
Identify which acts are considered wasail (means) and which are ghaayat (ends). Wasail include wudu, ghusl, removing najasah, covering awrah, etc. Ends include prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj. The boundary is whether the act is primarily a condition for another act.
Some acts may have dual nature, e.g., ghusl for janabah is both a condition for prayer and an ibadah itself; but the Hanafi view treats it as a means for prayer.
5
Apply to a New Case
Consider tayammum: does it require intention of faradiyyah? According to this qawida, no, because it is also a means. But note that tayammum has its own conditions; the principle remains consistent.
Always check the specific rulings for each means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح جو چیزیں عبادات کے لئے شرط ہیں بذات خود مقصود نہیں جیسے وضو غسل وغیرہ ان کو انجام دیتے وقت فرضیت کی نیت شرط نہیں ہے تحصیل یعنی وجود میں لانے کے لئے نیست فرضیت کی ضرورت ہے اور ان شرائط کا صرف حصول یعنی وجود میں آنا کافی ہے جن کے لئے فرضیت نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہوتی چونکہ یہ وسائل ہیں اور وسائل میں نیت ہی شرط نہیں چہ جائے کہ نیت فرضیت شرط ہو۔ قال الحموي و التحقيق ان الوضوء المامور به يتأدى بغير نية لان المامور به حصوله لا تحصيله كسائر الشروط (مراقی الفلاح على شرح نور الايضاح ص: ۴۱ قديم
Explanation: Those things which are conditions for worship are not intended by themselves, like wudu and ghusl. At the time of performing them, the intention of obligatoriness is not a condition. Because the intent of obligatoriness is needed for tahsil (bringing into existence), not for husul (occurrence). And for these conditions, only their occurrence (coming into existence) is sufficient, because they are means. And in means, intention itself is not a condition, let alone intention of obligatoriness being a condition. Al-Hamawi said: The verification is that the commanded wudu is performed without intention, because the commanded thing is its occurrence, not its acquisition, like all other conditions. (Maraqi al-Falah, Sharh Nur al-Idah, p.41, old edition)
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage expounds a foundational rule: for acts that are preparatory conditions (shurut) for worship, such as wudu and ghusl, the intention of the obligatory nature of the act itself is not required. The commentary explains the reasoning: these acts are means (wasail), not ends. For means, the Shariah only requires their actual occurrence (husul), not the intention of fulfillment. This is unlike the principle for ends, where the intention of the commanded act (with its obligation status) is required. The commentary then cites al-Hamawi, who affirms that wudu is performed without intention because the commanded thing is the occurrence of the act, not the intention of the obligatoriness. This is a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
وسائل (wasaa'il): Means or preparatory acts that are not ends in themselves, like wudu and ghusl.
شرط (shart): A conditional element that must exist for worship to be valid.
فرضیت (faradiyyah): The legal quality of being obligatory (fard).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is intention of faradiyyah not required for wudu?
A) Because wudu is not an act of worship
B) Because wudu is a means, and for means only occurrence is required
C) Because intention is never required for any act
D) Because the Prophet said so

Key Takeaway
Intention of obligatoriness is not required for means of worship; only their occurrence matters.

Khutbah and Janazah: No Need for Faradiyyah Niyyah
Expanding a qawida to two new furuʿ: khutbah and janazah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'niyyah is for distinction' to determine when intention of obligation is not required, and construct a fatwa on a novel case using this principle.

Core Idea
When worship has only one possible ruling, intention for its status is unnecessary—intention is for distinction, not obligation.

The preceding discussion established that for acts like wudu, which are always fard, one need not intend 'fard' in the niyyah. This lesson extends that principle to two more acts: the Friday sermon (khutbah) and the funeral prayer (janazah). The reasoning is the same: these acts have a fixed, unambiguous obligation status, so the intention does not need to specify that they are obligatory. Instead, only the general intention to perform the worship is required. Understanding this principle helps a mufti avoid imposing unnecessary conditions on valid worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying qawida
The lesson applies the maxim that intention (niyyah) is for distinguishing (tamyiz) between different types or rulings of acts of worship. When an act has only one possible legal status (e.g., always fard), no distinction is needed, so no need to specify that status in the intention.
The maxim is derived from the broader principle: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' but specifically focused on niyyah's role.
2
Classify the worship's ruling variance
Determine whether the act can be performed in more than one legal category (e.g., fard/nafl, wajib/nafl). If it is always the same, then the intention of that category is superfluous.
Khutbah is always wajib; janazah is always fard kifayah.
3
Rule on the need for faradiyyah niyyah
If the act's category is fixed and never changes, one does not need to intend 'I am performing this as fard/wajib' because there is no ambiguity to remove.
This does not negate the general intention to perform the act itself; that is still required.
4
Apply to the given furuʿ
The text applies the rule to khutbah (wajib) and janazah (fard). In both cases, the intention of obligation is not needed.
For khutbah, the intention of 'khutbah' itself suffices; for janazah, intention to pray for the deceased is enough.
5
Construct the fatwa response
When a questioner asks whether a specific intention is required, a mufti can cite this principle to answer that no, if the act's ruling is determinate, the intention of its category is not needed.
Always confirm that the act indeed has only one possible ruling in the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا الخطبة: خطبہ بذات خود واجب ہے اس لئے اس میں فرضیت کی نیت کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے البتہ عیادت مقصورہ میں سے ہونے کی وجہ سے نفس نیت ضروری ہے۔ ولذا ينبغي ان تكون صلاة الجنازة : وعبادت مختلف اوصاف کے ساتھ متصف نہ ہو بلکہ اس کی ایک تی صفت متعین ہو تو اس عبادت میں فرضیت کی نیت کی ضرورت ہی نہیں اگر کوئی شخص نماز جنازہ پڑھے تو اس کے اوپر اس میں بھی فرضیت کی نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے کیونکہ نیت تمیز کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور یہاں تمیز کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ نماز جنازہ ہمیشہ فرض ہی ہوتی ہے نقل کبھی نہیں ہوتی یہی وجہ ہے کہ نماز جنازہ بصورت نفل نہیں لوٹائی جاتی ہے، بلکہ اگر فاسد ہو جائے تو از سرنو ہی ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس کی فرضیت خود ہی متعین ہے نیت تعین کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے۔
And similarly the khutbah: The khutbah is itself wajib, so there is no need for intention of faradiyyah in it. However, because it is part of the intended worship, the intention itself is necessary. Hence it is proper that the janazah prayer: If an act of worship is not described with different attributes but rather its singular attribute is determinate, then in that worship there is no need for intention of faradiyyah. If someone performs the janazah prayer, it is not necessary for him to intend faradiyyah in it, because intention is for distinguishing, and here there is no need for distinction because the janazah prayer is always fard, it is never nafl. This is why the janazah prayer is not repeated as nafl; rather if it becomes invalid, it is done anew. So its obligatoriness is itself determinate; there is no need for intention of determination.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage applies the same principle to two other acts: khutbah (Friday sermon) and salat al-janazah (funeral prayer). The khutbah is inherently wajib (obligatory), so one does not need to intend its obligatoriness separately; however, because it is an act of worship, the basic intention to perform it is still required. For the janazah prayer, it is always fard kifayah and never performed as nafl; therefore, since there is no ambiguity about its status, intention of determination (that it is fard) is not needed. The commentary emphasizes that intention serves to distinguish between different types of worship, and when there is only one possible status, the distinction is unnecessary.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khutbah): The Friday sermon delivered before Friday prayer.
صلاۃ الجنازۃ (salat al-janazah): Funeral prayer performed over the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is intention of faradiyyah not required for janazah prayer?
A) Because it is not an act of worship
B) Because it is always fard and never nafl, so no distinction needed
C) Because the deceased does not need it
D) Because the intention is made by the deceased's family

Key Takeaway
Intention is for distinguishing between different rulings; when an act is always fard/wajib, no need to intend its obligatoriness in the niyyah.

Intention of Faradiyyah Not Required for Child's Prayer
Ruling on child's prayer and faradiyyah intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that intention of obligation (faradiyyah) is not required when the act is not obligatory, using the case of a child's prayer as a furu'.

Core Idea
Intention of obligation is only meaningful when the act itself is obligatory.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's commentary addresses a subtle point: how should a child who has not reached puberty intend prayer? Since prayer is not fard (obligatory) upon the child, requiring him to intend faradiyyah (that it is obligatory) would be inappropriate. Instead, the child should intend the specific prayer as the one Allah made fard on obligated adults. This ruling illustrates a broader qawida (legal maxim) that ties the requirement of intention to the existence of obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage asks: how should a child intend prayer? The issue is whether intention of faradiyyah is required.
The child is a non-obligated person (ghayr mukallaf).
2
Analyse the commentator's reasoning
Ibn Nujaym uses talil (reasoning): since prayer is not fard on the child, faradiyyah intention is meaningless and thus not a condition.
The illah (cause) is the absence of obligation.
3
Extract the qawida
The underlying maxim is: 'Intention of obligation is conditional upon the act being obligatory.' In Arabic: لا تشترط نية الفرضية إلا في الفرض.
This is a wusta (intermediate) qawida in Hanafi legal theory.
4
Apply the qawida to the furu'
The child's prayer is a furu' (derived case). The qawida dictates that faradiyyah intention is not a condition; the child's prayer is valid with a general intention.
The child should intend: 'I am praying the Zuhr prayer which Allah made fard upon the obligated.'
5
Determine the mufta bihi
This ruling from Ibn Nujaym is the relied-upon position in the later Hanafi school. It aligns with the principle that obligation precedes intention.
No contrary view is mentioned; this is the operative fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم ار حکم صلاة الصبی: اس جگہ یہ مسئلہ مذکورہے کہ بچہ نماز کی نیت کیسے کرے؟ علامہ ابن نجیم لمصر ٹی اس کے بارے میں فرماتے ہیں کہ بچہ نماز کی نیت کیسے کرے، اس سلسلہ میں مجھے کوئی صریح حکم تو نہیں ملا لہ منساب یہ ہے کہ بچہ کے حق میں فرضیت کی نیت شرط نہیں ہونی چاہئے کیونکہ بچہ کے حق میں نماز فرض نہیں ہے، ہاں وہ ان طرح نیت کرے کہ اس وقت اللہ نے مکلف بندوں پر جو نماز فرض کی ہے میں وہ نماز پڑھ رہا ہوں ۔
And I have not seen the ruling for the prayer of a child: Here this issue is mentioned: how should a child intend prayer? Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says regarding this: How should a child intend prayer? I have not found a clear ruling in this matter. But what is appropriate is that intention of faradiyyah should not be a condition for the child, because prayer is not fard upon the child. Yes, he should intend in this way: 'I am performing the prayer which Allah has made fard upon the obligated servants at this time.'
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific sub-case: the prayer of a child who has not reached puberty. Since fard is not obligatory on the child, requiring him to intend that his prayer is fard does not make sense. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, states that he found no explicit ruling, but the appropriate view is that the child does not need to intend faradiyyah. Instead, the child should intend the specific prayer (e.g., Zuhr) with the general intention that it is the prayer Allah made obligatory on Muslims. This aligns with the principle that intention of obligation is only meaningful where obligation exists.

Key Terms
صبی (sabi): A minor child who has not reached puberty. In Hanafi fiqh, acts of worship performed by a child are valid and rewarded, but not obligatory.
فرضیت (faradiyyah): The quality of being fard (obligatory). Intention of faradiyyah means the worshipper intends that the act is being performed as an obligation.
نیت (niyyah): Intention; the mental resolve to perform a specific act of worship for the sake of Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because prayer is not fard upon the child
C) Because the child is too young to make a valid intention

Key Takeaway
A child's prayer is valid without intending faradiyyah because intention of obligation is conditional on the act being obligatory.

Intention for Repeated Prayer (I'ada) Due to Makruh or Wajib Omission
Determining whether the repeated prayer requires intention of faradiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal nature of a repeated prayer (i'ada) and apply the correct intention based on the Hanafi preferred view.

Core Idea
The repeated prayer for deficiency is compensatory nafl (jabirah), not a new fard; intend reparation, not faradiyyah.

This lesson examines a nuanced issue: when a prayer is repeated due to a makruh or wajib omission, what intention should one make? Hanafi jurists have different views, but the preferred position clarifies that the repeated act is a compensatory nafl, not a separate fard. Understanding this requires distinguishing between the act's legal nature and the worshipper's intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause of repetition
Determine whether the first prayer had a makruh tahrimi (e.g., delaying beyond time) or omitted a wajib (e.g., leaving witr). The cause affects the ruling of the repetition itself.
The repetition's own ruling (wajib, sunnah, mustahabb) is separate from its legal nature.
2
Determine the legal nature of the repeated prayer
According to the majority (Haskafi, Ibn Nujaym), the first prayer fulfills the fard obligation, but since it was defective, the repetition is a compensatory nafl (jabirah). The alternative views either consider it a new fard or both as fard.
The majority view is mufta bihi.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule: fard drops with first
The principle that the fard obligation is discharged by the first prayer (even if defective) means the second prayer cannot be fard. Therefore, the second prayer is nafl, but with the specific purpose of reparation.
This is based on the jurists' statement 'the fard drops with the first'.
4
Extract the required intention
Since the act is nafl, one should not intend 'fard'. Instead, the correct intention is to make up for the deficiency in the original fard. The text says: 'one intends that it is a reparation for the deficiency'.
Intending nafl with the specific purpose is sufficient; faradiyyah intention is not required in the majority view.
5
Note the furuat (subsidiary rulings)
The passage ends with a general rule: repetition is wajib if due to leaving a wajib, sunnah if for leaving a sunnah, and mustahabb if for a makruh tanzihi. This shows how the qa'ida generates multi-level rulings.
These are practical consequences (thamarah) of the cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الصَّلَاةُ المُعَادَةُ لإِرْتِكَابِ مَكْرُوْهِ، أَوَ تَرْكِ وَاجِبٍ: فَلَاشَكَّ أَنَّهَا جَابِرَةٌ، لَا فَرْضٌ لِقَوْلِهِمْ بِسُقُوْطِ الْفَرْضِ بِالأوْلى فَعَلَى هَذَا يَنْوِي كَوْنَهَا جَائِزَةٌ لِنَقْضِ الْقَرْضِ عَلَىٰ أَنَّهَا نقل تحقيقاً وَأمَّا عَلَى الْقَوْلِ : بأن القَرْضَ يَسْقُطُ بِهَا، فَلَاحِفَاءَ فِي اشْتِرَاطِ نِيَّةِ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال وہ نماز جولوٹائی جائے کسی مکروہ کے ارتکاب یا ترک واجب کی وجہ سے تو کوئی شک نہیں کہ نقص کو پوری کرنے والی ہے فرض نہیں ہے فقہاء کے کہنے کی وجہ سے کہ فرض پہلی سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے تو اس کے لئے نیت کرے گا کہ وہ فرض کی کمی کو پورا کرنے والی ہے اس بناء پر کہ وہ حقیقت میں نفل ہے اور بہر حال اس قول پر کہ اس کے ذریعہ فرض ساقط ہوتا ہے، تو خفا نہیں فرضیت کی نیت کے شرط ہونے میں۔ تشریح اگر کوئی نماز مکروہ تحریمی کے ارتکاب یا ترک واجب کی وجہ سے لوٹائی جارہی ہے تو دوسری نماز میں کیا نیت ہونی چاہئے تو اس کا دارو مدار اس بات پر ہے کہ دوسری نماز کی حیثیت کیا ہے ایک فریق کی رائے یہ ہے کہ پہلی نماز فرض تھی جس سے فرض ساقط ہو گیا البتہ اس میں کچھ کمی واقع ہو گئی تھی اس کمی اور نقص کو پورا کرنے کے لئے نماز کا اعادہ کیا جارہا ہے لہذا اس میں یہ نیت کی جائے گی کہ میں فرض میں نقصان کی تلافی کے لئے نماز پڑھ رہا ہوں اس لئے کہ فرض تو نماز اول سے ساقط ہو گیا اور یہ دوسری نماز اصل میں نفل ہے جس کا مقصد نقصان فرض کی تلافی ہے جیسا کہ علامہ حصکفی اور ابن نجیم نے تصریح کی ہے۔ دوسرے فریق کی رائے یہ ہے کہ دوسری نماز ہی اصل نماز ہے اس قول کی بنیاد پر دوسری نماز میں فرضیت کی نیت ضروری ہوگی چونکہ اول نماز میں خلل پیدا ہو گیا جس کی وجہ سے وہ اصل نماز نہ رہی۔ علامہ شامی کی رائے یہ ہے کہ دونوں نمازوں کی حیثیت فرض کی ہے لیکن پہلی نماز فرض ناقص ہے اور دوسری نماز فرضِ کامل ہے۔ (کم ہونہ کورفی شامی زکریا ۲ ج:۵۲۲) فائده: الاعادة ان كانت لترك واجب فواجبة وان كانت لترك سنة فسنة وان كانت لارتكاب مكروه تنزيهى فمستحب.
And as for the repeated prayer due to committing a makruh or leaving a wajib: there is no doubt that it is compensatory (jabirah), not fard, because of their saying that the fard drops with the first. On this basis, one intends that it is a reparation for the deficiency of the fard, on the basis that it is truly nafl. And on the opinion that the fard drops by it, then there is no hiddenness in the condition of intention of faradiyyah. Translation: And anyway, the prayer that is repeated due to committing a makruh or leaving a wajib, there is no doubt that it is reparative, not fard, because of the jurists' statement that the fard drops with the first. So for it, one will intend that it is fulfilling the deficiency of the fard, on the basis that it is actually nafl. And on the opinion that the fard drops by it, then it is not hidden that intention of faradiyyah is a condition. Explanation: If a prayer is repeated due to committing a makruh tahrimi or leaving a wajib, then what intention should be in the second prayer? This depends on the nature of the second prayer. One view is that the first prayer was fard and the fard dropped, but there was some deficiency; this repetition is to cover that deficiency. Therefore one should intend: 'I am praying to compensate for the deficiency in the fard,' because the fard dropped with the first prayer, and this second prayer is actually nafl whose purpose is to compensate the deficiency, as specified by Allamah al-Haskafi and Ibn Nujaym. The second view is that the second prayer itself is the original prayer. Based on this, intention of faradiyyah is necessary in the second prayer because the first prayer had a defect and thus it is no longer the original. Allamah al-Shami's view is that both prayers are fard: the first is an incomplete fard and the second is a complete fard. (as in al-Shami Zakariya 2:522) Benefit: The repetition, if it is for leaving a wajib, is wajib; if for leaving a sunnah, it is sunnah; if for committing a makruh tanzihi, it is mustahabb.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage addresses the intention for a prayer that is repeated (i'ada) because the first was performed with a makruh tahrimi (e.g., delaying beyond time) or with the omission of a wajib (e.g., missing a witr). The ruling depends on the legal nature of the repeated prayer. The majority view (adopted by al-Haskafi and Ibn Nujaym) is that the first prayer fulfills the fard obligation, but since it was defective, the repetition is a compensatory nafl (jabirah). Therefore, the worshipper should intend it as a reparation for the deficiency, not as a fard. A minority view holds that the second prayer replaces the first as the actual fard, so intention of faradiyyah is required. A third view by al-Shami considers both as fard, but the first is defective and the second perfect. The passage also notes a general rule: the repetition is wajib if due to leaving a wajib, sunnah if for leaving a sunnah, and mustahabb if for a makruh tanzihi. This highlights the application of the overarching principle that intention of obligation is tied to the act's actual legal status.

Key Terms
اعادہ (i'ada): Repeating a prayer due to a deficiency in the first performance.
جابرہ (jabirah): A compensatory act that makes up for a deficiency in an obligatory act.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An act that is prohibited but not with the force of haram; it is close to haram and requires repetition if it occurs in prayer.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory element whose omission in prayer requires compensation (sajdah sahw) or repetition if missed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the repetition itself if it is due to leaving a wajib?
A) It is fard.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is sunnah.
D) It is mustahabb.

Key Takeaway
The repeated prayer for a makruh or wajib omission is a compensatory nafl (jabirah), not a new fard, and the intention should be for reparation, not faradiyyah.

Intention of Ada vs Qada: The Principle from Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha
Examples of the maxim applied to time-specific acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to cases where the worshipper's intention for ada or qada is mistaken, and state the Hanafi ruling on validity.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, the essential intention is the specific act, not whether it is ada or qada.

When a worshipper intends to pray Zuhr but misjudges the time, does the prayer count? This lesson applies the major maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to clarify that the intention of the specific obligatory worship suffices; the mistake in specifying ada or qada is excused. We examine examples from prayer, fasting, and Hajj as presented in the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify each case in the passage
List the four distinct scenarios given: (1) person prays with ada intention but time has ended, (2) prisoner fasts with ada intention uncertainty, (3) person prays with qada intention but time remains, (4) prisoner fasts in Ramadan with qada intention. Also note the Hajj rule.
2
Determine the intention and actuality
For each case, note what the worshipper intended (ada or qada) and what actually occurred (time status).
3
Extract the ruling from the passage
The passage states each worship is valid as the actual status (e.g., ada prayer becomes qada if time passed) because the essential intention of the specific worship was present.
The mistake is in the non-essential temporal specification.
4
Generalise the principle
What matters is the intention of the type of worship (e.g., Zuhr, Ramadan fast); specifying ada or qada is not required for validity.
This is a direct application of 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
5
Connect to the maxim
The ruling follows the true intention (the specific act), not the mistaken label of ada/qada. The maxim teaches that the actual purpose governs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بت کی تو اس مثال میں قضاء بہ نیت اور پائی گئی۔بعد اور گمان یہ ہے کہ ابھی وقت باقی ہے تو اس کی یہ نماز قضا ہوئی اور اس نے یہ مجھ کر پڑھی ہے کہ وقت باقی ہے تو ادا کی وكنية الاسير : کوئی شخص قید میں تھا اور وہ دنیا کے حالات سے بالکل بے خبر تھا اس نے محض تحری اور اندازہ کر کے روزے رکھے اس نے یہ روزے ادا کی نیت سے رکھے تھے لیکن اس کے یہ روزے رمضان کے مہینہ کے بعد رکھے گئے یا بعض رمضان کے مہینہ میں اور بعض بعد میں تو اس کے روزے بیچ ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ اس نے ادا کی نیت سے پاروزے رکھے ہیں ۔ و عكسه كنية من نوى : اگر کسی نے ادا نماز قضاء کی نیت سے پڑھی یہ سمجھ کر کہ وقت نکل چکا ہے حالانکہ باقی خان اس کی نماز درست ہو جائے گی اور سیادا نیت قضاء کی مثال ہے۔وكنية الاسير الذی صام رمضان کسی قیدی نے علم نہ ہونے پر رمضان کے مہینہ میں قضاء کی نیت سے روزے رکھے تو اس کے یہ روزے رمضان کے اداروزوں میں شمار ہوں گے، کیونکہ اصل نیت پائی گئی لیکن گمان کی وجہ سے اس سے خطا ہو گئی اور اس جیسی خطا معاف ہے۔والصحة فيه: مذکورہ جزئیات میں اصل عبادت اور تعیین فرضیت کی نیت پائی گئی جوضروری ہے اور اداو قضاء کی نیت ضروری نہیں ہے، اور جو چوک ہوئی ہے اس میں ہوئی ہے جو غیر لازم تھی اس لئے وہ چوک مصنر نہیں ہے۔ راما الحج حج میں ادا اور قضاء کی تعیین ضروری نہیں ، کوئی شخص حج کی نیت کرے تو نیت میں اداء حج یا قضاء ج کی مین شرط نہیں ہے لہذا ا دا اور قضاء میں تمیز کرنے کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے۔
In this example of the idol, the qada prayer was intended and found. The doubt and assumption is that time remains, so his prayer became qada and he recited it thinking time remains, so it is ada. And the intention of the prisoner: A person was imprisoned and completely unaware of the world's conditions; he estimated and assumed and fasted. He intended these fasts as ada, but his fasts were kept after the month of Ramadan or partly in Ramadan and partly after, so his fasts will be valid [?] because he intended ada. And its opposite: the intention of one who intends: If someone prayed a current prayer with the intention of qada, thinking that time had passed, while in fact time remained, his prayer will be valid and it is an example of current with qada intention. And the intention of the prisoner who fasted Ramadan: A prisoner, due to ignorance, fasted in Ramadan with the intention of qada, then his fasts will count as the fasts of Ramadan, because the essential intention was found, but he erred due to assumption, and such an error is forgiven. And the validity therein: In the mentioned examples, the essential worship and the intention of determining the obligatory nature were found, which is necessary, and the intention of ada or qada is not necessary. And the mistake that occurred was in something non-essential, so that mistake is harmless. As for Hajj, in Hajj, specifying ada or qada is not necessary. If a person intends Hajj, it is not a condition in the intention to specify whether it is ada of Hajj or qada. Therefore, distinguishing between ada and qada in intention is not a condition.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the maxim 'Actions are judged by intentions' (الأمور بمقاصدها) applied to the distinction between current (ada) and make-up (qada) acts of worship. The author provides several examples. First, a person prays thinking it is still within the prayer time (intending ada), but the time has actually ended: the prayer counts as qada because the essential intention was to perform that specific prayer. Second, a prisoner who, due to ignorance of dates, intends ada for fasts that turn out to be after Ramadan or partly in and partly out: his fasts are valid as ada? Actually the text says they will be 'بیچ' (maybe 'valid'?) The author states they are valid because he intended ada. Third, the opposite: someone prays with qada intention thinking time is gone, but time remains: the prayer is valid as ada. Fourth, a prisoner in Ramadan intends qada but the fasts actually fall in Ramadan: they count as Ramadan fasts. The general principle drawn is that what is essential is the intention of the specific obligatory act (e.g., the Zuhr prayer, the Ramadan fasts); whether one specifies ada or qada is not required. The mistake in the non-essential aspect does not harm. Finally, for Hajj, no distinction between ada and qada is needed in intention at all. This is a Hanafi position: the intention of the type of worship suffices; the determination of time is not a condition for validity.

Key Terms
ادا (ada): Performance of an act of worship within its designated time.
قضاء (qada): Performance of an act of worship after its designated time as a make-up.
نیّت (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone prays a current prayer with the intention of qada, thinking time has passed, but time actually remains?
A) The prayer is invalid because intention did not match reality.
B) The prayer is valid as ada.
C) The prayer is valid as qada because that was the intention.
D) The prayer must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Intention of the specific obligatory act (e.g., Zuhr, Ramadan fast) suffices; specifying ada or qada is not required for validity in Hanafi fiqh.

The Maxim: No Riya in Obligatory Acts (La Riya fi al-Fara'id)
Discussion on sincerity, hadith on riya, and scholars' views on riya in faraid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim 'la riya fi al-fara'id', apply it to distinguish between obligatory and voluntary acts, and evaluate the differing scholarly opinions on the effect of riya.

Core Idea
Riya does not invalidate obligatory acts, but destroys reward — a key Hanafi distinction.

This passage presents a crucial Hanafi maxim: 'There is no riya (show-off) in obligatory acts.' While sincerity (ikhlas) is required for full reward, the validity of obligatory acts is not nullified by the presence of riya. The author supports this with a hadith and a scholarly dispute, ultimately affirming the relied-upon position that riya does not prevent the obligation from being fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim
Locate the maxim in the text: 'لا رياء في الفرائض' (no riya in obligatory acts). Understand its scope: it applies to all obligatory acts, not voluntary ones.
The maxim is stated in al-Khulasa and endorsed by later Hanafi authorities.
2
Examine the Supporting Evidence
Read the hadith from Tirmidhi about the 'pit of sorrow' for those who show off. This highlights the severity of riya and the need for sincerity, but does not address validity of obligatory acts.
The hadith warns against riya in general, but the maxim narrows its effect on obligatory acts.
3
Trace the Scholarly Dispute
Follow the disagreement: Zaylai says sincerity is needed in prayer; Ibn Nujaym notes the maxim; Hamawi objects using the exception of fasting. The final position reaffirms the maxim: riya does not invalidate the obligatory act.
The dispute is about whether riya can prevent the obligation from being discharged, not about reward.
4
Derive the Operative Ruling for Fatwa
The mufta bihi position: if someone performs an obligatory act with riya, the act is valid and the obligation is discharged, but the reward is lost. This is based on the maxim and the exception of fasting (where riya cannot enter at all).
This ruling applies to all fara'id, including prayer, fasting, zakat, etc. Voluntary acts are different: riya invalidates them entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْخَامِسُ فِي بَيَانِ الْإِخْلَاصِپانچویں بحث اخلاص نیت کے بیان میںپانچویں بحث اخلاص نیت کے بیان میں ہے، اخلاص کا علم صرف اللہ کو ہوتا ہے نہ فرشتوں کو اور نہ شیطان کو، بندہ جب اللہ کی بارگاہ میں کوئی عمل پیش کرتا ہے تو ضروری نہیں کہ وہ قبول بھی ہو جائے بلکہ قبولیت کے لئے اخلاص کا ہیں: شرط ہے، اخلاص کے بغیر کوئی بھی عمل خواہ وہ ظاہر کتنا ہی خوشنما نظر آئے اور بڑا معلوم ہو لیکن اللہ کے یہاں اس کی کوئی قدر و قیمت نہیں ہے بلکہ دکھلاوے کے لئے اعمال کرنے والوں کا انجام آخرت میں بہت خراب اور برا ہوگا۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم تعوذوا بالله من جب الحزن قالوا يا رسول الله و ماجب الحزن؟ قال واد في جهنم يتعوذ منه جهنم كل يوم مائة مرة قيل يارسول الله ومن يدخله قال القراء المرائون باعمالهم. (ترمذی ج۲، ص: ۶۳) صَرَّحَ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ بأنَّ الْمُصَلَّى يَحْتَاجُ إلى بيةِ الإِخْلَاص فِيْهَا وَلَمْ أَرَ مَنْ أَوْ ضَحَهُ، لَكِنْ صَرَّحَ فِي الْخُلَاصَةِ بِأَنَّهُ لَا رِيَاءَ فِي الْفَرَائِضِ.ترجمه: علامہ زیلعی نے صراحت کی ہے کہ نماز میں نمازی کو اخلاص نیت کی ضرورت ہے اور میں نے نہیں دیکھا کسی نے اس کی وضاحت کی ہو لیکن خلاصہ میں تصریح ہے کہ فرائض میں ریاد نہیں ہے۔ تشریح: علامہ زیلعی فرماتے ہیں کہ تقرب کے لئے اخلاص نیت ضروری ہے لہذا نمازی کے لئے نماز میں بھی اخلاص نیت ضروری ہے علامہ ابن نجیم فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کی پوری وضاحت میری نظروں سے نہیں گذری البتہ خلاصہ میں صرف اتنا ہے کہ فرائص میں دکھلاوا نہیں ہوتا ، لہذا اس گمان سے کہ ریاء نہ کیا جائے فرائض کو نہیں چھوڑ چاہئے ، علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ مصنف کی یہ بات واقعات کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ روزہ صرف ایک ایسی عبادت ؟ جس کے بارے میں حدیث سے ثابت ہے کہ اس کے اندر ریاء داخل نہیں ہوتی ہے اس کے علاوہ دیگر طاعات میں ریا و داخل ہو سکتی ہے، لہذا صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ واجب کے ساقط ہونے میں فرائض کے اندر ریا مانع نہیں ہے۔ الرجاء لا يدخل فى الفرائض كذا في الخلاصه (بندیدن ج: ۶۷)
The fifth: On explaining sincerity. The fifth discussion is on explaining sincerity of intention. The knowledge of sincerity is only with Allah, not with angels nor with Satan. When a servant presents an action to Allah, it is not necessary that it be accepted; rather, for acceptance, sincerity is a condition. Without sincerity, any action, no matter how outwardly pleasing and great it may appear, has no value with Allah; rather, the end of those who perform actions for show will be very bad and evil in the Hereafter. From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Seek refuge with Allah from the pit of sorrow.' They said: 'O Messenger of Allah, what is the pit of sorrow?' He said: 'A valley in Hell from which Hell seeks refuge a hundred times every day.' It was said: 'O Messenger of Allah, who enters it?' He said: 'The reciters who show off with their deeds.' (Tirmidhi, vol. 2, p. 63) Zaylai stated that the one praying needs sincerity of intention in prayer, and I have not seen anyone who clarified it, but in al-Khulasa it is stated that there is no riya (show-off) in obligatory acts. Translation: Allama Zaylai has stated that in prayer, the worshiper needs sincerity of intention, and I have not seen anyone who clarified it, but in al-Khulasa it is stated that there is no riya in obligatory acts. Explanation: Allama Zaylai says that for seeking nearness to Allah, sincerity of intention is necessary, so for the worshiper, sincerity of intention in prayer is necessary. Allama Ibn Nujaym says that I have not come across a full explanation of this, but in al-Khulasa there is only this much that in obligatory acts, there is no show-off. Therefore, one should not leave obligatory acts for fear of riya. Allama Hamawi says that the author's statement is contrary to reality because fasting is a worship regarding which it is proven by hadith that riya does not enter into it; besides that, riya can enter other acts of obedience. So the correct view is that riya is not a preventer of the fulfillment of the obligatory duty. Riya does not enter into obligatory acts as stated in al-Khulasa (Bandidin, vol. 67).
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage opens the fifth discussion on sincerity (ikhlas) in intention. The author begins by stating that only Allah knows truly whether an action is sincere. Without sincerity, no action is accepted. He then cites a hadith from Tirmidhi warning against those who recite Quran or do deeds with riya (show-off) – they will be in a terrible place in Hell. Next, he brings a scholarly discussion. Zaylai asserts that the worshiper needs sincerity in prayer, but adds that he hasn't seen anyone clarify this requirement in detail. However, in the book al-Khulasa, it is explicitly stated that there is no riya in farid (obligatory acts) – meaning that riya does not affect the validity or completion of obligatory acts. Ibn Nujaym agrees, saying that since farid are obligatory, one should not abandon them out of fear of riya. Hamawi criticizes this, noting that fasting is an exception: hadith indicate that riya does not enter fasting, but for other obedient acts, riya can enter. However, the final relied-upon position (mukhtar) is that riya does not prevent the obligation from being fulfilled; in other words, if one performs an obligatory act with riya, the act is still valid and the obligation is discharged, though the reward may be diminished. This is a nuanced Hanafi position: while sincerity is required for full reward, the validity of obligatory acts is not nullified by the presence of riya. The passage ends by reaffirming the statement from al-Khulasa that riya does not enter the farid.

Key Terms
إخلاص (ikhlas): Sincerity in intention, performing an act solely for Allah's sake.
رياء (riya): Show-off, performing worship to be seen and praised by people.
فرائض (fara'id): Obligatory acts of worship in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position discussed, what is the effect of riya (show-off) on an obligatory prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but the reward is lost.
C) The prayer is invalid only if the riya was deliberate.
D) The prayer becomes a nafl (optional) prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'la riya fi al-fara'id' means obligatory acts remain valid despite riya, but sincerity is required for reward.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

The Principle: No Riya in Obligatory Acts (لا رياء في الفرائض)
Explaining the rule of riya in fara'id and its applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qa'ida that riya does not prevent the falling of obligation for fara'id, identify its scope, and apply it to a scenario.

Core Idea
In fara'id, riya does not invalidate the obligation, only the reward.

The Hanafi school teaches that sincerity (ikhlas) is essential for acceptance, but when it comes to the mere discharge of obligatory acts (fara'id), the presence of riya does not prevent the obligation from being fulfilled. This lesson examines the qa'ida 'لا رياء في الفرائض' and its implications, supported by the sub-maxim 'al-ibrah li al-sabiq'.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the qa'ida and its source
Locate the phrase 'لا رياء في الفرائض' in the passage. Understand that it comes from al-Khulasa, a Hanafi fatwa work.
The qa'ida is a dabt (sub-maxim) within the broader maxims, restricting the effect of riya in obligatory acts.
2
2. Understand the definition of riya
Riya is showing off in worship. The passage distinguishes between the obligation falling (suyut al-wajib) and reward (thawab). Riya destroys reward but does not invalidate the obligation.
3
3. Note the exception of fasting
Fasting is unique: the hadith indicates that riya cannot enter it at all. This is an istithna' to the general applicability of the qa'ida.
Other fara'id can have riya, but it doesn't affect the obligation.
4
4. Apply to a scenario
Consider a person who begins prayer sincerely but later feels pride. According to the qa'ida, the prayer is valid in terms of obligation, though reward is lost.
This is based on the sub-maxim 'al-ibrah li al-sabiq' (consideration is for the beginning).

Source Text

الْخَامِسُ فِي بَيَانِ الْإِخْلَاصِ
پانچویں بحث اخلاص نیت کے بیان میں
پانچویں بحث اخلاص نیت کے بیان میں ہے، اخلاص کا علم صرف اللہ کو ہوتا ہے نہ فرشتوں کو اور نہ شیطان کو، بندہ جب اللہ کی بارگاہ میں کوئی عمل پیش کرتا ہے تو ضروری نہیں کہ وہ قبول بھی ہو جائے بلکہ قبولیت کے لئے اخلاص کا ہیں: شرط ہے، اخلاص کے بغیر کوئی بھی عمل خواہ وہ ظاہر کتنا ہی خوشنما نظر آئے اور بڑا معلوم ہو لیکن اللہ کے یہاں اس کی کوئی قدر و قیمت نہیں ہے بلکہ دکھلاوے کے لئے اعمال کرنے والوں کا انجام آخرت میں بہت خراب اور برا ہوگا۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم تعوذوا بالله من جب الحزن قالوا يا رسول الله و ماجب الحزن؟ قال واد في جهنم يتعوذ منه جهنم كل يوم مائة مرة قيل يارسول الله ومن يدخله قال القراء المرائون باعمالهم. (ترمذی ج۲، ص: ۶۳) صَرَّحَ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ بأنَّ الْمُصَلَّى يَحْتَاجُ إلى بيةِ الإِخْلَاص فِيْهَا وَلَمْ أَرَ مَنْ أَوْ ضَحَهُ، لَكِنْ صَرَّحَ فِي الْخُلَاصَةِ بِأَنَّهُ لَا رِيَاءَ فِي الْفَرَائِضِ.
ترجمه: علامہ زیلعی نے صراحت کی ہے کہ نماز میں نمازی کو اخلاص نیت کی ضرورت ہے اور میں نے نہیں دیکھا کسی نے اس کی وضاحت کی ہو لیکن خلاصہ میں تصریح ہے کہ فرائض میں ریاد نہیں ہے۔ تشریح: علامہ زیلعی فرماتے ہیں کہ تقرب کے لئے اخلاص نیت ضروری ہے لہذا نمازی کے لئے نماز میں بھی اخلاص نیت ضروری ہے علامہ ابن نجیم فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کی پوری وضاحت میری نظروں سے نہیں گذری البتہ خلاصہ میں صرف اتنا ہے کہ فرائص میں دکھلاوا نہیں ہوتا ، لہذا اس گمان سے کہ ریاء نہ کیا جائے فرائض کو نہیں چھوڑ چاہئے ، علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ مصنف کی یہ بات واقعات کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ روزہ صرف ایک ایسی عبادت ؟ جس کے بارے میں حدیث سے ثابت ہے کہ اس کے اندر ریاء داخل نہیں ہوتی ہے اس کے علاوہ دیگر طاعات میں ریا و داخل ہو سکتی ہے، لہذا صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ واجب کے ساقط ہونے میں فرائض کے اندر ریا مانع نہیں ہے۔ الرجاء
لا يدخل فى الفرائض كذا في الخلاصه (بندیدن ج: ۶۷)

وَفِي الْبَزَّازِيَةِ شَرَعَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ بِالْإِخْلَاصِ ، ثُمَّ خَالَطَة الرِّيَاءُ، فَالْعِبْرَةُ لِلسَّابِقِ، وَلَا رِيَاءَ فِي الْفَرَائِضِ فِي سُقُوْطِ الْوَاجِبِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: الصَّلَوةُ لِإِرْضَاءِ الْحُصُوْمِ لَا تُفَيِّدُ، بَلْ يُصَلّى لِوَجْهِ اللهِ تَعَالَى، فَإِنْ كَانَ خَصْمُهُ لَمْ يَعْفِ يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ حَسَنَاتِهِ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ. وَجَاءَ فِي بَعْضِ الْكُتُبِ أَنَّهُ يُؤْخَذُ لِدَانِقٍ ثَوَابُ سَبْعِ مِائَةِ صَلَاةٍ بِالْجَمَاعَةِ، فَلَا فَائِدَةَ فِي النِّيَّةِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ عَفَاء فَلَا يُؤَاخَذُ بِهِ فَمَا الْفَائِدَةُ حِيْنَئِذٍ؟ إِنْتَهَى.
:ترجمہ اور بزازیہ میں ہے کہ اخلاص کے ساتھ نماز شروع کی پھر ریاء آگئی تو اعتبار سابق کا ہوگا اور واجب کے سقوط کے حق میں فرائض میں ریاء نہیں پھر کہا نماز مد مقابل کو راضی کرنے کے لئے مفید نہیں ہے، بلکہ اللہ کی رضاء کے لئے نماز پڑھے پس اگر اس کے مد مقابل نے معاف نہ کیا تو قیامت کے دن اس کی نیکیوں میں سے لیا جائے گا اور بعض کتابوں میں آیا ہے کہ ایک دائق کے بدلہ سات سو با جماعت نماز کا ثواب لیا جائے گا تو نیت میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں اور اگر معاف کر دیا تو مواخذہ نہیں تو اس وقت کیا فائدہ؟ بزازیہ کی بات پوری ہوئی۔ تشریح اگر کسی شخص نے اخلاص کے ساتھ نماز شروع کی پھر ریاء کا خیال آگیا تو اس کا کچھا انتہار نہیں بلکہ العبرة للسابق کے قاعدہ کی بناء پر شروع کرنے کا اعتبار ہوگا لہذا واجب ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گا اور سقوط واجب کے حق میں یہ ریاء مائع اور رکاوٹ ثابت نہ کی۔و انه لا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوط الواجب (شای زکریا ج ۲ ص:۹۰) و في التار تار خانيه لو افتتح خالصاً لله تعالى و دخل في قلبه الرياء فهو على ما افتتح رياء کے ساتھ جو نماز پڑھی جائیگی اس سے نماز فرض ادا ہو جائے گی اگر چہ تو اب نہیں ملے گا اس لئے کہ شروع کا اعتبار ہے۔ ثم قال الصلاة لارضاء الخصوم: اس عنوان کے تحت یہ مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص اس نیت سے نماز پڑھے کہ عدالت میں اس کی گواہی قبول ہو جائے ، اور اس کے مخالفین بھی اس سے راضی ہو جا ئیں تو اس نیت سے پڑھی جانے والی نماز بالکل مفید نہ ہو گی بلکہ آخرت میں تو وہ نماز مفید ہوگی جو اللہ کی رضاء کو مقصود بنا کر پڑھی جائے اس لئے بندوں کو چاہئے کہ وہ اللہ کی رضاء کے لئے نماز پڑھیں کیونکہ اگر دنیا میں کسی کا حق لیا اور اس نے معاف نہ کیا تو آخرت میں اس کے بدلہ میں اس کی نیکیاں لی جائیں گی۔ اس دنیا میں اگر کسی شخص نے کسی کا حق کیا تو آخرت میں حق دبانے والے کی نیکیاں لیکر حق والے کو دی جائیں گی جس کا تناسب اس سے معلوم ہو سکتا ہے کہ ایک دائق یعنی درہم کے چھٹے حصہ کے بدلہ میں جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھی جانے والی سات سولمازوں کا ثواب حق والے کو حق تلفی کرنے والے سے لیکر دیا جائیگا اس لئے اسے خوش کرنے کی نیت سے نماز پڑھنے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر اس نے معاف نہ کیا تو آخرت میں اتنی نمازوں کا ثواب اسے دینا ہو گا لہذا اسے خوش کرنے کے لئے جو نماز پڑھی گئی ہے وہ بریکار گئی اور اگر اس نے معاف کر دیا تو اب اسے خوش
The fifth section: concerning the explanation of sincerity. The knowledge of sincerity is only with Allah, not with angels nor with Satan. When a servant presents an action in the court of Allah, it is not necessary that it be accepted; rather, for acceptance, sincerity is a condition. Without sincerity, no action, no matter how pleasing it appears outwardly and seems great, has any value with Allah. Rather, those who perform actions for show will have a very bad and evil outcome in the Hereafter. From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Seek refuge with Allah from the pit of grief.' They said: 'O Messenger of Allah, what is the pit of grief?' He said: 'A valley in Hell from which Hell itself seeks refuge a hundred times each day.' It was said: 'O Messenger of Allah, who enters it?' He said: 'The reciters who show off with their deeds.' (Tirmidhi, vol. 2, p. 63). Zayla'i explicitly stated that the one praying needs sincerity of intention in it, and I have not seen anyone clarify it, but in al-Khulasa it is explicitly stated that there is no riya in obligatory acts. Translation: Allama Zayla'i has stated that the one praying needs sincerity of intention in prayer, and I have not seen anyone explain it, but in al-Khulasa it is stated that there is no riya in obligatory acts. Explanation: Allama Zayla'i says that for seeking nearness, sincerity of intention is necessary; therefore, for the one praying, sincerity of intention is necessary in prayer. Allama Ibn Nujaym says that I have not seen a complete explanation of this, but in al-Khulasa there is only that there is no showing off in obligatory acts. Therefore, one should not leave obligatory acts due to the suspicion of riya. Allama Hamawi says that the author's statement contradicts reality because fasting is the only act of worship regarding which it is established from hadith that riya does not enter it; as for other acts of obedience, riya can enter. Therefore, the correct view is that riya is not an obstacle in the falling of the obligation for obligatory acts. 'Riya does not enter in obligatory acts' — thus in al-Khulasa (Binding, p. 67). And in al-Bazzaziyyah: He began the prayer with sincerity, then riya mixed with it, so consideration is for the earlier, and there is no riya in obligatory acts regarding the falling of the obligation. Then he said: 'Prayer for pleasing opponents is not beneficial; rather, one should pray for the sake of Allah the Exalted. If his opponent does not forgive, then on the Day of Resurrection, (the reward) will be taken from his good deeds.' And it has come in some books that for a daniq (a small coin), the reward of seven hundred prayers in congregation will be taken, so there is no benefit in the intention. And if he forgives, then there is no punishment; so what benefit is there then?' End. Translation: And in al-Bazzaziyyah: He began the prayer with sincerity, then riya came, so consideration is for the earlier, and there is no riya in obligatory acts regarding the falling of the obligation. Then he said: Prayer for pleasing opponents is not beneficial; rather, one should pray for the sake of Allah. Then if his opponent did not forgive, on the Day of Resurrection good deeds will be taken from him. And in some books it is stated that for a daniq, the reward of seven hundred congregational prayers will be taken, so there is no benefit in the intention. And if he forgave, then there is no punishment; so what benefit is there then? The statement of Bazzaziyyah is complete. Explanation: If a person began prayer with sincerity, then the thought of riya came, it does not have any effect; rather, based on the principle 'consideration is for the earlier', the beginning is considered, so the obligation falls from his responsibility, and regarding the falling of the obligation, this riya does not act as a preventer or obstacle. 'And indeed there is no riya in obligatory acts regarding the falling of the obligation' (Shami Zakariyya, vol. 2, p. 90). And in al-Tatar Khaniyyah: If he begins purely for Allah the Exalted and then riya enters his heart, then he is upon what he began. A prayer offered with riya will fulfill the obligatory prayer, even though there will be no reward, because the beginning is considered. Then he said: 'Prayer for pleasing opponents' — under this heading is the issue that if a person prays with the intention that his testimony be accepted in court and his opponents become pleased with him, then the prayer offered with this intention is completely useless; rather, in the Hereafter, that prayer will be beneficial which is offered with the intention of seeking Allah's pleasure. Therefore, servants should pray for Allah's pleasure, because if someone takes a right in this world and the other does not forgive, then in the Hereafter, his good deeds will be taken in exchange. In this world, if someone usurps another's right, then in the Hereafter, the good deeds of the usurper will be taken and given to the rightful owner. The proportion can be understood from the fact that for a daniq, i.e., one-sixth of a dirham, the reward of seven hundred prayers offered in congregation will be taken from the wrongdoer and given to the rightful owner. Therefore, there is no benefit in praying with the intention of pleasing him, because if he does not forgive, then in the Hereafter, the reward of so many prayers will have to be given; thus the prayer offered to please him is wasted. And if he forgives, then now he is pleased.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is from the fifth section of the book, dealing with sincerity (ikhlas) in intention. The author begins by emphasizing that sincerity is known only to Allah, and without it no deed is accepted. He supports this with a hadith warning against showing off. Then he presents a legal maxim: 'There is no riya (show-off) in obligatory acts (fara'id).' This maxim is discussed with references: Zayla'i states that the one praying needs sincerity, but Ibn Nujaym notes that no one has fully explained this, except that al-Khulasa explicitly states that riya does not enter fara'id in terms of the obligation falling. Hamawi criticizes this, saying that only fasting is free from riya, while other acts can have riya; however, the correct view is that riya does not prevent the obligation from being fulfilled. Then from al-Bazzaziyyah, the rule is applied: if one starts prayer sincerely and then riya enters, the consideration is for the beginning (al-ibrah li al-sabiq), so the obligation is discharged, though reward may be lost. Additionally, prayer performed to please opponents (e.g., to gain their acceptance in court) is not beneficial; one should pray purely for Allah. If the opponent does not forgive, the reward is taken on the Day of Judgment. A severe consequence is mentioned: for a small injustice (a daniq), the reward of 700 congregational prayers may be taken. Therefore, there is no benefit in such worldly intentions. The passage underscores the importance of sincerity and clarifies that riya does not invalidate the obligation of fara'id but affects reward.

Key Terms
إخلاص (ikhlas): Sincerity of intention in acts of worship, done solely for Allah's pleasure.
رياء (riya): Showing off; performing an act of worship to be seen by others rather than for Allah.
فرائض (fara'id): Obligatory acts of worship; in this context, primarily the five daily prayers and other obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi qa'ida discussed in this lesson, what is the effect of riya in obligatory acts (fara'id)?
A) It invalidates the act completely.
B) It prevents the obligation from being fulfilled.
C) It does not prevent the obligation from being fulfilled, but destroys reward.
D) It has no effect at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi qa'ida 'لا رياء في الفرائض' means that riya does not invalidate the obligation of fara'id, but it destroys reward; sincerity is essential for acceptance.
