Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Applications: The Rule of al-Ibrah li al-Sabiq and Praying for Worldly Gains
Applying the qa'ida and sub-maxim to specific cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi sub-maxim 'al-ibrah li al-sabiq' to cases of riya in salah and evaluate the consequence of worldly intentions in prayer.

Core Idea
If riya enters after a sincere start, the obligation is fulfilled; praying to please people has no benefit in the Hereafter.

This lesson applies the qa'ida to specific situations: when riya enters after a sincere intention, and when one prays with the worldly aim of pleasing opponents. The principle of 'consideration for the beginning' (al-ibrah li al-sabiq) is key to understanding the validity of the obligation.

Guided Path
1
1. Understand the sub-maxim al-ibrah li al-sabiq
This rule states that the initial intention governs the entire act. If one starts sincerely, later riya does not affect the validity of the obligation.
2
2. Apply to the case of riya after sincerity
From al-Bazzaziyya: if one begins prayer with sincerity and then riya enters, the prayer is valid because the beginning is considered.
The obligation falls even if reward is lost.
3
3. Analyze the case of praying to please opponents
The passage mentions that praying to satisfy opponents (e.g., to be accepted as a witness in court) is not beneficial; reward may be taken on Judgment Day if the opponent does not forgive.
This underscores the importance of pure intention.
4
4. Compare with the exception of fasting
Fasting is free from riya entirely, as per hadith, so this qa'ida does not apply in the same way.

الْخَامِسُ فِي بَيَانِ الْإِخْلَاصِ
پانچویں بحث اخلاص نیت کے بیان میں
پانچویں بحث اخلاص نیت کے بیان میں ہے، اخلاص کا علم صرف اللہ کو ہوتا ہے نہ فرشتوں کو اور نہ شیطان کو، بندہ جب اللہ کی بارگاہ میں کوئی عمل پیش کرتا ہے تو ضروری نہیں کہ وہ قبول بھی ہو جائے بلکہ قبولیت کے لئے اخلاص کا ہیں: شرط ہے، اخلاص کے بغیر کوئی بھی عمل خواہ وہ ظاہر کتنا ہی خوشنما نظر آئے اور بڑا معلوم ہو لیکن اللہ کے یہاں اس کی کوئی قدر و قیمت نہیں ہے بلکہ دکھلاوے کے لئے اعمال کرنے والوں کا انجام آخرت میں بہت خراب اور برا ہوگا۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم تعوذوا بالله من جب الحزن قالوا يا رسول الله و ماجب الحزن؟ قال واد في جهنم يتعوذ منه جهنم كل يوم مائة مرة قيل يارسول الله ومن يدخله قال القراء المرائون باعمالهم. (ترمذی ج۲، ص: ۶۳) صَرَّحَ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ بأنَّ الْمُصَلَّى يَحْتَاجُ إلى بيةِ الإِخْلَاص فِيْهَا وَلَمْ أَرَ مَنْ أَوْ ضَحَهُ، لَكِنْ صَرَّحَ فِي الْخُلَاصَةِ بِأَنَّهُ لَا رِيَاءَ فِي الْفَرَائِضِ.
ترجمه: علامہ زیلعی نے صراحت کی ہے کہ نماز میں نمازی کو اخلاص نیت کی ضرورت ہے اور میں نے نہیں دیکھا کسی نے اس کی وضاحت کی ہو لیکن خلاصہ میں تصریح ہے کہ فرائض میں ریاد نہیں ہے۔ تشریح: علامہ زیلعی فرماتے ہیں کہ تقرب کے لئے اخلاص نیت ضروری ہے لہذا نمازی کے لئے نماز میں بھی اخلاص نیت ضروری ہے علامہ ابن نجیم فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کی پوری وضاحت میری نظروں سے نہیں گذری البتہ خلاصہ میں صرف اتنا ہے کہ فرائص میں دکھلاوا نہیں ہوتا ، لہذا اس گمان سے کہ ریاء نہ کیا جائے فرائض کو نہیں چھوڑ چاہئے ، علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ مصنف کی یہ بات واقعات کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ روزہ صرف ایک ایسی عبادت ؟ جس کے بارے میں حدیث سے ثابت ہے کہ اس کے اندر ریاء داخل نہیں ہوتی ہے اس کے علاوہ دیگر طاعات میں ریا و داخل ہو سکتی ہے، لہذا صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ واجب کے ساقط ہونے میں فرائض کے اندر ریا مانع نہیں ہے۔ الرجاء
لا يدخل فى الفرائض كذا في الخلاصه (بندیدن ج: ۶۷)

وَفِي الْبَزَّازِيَةِ شَرَعَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ بِالْإِخْلَاصِ ، ثُمَّ خَالَطَة الرِّيَاءُ، فَالْعِبْرَةُ لِلسَّابِقِ، وَلَا رِيَاءَ فِي الْفَرَائِضِ فِي سُقُوْطِ الْوَاجِبِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: الصَّلَوةُ لِإِرْضَاءِ الْحُصُوْمِ لَا تُفَيِّدُ، بَلْ يُصَلّى لِوَجْهِ اللهِ تَعَالَى، فَإِنْ كَانَ خَصْمُهُ لَمْ يَعْفِ يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ حَسَنَاتِهِ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ. وَجَاءَ فِي بَعْضِ الْكُتُبِ أَنَّهُ يُؤْخَذُ لِدَانِقٍ ثَوَابُ سَبْعِ مِائَةِ صَلَاةٍ بِالْجَمَاعَةِ، فَلَا فَائِدَةَ فِي النِّيَّةِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ عَفَاء فَلَا يُؤَاخَذُ بِهِ فَمَا الْفَائِدَةُ حِيْنَئِذٍ؟ إِنْتَهَى.
:ترجمہ اور بزازیہ میں ہے کہ اخلاص کے ساتھ نماز شروع کی پھر ریاء آگئی تو اعتبار سابق کا ہوگا اور واجب کے سقوط کے حق میں فرائض میں ریاء نہیں پھر کہا نماز مد مقابل کو راضی کرنے کے لئے مفید نہیں ہے، بلکہ اللہ کی رضاء کے لئے نماز پڑھے پس اگر اس کے مد مقابل نے معاف نہ کیا تو قیامت کے دن اس کی نیکیوں میں سے لیا جائے گا اور بعض کتابوں میں آیا ہے کہ ایک دائق کے بدلہ سات سو با جماعت نماز کا ثواب لیا جائے گا تو نیت میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں اور اگر معاف کر دیا تو مواخذہ نہیں تو اس وقت کیا فائدہ؟ بزازیہ کی بات پوری ہوئی۔ تشریح اگر کسی شخص نے اخلاص کے ساتھ نماز شروع کی پھر ریاء کا خیال آگیا تو اس کا کچھا انتہار نہیں بلکہ العبرة للسابق کے قاعدہ کی بناء پر شروع کرنے کا اعتبار ہوگا لہذا واجب ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گا اور سقوط واجب کے حق میں یہ ریاء مائع اور رکاوٹ ثابت نہ کی۔و انه لا رياء في الفرائض في حق سقوط الواجب (شای زکریا ج ۲ ص:۹۰) و في التار تار خانيه لو افتتح خالصاً لله تعالى و دخل في قلبه الرياء فهو على ما افتتح رياء کے ساتھ جو نماز پڑھی جائیگی اس سے نماز فرض ادا ہو جائے گی اگر چہ تو اب نہیں ملے گا اس لئے کہ شروع کا اعتبار ہے۔ ثم قال الصلاة لارضاء الخصوم: اس عنوان کے تحت یہ مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص اس نیت سے نماز پڑھے کہ عدالت میں اس کی گواہی قبول ہو جائے ، اور اس کے مخالفین بھی اس سے راضی ہو جا ئیں تو اس نیت سے پڑھی جانے والی نماز بالکل مفید نہ ہو گی بلکہ آخرت میں تو وہ نماز مفید ہوگی جو اللہ کی رضاء کو مقصود بنا کر پڑھی جائے اس لئے بندوں کو چاہئے کہ وہ اللہ کی رضاء کے لئے نماز پڑھیں کیونکہ اگر دنیا میں کسی کا حق لیا اور اس نے معاف نہ کیا تو آخرت میں اس کے بدلہ میں اس کی نیکیاں لی جائیں گی۔ اس دنیا میں اگر کسی شخص نے کسی کا حق کیا تو آخرت میں حق دبانے والے کی نیکیاں لیکر حق والے کو دی جائیں گی جس کا تناسب اس سے معلوم ہو سکتا ہے کہ ایک دائق یعنی درہم کے چھٹے حصہ کے بدلہ میں جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھی جانے والی سات سولمازوں کا ثواب حق والے کو حق تلفی کرنے والے سے لیکر دیا جائیگا اس لئے اسے خوش کرنے کی نیت سے نماز پڑھنے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر اس نے معاف نہ کیا تو آخرت میں اتنی نمازوں کا ثواب اسے دینا ہو گا لہذا اسے خوش کرنے کے لئے جو نماز پڑھی گئی ہے وہ بریکار گئی اور اگر اس نے معاف کر دیا تو اب اسے خوش
The fifth section: concerning the explanation of sincerity. The knowledge of sincerity is only with Allah, not with angels nor with Satan. When a servant presents an action in the court of Allah, it is not necessary that it be accepted; rather, for acceptance, sincerity is a condition. Without sincerity, no action, no matter how pleasing it appears outwardly and seems great, has any value with Allah. Rather, those who perform actions for show will have a very bad and evil outcome in the Hereafter. From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Seek refuge with Allah from the pit of grief.' They said: 'O Messenger of Allah, what is the pit of grief?' He said: 'A valley in Hell from which Hell itself seeks refuge a hundred times each day.' It was said: 'O Messenger of Allah, who enters it?' He said: 'The reciters who show off with their deeds.' (Tirmidhi, vol. 2, p. 63). Zayla'i explicitly stated that the one praying needs sincerity of intention in it, and I have not seen anyone clarify it, but in al-Khulasa it is explicitly stated that there is no riya in obligatory acts. Translation: Allama Zayla'i has stated that the one praying needs sincerity of intention in prayer, and I have not seen anyone explain it, but in al-Khulasa it is stated that there is no riya in obligatory acts. Explanation: Allama Zayla'i says that for seeking nearness, sincerity of intention is necessary; therefore, for the one praying, sincerity of intention is necessary in prayer. Allama Ibn Nujaym says that I have not seen a complete explanation of this, but in al-Khulasa there is only that there is no showing off in obligatory acts. Therefore, one should not leave obligatory acts due to the suspicion of riya. Allama Hamawi says that the author's statement contradicts reality because fasting is the only act of worship regarding which it is established from hadith that riya does not enter it; as for other acts of obedience, riya can enter. Therefore, the correct view is that riya is not an obstacle in the falling of the obligation for obligatory acts. 'Riya does not enter in obligatory acts' — thus in al-Khulasa (Binding, p. 67). And in al-Bazzaziyyah: He began the prayer with sincerity, then riya mixed with it, so consideration is for the earlier, and there is no riya in obligatory acts regarding the falling of the obligation. Then he said: 'Prayer for pleasing opponents is not beneficial; rather, one should pray for the sake of Allah the Exalted. If his opponent does not forgive, then on the Day of Resurrection, (the reward) will be taken from his good deeds.' And it has come in some books that for a daniq (a small coin), the reward of seven hundred prayers in congregation will be taken, so there is no benefit in the intention. And if he forgives, then there is no punishment; so what benefit is there then?' End. Translation: And in al-Bazzaziyyah: He began the prayer with sincerity, then riya came, so consideration is for the earlier, and there is no riya in obligatory acts regarding the falling of the obligation. Then he said: Prayer for pleasing opponents is not beneficial; rather, one should pray for the sake of Allah. Then if his opponent did not forgive, on the Day of Resurrection good deeds will be taken from him. And in some books it is stated that for a daniq, the reward of seven hundred congregational prayers will be taken, so there is no benefit in the intention. And if he forgave, then there is no punishment; so what benefit is there then? The statement of Bazzaziyyah is complete. Explanation: If a person began prayer with sincerity, then the thought of riya came, it does not have any effect; rather, based on the principle 'consideration is for the earlier', the beginning is considered, so the obligation falls from his responsibility, and regarding the falling of the obligation, this riya does not act as a preventer or obstacle. 'And indeed there is no riya in obligatory acts regarding the falling of the obligation' (Shami Zakariyya, vol. 2, p. 90). And in al-Tatar Khaniyyah: If he begins purely for Allah the Exalted and then riya enters his heart, then he is upon what he began. A prayer offered with riya will fulfill the obligatory prayer, even though there will be no reward, because the beginning is considered. Then he said: 'Prayer for pleasing opponents' — under this heading is the issue that if a person prays with the intention that his testimony be accepted in court and his opponents become pleased with him, then the prayer offered with this intention is completely useless; rather, in the Hereafter, that prayer will be beneficial which is offered with the intention of seeking Allah's pleasure. Therefore, servants should pray for Allah's pleasure, because if someone takes a right in this world and the other does not forgive, then in the Hereafter, his good deeds will be taken in exchange. In this world, if someone usurps another's right, then in the Hereafter, the good deeds of the usurper will be taken and given to the rightful owner. The proportion can be understood from the fact that for a daniq, i.e., one-sixth of a dirham, the reward of seven hundred prayers offered in congregation will be taken from the wrongdoer and given to the rightful owner. Therefore, there is no benefit in praying with the intention of pleasing him, because if he does not forgive, then in the Hereafter, the reward of so many prayers will have to be given; thus the prayer offered to please him is wasted. And if he forgives, then now he is pleased.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is from the fifth section of the book, dealing with sincerity (ikhlas) in intention. The author begins by emphasizing that sincerity is known only to Allah, and without it no deed is accepted. He supports this with a hadith warning against showing off. Then he presents a legal maxim: 'There is no riya (show-off) in obligatory acts (fara'id).' This maxim is discussed with references: Zayla'i states that the one praying needs sincerity, but Ibn Nujaym notes that no one has fully explained this, except that al-Khulasa explicitly states that riya does not enter fara'id in terms of the obligation falling. Hamawi criticizes this, saying that only fasting is free from riya, while other acts can have riya; however, the correct view is that riya does not prevent the obligation from being fulfilled. Then from al-Bazzaziyyah, the rule is applied: if one starts prayer sincerely and then riya enters, the consideration is for the beginning (al-ibrah li al-sabiq), so the obligation is discharged, though reward may be lost. Additionally, prayer performed to please opponents (e.g., to gain their acceptance in court) is not beneficial; one should pray purely for Allah. If the opponent does not forgive, the reward is taken on the Day of Judgment. A severe consequence is mentioned: for a small injustice (a daniq), the reward of 700 congregational prayers may be taken. Therefore, there is no benefit in such worldly intentions. The passage underscores the importance of sincerity and clarifies that riya does not invalidate the obligation of fara'id but affects reward.

Key Terms
العبرة للسابق (al-ibrah li al-sabiq): Consideration is for the beginning; the initial intention governs the validity of an act.
سقوط الواجب (suyut al-wajib): The falling of the obligation; the act is considered fulfilled and the person is no longer liable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who begins prayer sincerely and then riya enters his heart?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and he gets full reward.
C) The obligation is fulfilled but he loses reward.
D) The prayer is only valid if he repents immediately.

Key Takeaway
The sub-maxim 'al-ibrah li al-sabiq' ensures that the obligation of salah is fulfilled if one starts sincerely, but riya or worldly intentions destroy reward.

The Principle of 'Al-Ibra li's-Sabiq': Riyā' in Farā'id
Explaining the ruling from al-Bazzāziyya regarding riyā' entering after sincere intention in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'al-ibratu li's-sabiq' to cases of riyā' in farā'id and identify when the obligation is discharged.

Core Idea
Riyā' after sincere beginning does not nullify the obligation; the first intention rules.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-ibratu li's-sabiq' (consideration is given to the first) as applied to obligatory acts of worship. The passage from al-Bazzāziyya illustrates that if riyā' enters after a sincere start, the obligation is still fulfilled. We will also explore the limits of this principle and a related discussion on praying to please others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida and its scope
Locate the statement 'fāl-ʿibra li's-sābiq' and note that it applies specifically to farā'id (obligatory acts). The qawida is a sub-maxim (dabt) of the broader 'al-umūr bi-maqāṣidihā'.
The scope is limited to farā'id, not nawāfil.
2
Analyze the furū' case from al-Bazzāziyya
The text gives a scenario: starting salah with sincerity, then riyā' mixes in. Apply the qawida: the first intention (sincerity) governs, so the salah is valid and the obligation is dropped.
The sub-rule 'lā riyā'a fil-farā'id fī suqūṭ al-wājib' reinforces this.
3
Distinguish the extreme case: riyā' from the beginning
The second part of the passage deals with praying solely to please adversaries. Here, the initial intention is not sincere; the qawida does not apply, and the prayer is not beneficial.
This case is governed by the general principle that acts must be for Allah's sake.
4
Connect to the supporting hadith
The hadith from Musnad Ahmad about the bankrupt person illustrates the consequence: if one wrongs others, their good deeds will be taken. This supports the warning against insincere prayers.
The hadith is cited to emphasize the seriousness of riyā' and the loss of reward.
5
Formulate a fatwa
Using the qawida, a mufti rules that if riyā' enters after sincere beginning, the obligation is fulfilled. However, if the intention from the start was insincere (e.g., to show off), the act is invalid or loses reward entirely.
The mufti must distinguish between the two scenarios based on the timing of riyā'.

Source Text

وَفِي الْبَزَّازِيَةِ شَرَعَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ بِالْإِخْلَاصِ ، ثُمَّ خَالَطَة الرِّيَاءُ، فَالْعِبْرَةُ لِلسَّابِقِ، وَلَا رِيَاءَ فِي الْفَرَائِضِ فِي سُقُوْطِ الْوَاجِبِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: الصَّلَوةُ لِإِرْضَاءِ الْحُصُوْمِ لَا تُفَيِّدُ، بَلْ يُصَلّى لِوَجْهِ اللهِ تَعَالَى، فَإِنْ كَانَ خَصْمُهُ لَمْ يَعْفِ يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ حَسَنَاتِهِ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ. وَجَاءَ فِي بَعْضِ الْكُتُبِ أَنَّهُ يُؤْخَذُ لِدَانِقٍ ثَوَابُ سَبْعِ مِائَةِ صَلَاةٍ بِالْجَمَاعَةِ، فَلَا فَائِدَةَ فِي النِّيَّةِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ عَفَاء فَلَا يُؤَاخَذُ بِهِ فَمَا الْفَائِدَةُ حِيْنَئِذٍ؟ إِنْتَهَى.
:ترجمہ اور بزازیہ میں ہے کہ اخلاص کے ساتھ نماز شروع کی پھر ریاء آگئی تو اعتبار سابق کا ہوگا اور واجب کے سقوط کے حق میں فرائض میں ریاء نہیں پھر کہا نماز مد مقابل کو راضی کرنے کے لئے مفید نہیں ہے، بلکہ اللہ کی رضاء کے لئے نماز پڑھے پس اگر اس کے مد مقابل نے معاف نہ کیا تو قیامت کے دن اس کی نیکیوں میں سے لیا جائے گا اور بعض کتابوں میں آیا ہے کہ ایک دائق کے بدلہ سات سو با جماعت نماز کا ثواب لیا جائے گا تو نیت میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں اور اگر معاف کر دیا تو مواخذہ نہیں تو اس وقت کیا فائدہ؟ بزازیہ کی بات پوری ہوئی۔ تشریح اگر کسی شخص نے اخلاص کے ساتھ نماز شروع کی پھر ریاء کا خیال آگیا تو اس کا کچھا انتہار عن ابي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال هل تدرون من المفلس قالوا المفلس فينا يا رسول الله من لا دراهم له ولا متاع - الى قوله واكل مال هذا فيقعد فيقتص هذا من حسناته وهذا من حسناته فان فنيت حسناته قبل ان يقص ما عليه من الخطايا اخذ من خطايا هم فطرحت عليه ثم طرح في النار (مسند احمد ج ۳، ص: ۳۰۳)
And in al-Bazzâziyya: He started salah with sincerity, then riyâ' mixed with it; then consideration is given to the first, and there is no riyâ' in farâ'id regarding dropping the obligation. Then he said: Salah for pleasing adversaries is not beneficial, rather one prays for the sake of Allah the Exalted. If his adversary did not forgive, then on the Day of Judgment it will be taken from his good deeds. And it is stated in some books that for a dâniq, the reward of seven hundred congregational prayers is taken, so there is no benefit in the intention. And if he forgave, then he is not held accountable—so what is the benefit then? End. Urdu translation and commentary expanding on the ruling, including references and hadith from Musnad Ahmad.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage defines the Hanafi qâ'ida 'al-ibratu li's-sâbiq' (consideration is given to the first) as applied to riyâ' (ostentation) in worship. The author first quotes al-Bazzâziyya stating that if a person starts salah sincerely and later riyâ' enters, the initial intention prevails. As a result, the salah is valid and the obligation is dropped. The text then discusses an extreme case: praying with the intention of pleasing adversaries is useless—if the adversary does not forgive, the reward is taken on Judgment Day; if he forgives, there was no benefit. The author then provides a detailed Urdu commentary explaining that riyâ' does not invalidate farâ'id (obligatory acts) regarding the dropping of the obligation. The hadith from Musnad Ahmad about the true bankrupt person supports the point that if one has wronged others, their good deeds will be taken. The key takeaway: for farâ'id, riyâ' after sincere beginning does not invalidate the obligation; the act is valid and the liability is discharged, though reward may be diminished.

Key Terms
الرياء (ar-riyā'): Performing an act of worship to be seen by others, with a motive other than Allah's pleasure.
العبرة للسابق (al-ʿibra li's-sābiq): The legal principle that when two states occur, the earlier one is given weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle 'al-ibratu li's-sâbiq', if a person starts Fajr salah with sincere intention and then riyâ' enters during the prayer, what is the ruling regarding the obligation?
A) The salah is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The salah is valid and the obligation is dropped.
C) The salah is valid but reward is nullified and obligation remains.
D) The salah is invalid only if riyâ' continues until the end.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle 'al-ibratu li's-sabiq' ensures that a sincere beginning in farā'id overcomes later riyā' for the purpose of discharging the obligation, though reward may be diminished.

The Indivisibility of Bloodshed: Intention in Shared Sacrifice
Explaining the ruling and the qawida on shared sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'إذا لم يقع البعض قربة خرج الكل عن أن يكون قربة' to scenarios of shared udhiya and evaluate its implications for intention.

Core Idea
The bloodshed is indivisible; if any partner lacks devotion, the entire sacrifice is invalid for all.

This lesson examines a critical refinement from al-Bazzâziyya: while farai'd are valid despite riya, udhiya requires absolute sincerity from every partner. When a budnah is shared, all must intend qurbah; otherwise the whole sacrifice fails. We will unpack the underlying qawida and its reasoning—the indivisibility of bloodshed—and apply it to modern qurbani groups.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage and note the condition: a budnah (cow/camel) can be shared by seven, provided all intend qurbah. If one intends only meat or is a Christian, the sacrifice is invalid for all.
Notice this is stricter than the ruling on riya in farai'd.
2
Extract the qawida
The authors state: 'إذا لم يقع البعض قربة خرج الكل عن أن يكون قربة' (If part does not occur as devotion, the whole ceases to be devotion). Write this maxim down.
This is a sughra (minor) maxim, classified as a dabt restricting a larger principle.
3
Understand the reasoning: indivisibility of bloodshed
The cause (علة) is 'الإراقة لا تتجزأ' (bloodshed is indivisible). The act of slaughter cannot be split into devotional and non-devotional parts; it is a single unit.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on the nature of the act.
4
Apply the qawida to an extended case
The passage extends the ruling: if someone sacrifices for Allah and for other than Him, a fortiori it does not suffice and is prohibited. Trace how the qawida applies.
This shows the maxim's wider application beyond shared sacrifices.
5
Contrast with the ruling on riya in farai'd
Note that al-Bazzâzi says farai'd are valid despite riya. Why the difference? Because farai'd are owed to Allah and the act itself fulfills the obligation regardless of intention, whereas udhiya's validity depends on the intention of qurbah and the indivisibility of bloodshed.
This contrast highlights that the qawida is specific to blood sacrifice.

وَ قَدْ أَفَادَ البَزَّازِي بِقَوْلِهِ فِي حَقِّ سُقُوطِ الْوَاجِبِ: إِنَّ الْفَرَائِضَ مَعَ الرِّيَاءِ صَحِيحَةٌ مُسْقِطَةٌ لِلْوَاجِبِ، وَلكِنْ ذَكَرُوْا فِي كِتَابِ الْأضْحِيَّةِ، بِأَنَّ الْبُدْنَةَ تُجْزِى عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ، إِنْ كَانَ الْكُلُّ مُرِيدِيْنَ الْقُرْبَةَ وَإِنِ اخْتَلَفَتْ جِهَاتُهَا مِنْ أَضْحِيَّةٍ وَ قِرَانِ وَ مُتْعَةٍ، قَالُوْا فَلَوْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمْ مُرِيدًا لَحْماً لِأهْلِهِ، أَوْ كَانَ نَصْرَانِيًّا لَمْ يُجْزِ عَنْ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ، وَعَلَّلُوْا بِأَنَّ البعض إذا لَمْ يَقَعُ قُرْبَةً خَرَجَ الكُل عَن أن يكون قُرْبَةً لِأَنَّ الْإِرَاقَةَ لَا تَتَجَزَى، فَعَلَى هَذَا لَوْ ذَبَحَهَا أُضْحِيَّةٌ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَلِغَيْرِهِ لَا تُجْزِتُهُ بِالْأَوْلَى، وَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ تَحْرُمَ. ترجمه: اور بزازیہ کے قول فی حق سقوط الواجب سے معلوم ہوا کہ فرائض ریاء کے ساتھ صحیح ہیں واجب کو ساتھ کرنے والے ہیں لیکن فقہاء نے کتاب الاضحیہ میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ بدنہ سات کی طرف سے کافی ہو جاتا ہے اگر سب قربت کے چاہنے والے ہوں اگر چہ اس کی جہتیں مختلف ہوں یعنی قربانی قران اور متعہ۔ فقہاء نے فرمایا ان میں سے اگر ایک اپنے گھر والوں کے لئے گوشت کا چاہنے والا ہو یا نصرانی ہو تو ان میں سے کسی کی طرف سے کافی نہیں اور علت یہ بیان کی کہ جب بعض حصہ قربت نہ ہو تو کل قربت ہونے سے نکل جاتا ہے اس لئے کہ اراقہ دم میں تجری نہیں ہے پس اسی بیا پر اگر بدنہ کواللہ اور غیر اللہ کے لئے ذبح کیا تو بدرجہ اولی اس کے لئے کافی نہیں ہو گا اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ حرام ہو۔ تشریح: بزازیہ کے قول سے یہ معلوم ہوا کہ ریا کے ساتھ فرائض کی ادائیگی صحیح ہو جاتی ہے اور ذمہ سے واجب ساقط ہو جاتا ہے، اگر سات آدمیوں نے بد نہ قربت کی نیت سے ذبح کیا تو ساتوں آدمیوں کی طرف سے کافی ہو جائے گا اور قربانی درست ہو جائے گی، اگر چہ قربت کی جہت مختلف ہو، مثلاً کسی کی نیت قربانی کی ہو کسی کی قران کی سی کی تمتع کی لیکن اگر کسی ایک کی نیت بھی گوشت کھانے کی ہو یا کوئی ایک بھی ان میں سے نصرانی ہو، تو کسی کی قربانی درست نہ ہوگی اور اس کی علت یہ ہے کہ جب بعض کی طرف سے قربت کی نیت نہیں پائی گئی مثلا گوشت کے قصد کرنے والے کی طرف سے۔ اسی طرح اہمیت مفقود ہونے کی وجہ سے نصرانی کی طرف سے بھی قربت نہیں پائی گئی تواب کسی کی
And al-Bazzâzi has benefited by his saying regarding the dropping of obligation: The farâ'id with riyâ' are valid and drop the obligation. But they mentioned in the book of Adhiya that a budnah (camel) suffices for seven if all desire qurbah (devotion) even if their directions differ—udhiya, qiran, or tamattu'. They said: If one of them intends meat for his family, or is a Christian, it does not suffice for any of them. They reasoned that if part does not occur as qurbah, the whole ceases to be qurbah because the bloodshed is indivisible. Based on this, if he sacrificed it for Allah Ta'ala and for other than Him, a fortiori it does not suffice, and it should be prohibited. (Urdu translation and commentary follow.)
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from al-Bazzâziyya, contrasting the ruling on riyâ' in farâ'id with the stricter requirement for intention in udhiya. The author states that while farâ'id are valid despite riyâ' (as seen earlier), the sacrifice (udhiya) requires that all partners share the intention of qurbah (devotion to Allah). If one partner intends only to eat meat or is a Christian (who does not intend qurbah), then the entire sacrifice is invalid for everyone. The reasoning is that the bloodshed (irâqat al-dam) is indivisible—the act cannot be split into a devotional part and a non-devotional part. The author extends this by qiyas: if one sacrifices for Allah and for other than Allah, a fortiori it is invalid and even prohibited. The commentary emphasizes that the ruling in farâ'id is an exception related to the dropping of obligation, not to the acceptance of reward.

Key Terms
البُدْنَة (al-budnah): A sacrificial camel or cow that can be shared by up to seven participants.
القُرْبَة (al-qurbah): An act of worship performed to draw close to Allah; sincere intention for devotion.
الإِرَاقَةُ (al-irāqah): The flowing of blood (specifically from slaughter).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida in this lesson, what is the consequence if one of seven partners in a budnah intends only to eat meat (not qurbah)?
A) The sacrifice is valid for the other six, but invalid for the meat-intending partner.
B) The entire sacrifice is invalid for all seven.
C) The sacrifice is valid if the meat is shared among all.
D) The sacrifice is valid if the meat-intending partner repents after slaughter.

Key Takeaway
In shared sacrifice, the intention of qurbah must be present in every partner; otherwise the indivisible bloodshed renders the entire sacrifice invalid.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Riya' in Worship: Definition and Rulings
Quotes multiple sources to define riya' and give rulings on its effect on prayer and fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define riya', differentiate its two types, state the three Hanafi opinions on riya' in prayer, explain why riya' does not enter into fasting, and apply the principle that one should not abandon worship due to baseless fear of riya'.

Core Idea
Riya' nullifies reward but preserves the initial intention; fear of riya' must not prevent worship.

This lesson examines the concept of riya' (showing off) in worship, drawing from authoritative Hanafi sources. We will unpack its definition, its effect on prayer and fasting, and the crucial distinction between initial intention and later distraction. You will also learn the practical guidance for a mufti counseling one who fears riya'.

Guided Path
1
Define riya' from the text
Identify the two definitions given: (1) Only praying when people see, otherwise not; (2) Praying with excellence when seen, but poorly alone. Note the key phrase: 'لو خلى عن الناس لا يصلي'.
The first definition is a total dependency on audience; the second is a difference in quality.
2
Understand the ruling on riya' that enters during prayer
The passage states that if one begins purely for Allah and then riya' enters, it is judged by the initial intention. This is a key principle: the act remains valid and reward is for the original intention.
Contrast with the case where one entertains riya' without repelling it – reward may decrease.
3
Analyze the three opinions on riya' in prayer from al-Yanabi'
Ibrahim ibn Yusuf: no reward and sin; some say takfir (reject the act as if it never happened); some say no reward and no sin, as if he did not pray. Identify which opinion is relied upon (mufta bihi).
The majority of later Hanafis adopt the first opinion: sin and loss of reward.
4
Explain why riya' does not enter fasting
Fasting is hidden; one cannot show off the act itself. However, riya' can occur in informing others that one is fasting, which is a separate issue.
This highlights a general principle: riya' only affects acts that can be seen.
5
Apply the guidance from al-Walwalijiyya
If one fears riya' entering while praying or reciting Quran, one should not abandon the worship because it is a baseless fear. Instead, one should repel the thought and continue.
This is a fatwa principle: do not leave an obligation or recommended act due to mere suspicion.

وَفِي التَّاتَارُ خَانِيَّة لَوِ افْتَتَحَ خَالِصًا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى، ثُمَّ دَخَلَ فِي قَلْبِهِ الرِّيَاءُ فَهُوَ عَلَى مَا افتتح، والرِّيَاءُ أَنَّهُ لَوْ حَلَى عَن النَّاسِ لَا يُصَلَّى، وَلَوْ كَانَ مَعَ النَّاسِ يُصَلِّي فَأَمَّا لَوْ صَلَّى مَعَ النَّاسِ يُحْسِنُهَا، وَلَوْ صَلَّى وَحْدَهُ لا يُحْسِنُهَا، فَلَهُ ثَوَابُ أَصْلِ الصَّلَوَةِ دُونَ الإحْسَان وَلَا يَدْخُلُ الرِّيَاءُ فِي الصَّوْمِ. وَفِى الْيَنَابِيْعِ، قَالَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ بْنُ يُوسُف لَوْصَلَّى رِيَاءً، فَلَا أَجْرَ لَهُ، وَعَلَيْهِ الْوِزْرُ، وَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ يُكَفِّرُ، وَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ: لَا أَجْرَلَهُ، وَلَا وِزْرَ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ كَأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُصَلِّ . وَفِي الْوَلْوَالْجِيَّةِ : إِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يُصَلِّيَ، أَوْ يَقْرَا الْقُرْآنَ فَيَخَافُ أَنْ يُدْخُلَ عَلَيْهِ الرِّيَاءُ فَلا يَنبَغِى أن يُترك لأنه أمر موهوم انتهى ترجمه : اور تاتارخانیہ میں ہے کہ اگر خالص اللہ تعالی کے لئے شروع کی پھر اس کے قلب میں ریاء آگئی تو وہ اس پر محمول ہوگی جس پر شروع کی اور ریاء یہ ہے کہ اگر لوگوں سے الگ ہو جائے تو نماز نہ پڑھے اور اگر لوگوں کے ساتھ ہو تو نماز پڑھے اور بہر حال اگر لوگوں کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے تو اس کو اچھی طرح پڑھے اور اگر تنہا نماز پڑھے تو اس کو اچھی طرح نہ پڑھے تو اس کے لئے اصل نماز کا ثواب ہوگا نہ کہ اخلاص کا اور ریاء روزہ میں داخل نہیں ہوتی اور ینابيع میں ہے ابراہیم بن یوسف نے کہا اگر دکھلاوے کے طور پر نماز پڑھی تو اس کے لئے ثواب نہیں اور اس پر گناہ ہے، اور بعض نے کہا اس کی تکفیر کی جائے گی اور بعض نے کہا کہ اس کے لئے نہ اجر ہے اور نہ اس پر گناہ اور وہ کیا ہے کہ گویا اس نے نماز ہی نہیں پڑھی، اور ولوالجیہ میں ہے جب نماز پڑھنے کا ارادہ کرے یا قرآن پڑھے کا اور ڈر ہو ریا کے داخل ہونے کا تو چھوڑنا مناسب نہیں اس لئے کہ یہ امر موہوم ہے ولوالجیہ کا کلام پورا ہوا۔ تشریح : تاتارخانیہ میں ہے کہ اگر اللہ کی رضاء کے لئے نماز شروع کی اور دوران صلاۃ نماز میں ریا آگئی ہے اختبار شروع کی صورت حال کا ہوگا اسلئے کہ دور انصلا جو چیز پیش آتی ہے اس سے بچنا مشکل نہیں البتہ اگر ہاں کا خیال لایا گیا یا خود آیا اور اسے دور کرنے کی کوشش نہ کی گئی تو ثواب میں کمی ہو جائے گی۔ والرياء انه لو خلی: ریاء کے دو مطلب ہو سکتے ہیں: (۱) لوگوں کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے تو نماز پڑھ لیتا ہے اور اگر تنہائی میں ہوتا ہے تو نماز نہیں پڑھتا۔ (۲) دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر لوگوں کے سامنے نماز پڑھتا ہے تو خوب اچھی طرح ہر چیز کا خیال کر کے نماز پڑھتا ہے اور تنہائی میں ہوتا ہے تو یوں ہی جلدی جلدی نماز پڑھتا ہے پس اس صورت حال میں بھی اصل صلاۃ کا ثواب تو مل جائے گا لیکن صفت احسان مفقود ہونے کی وجہ سے احسان کا ثواب نہ ملے گا۔ عن ابي هريرة قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوماً بارزاً للناس الى قوله - ما الإحسان قال ان تعبد الله کانک تراه فان لم تكن تراه فانه براك (مسلم ج ۱، ص: ۲۹) ولا يدخل الرياء في الصوم: روزہ کے اندر ریاء کا دخل نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ریا کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ لوگوں کے سامنے روزہ کا اظہار کرے اور اندر کھائے پنے، تب اس کا وہ روزہ روزہ ہی نہ رہے گا، لہذا اس لئے یہ کہنا پڑے گا، کہ ریاء وہاں ہوتی ہے جہاں کوئی مطلع ہو سکے، اور روزہ میں یہ ممکن نہیں ہے، ہاں البتہ اس طور پر ریاء ہو سکتی ہے کہ وہ کسی کے سامنے اپنے روزہ دار ہونے کا اظہار کرے لیکن علامہ حموی نے شیخ ابن حجر شارح مشکوۃ کے حوالہ سے نقل کیا ہے کہ جب دوار گوں کے سامنے روزہ کا اظہار کرے تو ریاء روزہ میں داخل نہیں ہوتی بلکہ ریا، روزہ کی خبر دینے میں ہے۔ وفي الينابيع : ینابیع میں ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ریا نماز پڑھی تو ابراہیم ابن یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے دکھلاوے کے لئے نماز پڑھی تو کوئی ثواب نہ ملے گا بلکہ الٹا گناہ ہو گا، دوسرا قول بعض فقہا، کا یہ ہے کہ کافر ہو جائے گا، اور تیرا قول بعض فقہاء کا یہ ہے کہ نہ تو اب ملے گا اور نہ گناہ ایسا سمجھا جائے گا گویا اس نے نماز پڑھی ہی نہیں ۔ وفي الولو الجية : اگر کوئی شخص قرآن کریم پڑھنا چا ہے یا نماز پڑھنے کا ارادہ کرے اور اسے نفس میں ریاء کے داخل ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو، تو وہ محض اس امر موہوم کی وجہ سے اپنے معمول کو نہ چھوڑے، بلکہ اسے پورا کرے کیونکہ شروع میں کسی بھی عمل کے تین درجے ہوتے ہیں ۔ (۱) مشق (۲) رياء (۳) عبادت ۔ لندا محض اس شیطانی خیال کی وجہ سے اپنے معمول کو نہ چھوڑنا چاہتے بلکہ جب یہ خیال دل میں آئے جب اس وقت یہ سوچ لے کہ میں یہ عمل بندوں کے لئے نہیں کر رہا ہوں بلکہ اللہ کے لئے کر رہا ہوں اور بندہ میرے عمل کا کچھ بھی عوش نہیں دے سکتا ہے۔
In al-Tatar Khaniyya: If one begins purely for Allah, then riya enters his heart, it is considered upon what he began. Riya is that if he were alone without people, he would not pray; but if with people, he prays. Or if he prays with people, he does it well, but alone he does not do it well; then he has the reward of the original prayer, not of ihsan. And riya does not enter into fasting. In al-Yanabi‘: Ibrahim ibn Yusuf said: If one prays with riya, he has no reward, and upon him is sin. Some said: he becomes a kafir. Some said: he has no reward and no sin, and it is as if he did not pray. In al-Walwalijiyya: If one intends to pray or recite Quran and fears that riya will enter him, he should not abandon it because it is a baseless fear. End. Translation: In Tatar Khaniyya... etc.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a definition-based exploration (qawida definition) of riya (showing off) in worship, quoting multiple authoritative Hanafi sources. It begins with al-Tatar Khaniyya: if one starts an act purely for Allah, then riya enters later, it is judged by the initial intention. Two definitions of riya are given: (1) only praying when people see, otherwise not; (2) praying better when people see. In the second case, reward for the basic prayer remains but not for excellence (ihsan). Riya does not enter fasting because fasting is hidden. Then from al-Yanabi‘, there are three opinions on praying with riya: no reward + sin (Ibrahim ibn Yusuf); takfir (some); no reward and no sin (some, as if he didn't pray). From al-Walwalijiyya, one should not abandon worship due to fear of riya, as it is a mere illusion. The commentary adds that if riya appears during prayer, the initial intention is upheld; but if one consciously entertains riya without repelling it, reward decreases. It also explains the hadith on ihsan (worship as if you see Allah). Riya in fasting is not possible because it is internal, but announcing one's fasting is riya in informing, not in the fast itself. Finally, three stages of action are mentioned: hardship, riya, worship; one should resist shaytani thoughts. The main lesson is that riya is a serious issue but should not prevent worship; intentions are key, and the ruling depends on the degree of riya.

Key Terms
الرياء (al-riya'): Performing an act of worship to be seen and praised by people, not for Allah.
الإحسان (al-ihsan): Worship as if seeing Allah, with excellence and mindfulness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Walwalijiyya, what should a person do if he fears that riya' will enter his prayer or Quran recitation?
A) Stop the act immediately to avoid sin
B) Continue because it is a baseless fear
C) Make a loud announcement that he is doing it for Allah
D) Shorten the act to minimize risk

Key Takeaway
Riya' is a serious sin that nullifies the reward of worship, but a passing thought does not invalidate the act; one must not abandon worship due to unfounded fear of riya'.

Applying Intentions: The Trader, the Pilgrim, and the Debtor Seeker
Clarifies reward for trader in jihad, merchant in Hajj, and debtor-seeker in Tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to determine the entitlement to reward or booty in jihad, hajj, and tawaf, and state the mufta bihi ruling for each scenario.

Core Idea
Primary intention determines reward; subsidiary worldly purposes do not harm if the primary intention is valid.

The rule 'Actions are according to intentions' (al-umur bi-maqasidiha) is a foundational maxim of Islamic law. This lesson explores its application through three practical cases from the Hanafi tradition: a trader accompanying mujahideen, a pilgrim who trades on the way, and a person seeking a debtor while performing tawaf or standing at Arafat. By working through these examples, you will see how the primary intention governs the ruling, and how subsidiary aims do not invalidate the act if they are secondary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida and its scope
Recall the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' and note that it governs acts of worship and transactions. In this passage, it is applied to ibadat (hajj, tawaf) and jihad (siyar).
This is a kubra (major) maxim covering all chapters.
2
Analyze the first case: the trader in jihad
Examine why the trader who crosses the border with the sole intention of trade gets no share of booty. The key is his primary intention at the moment of entering dar al-harb. If he later fights, his primary intention shifts, and he becomes entitled.
Hanafi principle: 'One who enters for fighting deserves the share whether he fights or not; one who enters for other than fighting does not deserve the share even if he fights.' (from Al-Hindiya)
3
Analyze the second case: the pilgrim who trades
Consider the pilgrim whose primary intention is hajj but who engages in trade incidentally. His reward remains intact because hajj is the primary purpose. If he sets out primarily for trade, he loses the reward for hajj.
This illustrates that the intention at the start of the journey is decisive.
4
Analyze the third case: tawaf vs. wuquf seeking a debtor
Note the difference: tawaf without intention of worship is invalid because intention (niyyah) is a condition for tawaf. Wuquf at Arafat, however, is valid even without specific intention of worship because the act itself of standing suffices; seeking a debtor does not overpower the worship.
The distinction hinges on the role of intention in each act's validity.
5
Synthesize the rule
Conclude that the primary intention determines the reward or legal validity. Subsidiary worldly purposes do not affect the ruling as long as they are secondary. This is the operative rule for fatwa in Hanafi fiqh.
This is the mufta bihi position across all three scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَصَرَّحُوْا فِي كِتَابِ السِّيرِ بِأنَّ السُّوقِى لأسَهُم لَهُ، لأَنَّهُ عِنْدَ الْمُجَاوَزَةِ لَمْ يَقْصُدْ إِلَّا التِّجَارَةَ، لَا إِعْزَازَ الدِّيْنِ وَ إِرْهَابَ الْعَدُوِّ ، فَإِنْ قَاتَلَ إِسْتَحَقَّهُ؛ لِأَنَّهُ ظَهَرَ بِالْمُقَاتَلَةِ أَنَّ قصْدَهُ القِتَالُ، وَالتِّجَارَةُ تَبْع فَلَا تَضُرُّهُ كَالحَاجَّ، إِذَا إِنَّجَرَ فِي طَرِيقِ الْحَجِّ لَا يَنْقُصُ أجْرُهُ، ذَكَرَهُ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ. وَظَاهِرُهُ أَنَّ الْحَاجَّ إِذَا خَرَجَ تَاجِرًا، فَلَا أَجْرَ لَهُ، وَصَرَّحُوْا بِأَنَّهُ لَوْطَافَ طَالِبًا غَرِيْمَهُ لَا يُجْزِتُهُ، وَلَوْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ طَالِبًا غَرِيْمَهُ أَجْزَاهُ، وَالْفَرْقَ ظَاهِرٌ .

ترجمہ: اور فقہاء نے کتاب السیر میں وضاحت کی ہے کہ تاجر کے لئے کوئی حصہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے بجاتے وقت صرف تجارت کا ارادہ کیا ہے نہ کہ دین کی بلندی اور دشمن کو مرعوب کرنے کا پھر اگر و و قتال کرے تو وہ اس کا حق ہوگا اس لئے کہ تھمال سے ظاہر ہو گیا کہ اس کا اراد و قتال کا ہے اور تجارت ضمنا ہے جو اس کو مستمر نہیں ہے جیسے حج کرنے والا جنب جج کے راستہ میں تجارت کرے تو اس کا اجر کم نہ ہوگا زیلعی نے اس کو نہ کر کیا ہے، اور اس نیا ظاہر یہ ہے کہ حج کرنے والا بنب تجارت کی نیت سے نکلا تو اس کے لئے تو اب نہیں ہے اور فقہاء نے تصریح کی ہے کہ اگر وہ اپنے مقروض کو تلاش کرنے کی نیت سے طواف کرے تو اس کے لئے وہ کافی نہ ہوگا اور اگر اپنے مقریر کو تلاش کی نیت سے عرفہ میں مشہرا تو اس کو وہ کافی ہے اور فرق ظاہر ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جنب مجاہدین کا شکر دار الاسلام سے دار الحرب جہاد کے لئے نکلا تب ان کے ساتھ کوئی شخص روز مرہ کی ضروریات لیکر پھیری لگانے کے لئے ان کے ساتھ ہو گیا تو جب مال غنیمت حاصل ہوگا وہ اس پھیری کی نیت سے مجاہدین کے ساتھ جانے والے کو بھی ملے گا یا نہیں اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ اگر وہ جہاد میں شریک نہ ہوا تو اسے مال غنیمت میں سے کچھ حصہ نہ ملے گا، اس لئے کہ سرحد عبور کرتے وقت اس نے تجارت کا ارادہ کیا تھا۔ دین کی تقویت اور دشمن سے لڑنے اور ان کو بھگانے کا ارادہ نہیں تھا، اور اگر اس نے بالفعل جہاد میں شرکت کی تو سید ہاں غنیمت میں شریک ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس نے اگر چہ ابتداء مسفر تو بغرض تجارت کیا تھا لیکن بعد میں اس نے جہاد کی نیت کرلی اور اس نیت کا اختیار اس کے جہاد میں بالفعل شرکت کرنے سے ہو گیا۔ والأصل ان من دخل للقتال استحق السهم قاتل اولم يقاتل ومن دخل لغير القتال لم يستحق السهم الآن يقاتل (هند به ج ۲، ص ۲۰۸)

كالحاج إذا اتجر : اگر کوئی حاجی سفر حج کے لئے جاتا ہے اس کا مقصد حج ہی کا ہے لیکن راستہ میں ضمرہ تجارت بھی کر لیتا ہے تو اسے اس کی اجازت ہے اور اس سے اس کے اجر میں کوئی کمی نہیں آئے گی۔ لہذا اس کا ظاہری مفہوم یہ نکلتا ہے کہ اگر حاجی بھی تجارت کے مقصد سے حج کے لئے گیا تو اسے بھی اجر نہیں ملے گا۔ ويحترز من تجريد السفر من التجارة احسن ولو اتجر لا ينقض ثوابه كذا في البحر الرائق (هندیه ج ۱، ص: ۳۳۰)

وصرحوا : کسی شخص نے اپنے قرضدار کی تلاش میں نیت طواف کے بغیر طواف کیا تو اسکا یہ طواف کافی نہ ہوگا ہاں اگر طواف کی نیت کی تھی مگر مقروض کو بھی تلاش کر لیا تو اس صورت میں اس کا طواف صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ إذا طاف بالبيـت طـالـبـاً للغريم او هارباً من عدو او سبع ولا ينوى الطواف لا يجزئه طوالله (المحيط البرهانى ادارة القرآن كراچى ج ۳، ص: ۴۴۹) اور اگر کسی نے قرضدار کی تلاش میں وقوف عرفہ کیا تو اس کا یہ وقوف معتبر ہوگا، کیونکہ اس کا حصول کافی ہے اس لئے
And they explicitly stated in the book of Siyar that the trader has no share (of booty), because at the time of crossing the border he intended only trade, not the exaltation of the religion and intimidation of the enemy. But if he fights, he deserves it, because fighting shows that his intention was fighting, and trade is subsidiary, so it does not harm him, like the pilgrim who trades on the way of Hajj – his reward is not diminished. Zayla'i mentioned it. Its apparent meaning is that if a pilgrim goes out as a trader, he has no reward. And they explicitly stated that if one circumambulates seeking his debtor, it does not suffice him, but if he stands at Arafat seeking his debtor, it suffices him, and the difference is clear.

Translation: And the jurists explained in Kitab al-Siyar that the trader has no share, because at crossing he intended only trade, not exaltation of religion and intimidation of enemy. Then if he fights, he will be entitled, because fighting shows that his intention was fighting, and trade is subsidiary, which does not harm him, like the pilgrim who trades on the way of Hajj – his reward is not diminished. Zayla'i mentioned it. Its apparent meaning is that if the pilgrim went out with the intention of trade, he has no reward. And the jurists explicitly stated that if one circumambulates seeking his debtor, it does not suffice him, but if he stands at Arafat seeking his debtor, it suffices him, and the difference is clear.

Explanation of the issue: When the army of mujahideen went out from Dar al-Islam to Dar al-Harb for jihad, a person accompanied them to peddle daily necessities. When the booty is obtained, will that person who went with the intention of peddling also get a share? The detail is that if he did not participate in jihad, he will not get any share from the booty, because at the time of crossing the border he intended trade, not strengthening the religion and fighting the enemy. But if he actually participated in jihad, then he will be a partner in the booty, because even though he initially set out for trade, later he formed the intention of jihad, and this intention became effective by his actual participation in jihad. The principle: The one who enters for fighting deserves the share whether he fights or not; the one who enters for other than fighting does not deserve the share even if he fights. (Al-Hindiya, vol. 2, p. 208)

Like the pilgrim who trades: If a pilgrim goes for Hajj, his intention is Hajj, but he also engages in subsidiary trade on the way, he is permitted and his reward is not diminished. Therefore, its apparent meaning is that if the pilgrim also went for Hajj with the intention of trade, he will get no reward. 'One should avoid stripping the journey of trade, it is better; even if he trades, his reward is not nullified.' So in al-Bahr al-Raiq. (Al-Hindiya, vol. 1, p. 330)

And they explicitly stated: If a person circumambulated seeking his debtor without the intention of tawaf, his tawaf will not be sufficient. However, if he intended tawaf but also sought his debtor, then his tawaf is valid. 'If he circumambulates the House seeking a debtor, or fleeing from an enemy or a beast, and does not intend tawaf, his tawaf does not suffice him.' (Al-Muhit al-Burhani, vol. 3, p. 449) And if one stood at Arafat seeking his debtor, his standing is valid, because its achievement is sufficient for it.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage expounds the rule that the reward or entitlement in acts of worship or jihad depends on the primary intention. It presents three cases: (1) A trader who goes with the mujahideen: if he does not fight, he gets no share of booty; if he fights, he does get a share, because the fighting shows his primary intention was jihad, trade being subsidiary. (2) A pilgrim who trades on the way: if his primary intention is Hajj, trade does not diminish reward; but if he goes primarily for trade, he gets no reward. (3) Tawaf and Wuquf: if one circumambulates the Kaaba only seeking a debtor, without intending tawaf, it is not valid; but if one stands at Arafat seeking a debtor, it is valid because the act of standing itself suffices, and the intention of seeking a debtor does not overpower the worship. The principle is that the primary intention determines the ruling; subsidiary worldly purposes do not affect it.

Key Terms
سهم (sahm): Share of booty for a participant in jihad
مغازاة (mugazat): Crossing the border into enemy territory for jihad
أجزاء (ijzaa): Sufficiency of an act to fulfill the obligation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a trader who crosses the border with the mujahideen with the sole intention of trade but then actually fights?
A) He gets no share of booty because his initial intention was trade.
B) He gets a share because his actual participation shows his intention became jihad.
C) He becomes a kafir.
D) He gets share only if he intended jihad from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' is applied to determine reward and validity based on the primary intention, with subsidiary worldly aims not affecting the ruling.

Maxim: What is Included Does Not Need Separate Intention
Determining when a separate niyyah is required in acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'ما ضمن غيره لا يحتاج إلى نية مستقلة' to distinguish when a separate niyyah is required in acts of worship, using Tawaf and Wuquf as key examples.

Core Idea
An act included under a main ritual is covered by its intention; an independent act needs its own.

In Hanafi fiqh, intention (niyyah) is a prerequisite for most acts of worship. However, not every act within a larger ritual requires a fresh intention. This passage from the Ashbah wa al-Nazair literature establishes a critical refinement: acts that are inherently included (ضمن) under a main ritual are automatically covered by the ritual's intention, whereas independent acts demand their own. As a mufti, recognizing this distinction prevents invalidating acts that are actually valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act's relationship to the ritual
Determine whether the act is a component of a broader worship (e.g., Wuquf is part of Hajj) or a standalone act (e.g., Tawaf can be performed independently).
Wuquf is a rukn of Hajj; Tawaf is a sunnah that can be done anytime.
2
Apply the maxim
Apply the maxim 'ما ضمن غيره لا يحتاج إلى نية مستقلة': if the act is included, the main intention suffices; if independent, a separate intention is required.
This maxim is a dabt under the larger principle 'الأمور بمقاصدها'.
3
Test with the given furu' (cases)
Apply the maxim to the two cases: (1) Tawaf without niyyah of Tawaf is invalid; (2) Wuquf without separate niyyah but seeking debtor is valid.
The text explicitly contrasts these to illustrate the rule.
4
Extend to a new scenario
Consider Sa'i between Safa and Marwa performed without separate intention but seeking a friend. Is it valid? (Answer: It is included in Hajj, so valid, similar to Wuquf).
This helps internalize the rule's scope.

Source Text

وصرحوا : کسی شخص نے اپنے قرضدار کی تلاش میں نیت طواف کے بغیر طواف کیا تو اسکا یہ طواف کافی نہ ہوگا ہاں اگر طواف کی نیت کی تھی مگر مقروض کو بھی تلاش کر لیا تو اس صورت میں اس کا طواف صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ إذا طاف بالبيـت طـالـبـاً للغريم او هارباً من عدو او سبع ولا ينوى الطواف لا يجزئه طوالله
المحيط البرهانى ادارة القرآن کراچی ج ۳، ص : ۴۴۹)
اور اگر کسی نے قرضدار کی تلاش میں وقوف عرفہ کیا تو اس کا یہ وقوف معتبر ہوگا، کیونکہ اس کا حصول کافی ہے اس لئے
نیت بھی لازم نہیں ہے، جہاں تحصیل ضروری ہوتی ہے اس میں نیت بھی لازم ہوتی ہے، نیز حج کے افعال میں وقوف عرفہ بھی شامل ہے اور جب حاجی حج کی نیت کرتا ہے تو اس میں وقوف بھی شامل ہو جاتا ہے بخلاف طواف کے اگر چہ طواف اس احرام کے ضمن میں ایک فعل ہے لیکن من وجہ مستقل بذاتہ معلوم ہوتا ہے تو اس میں احتیاط یہی ہے کہ مستقل نیت کو لازم کیا جائے اور طواف میں صرف مقروض کو تلاش کرنے کی نیت تھی نہ کہ طواف کی اس لئے طواف ادا نہ ہو گا۔
And they explicitly stated: If a person performs Tawaf around the House seeking a debtor or fleeing from an enemy or a beast without intending Tawaf, his Tawaf is not valid. But if he intended Tawaf and also sought the debtor, then his Tawaf is valid. From al-Muhit al-Burhani. And if a person performed Wuquf at Arafat seeking a debtor, his Wuquf is valid, because its attainment is sufficient; therefore intention is not required. Where attainment is necessary, intention is also necessary. Moreover, Wuquf at Arafat is included among the actions of Hajj, and when a pilgrim intends Hajj, Wuquf is included in it, unlike Tawaf. Although Tawaf is also an action within Ihram, it is considered an independent act in some respects, so caution demands that a separate intention be required. In the case of Tawaf, he only intended to seek the debtor, not Tawaf, so the Tawaf is not valid.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage refines the general principle of intention (niyyah) by distinguishing between two acts: Tawaf and Wuquf. Tawaf is considered an independent act that requires its own separate intention; therefore, if one simply intends to find a debtor, the Tawaf is invalid. However, if one intended Tawaf and also incidentally sought a debtor, the Tawaf remains valid. Wuquf at Arafat, on the contrary, is not an independent act but a part of the overall Hajj ritual. Once a person intends Hajj, all its components, including Wuquf, are covered by that single intention. Hence, even if one also intends to find a debtor, the Wuquf is valid. The reasoning given is that when an act is included (dakhil) under the main act, no separate intention is needed; when it is independent (mustaqill), a specific intention is required.

Key Terms
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah, an independent act of worship requiring its own niyyah.
وقوف عرفہ (wuquf 'arafah): Standing at Arafat, a fundamental part of Hajj, included in the overall Hajj intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Wuquf at Arafat not require a separate intention when performed while seeking a debtor?
A) Because Wuquf is not an act of worship
B) Because it is included under the overall intention of Hajj
C) Because seeking a debtor is a valid intention for worship
D) Because the jurists made an exception for Wuquf

Key Takeaway
An act that is included within a larger ritual does not require its own intention; an independent act does.

Intention Required for Independent Acts of Worship: The Case of Tawaf
Applying the rule that intention is necessary where the act is perceived as independent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida on intention to determine when a separate niyyah is required for an act of worship, and identify the ruling when intention is missing.

Core Idea
An act perceived as independent requires its own intention; if missing, the act is invalid.

This lesson examines a subtle yet crucial Hanafi legal maxim regarding intention (niyyah) in acts of worship. The key insight is that some acts are automatically covered by a general intention, while others—though part of a larger ritual—are considered independent and demand their own specific intention. The passage uses two Hajj-related cases—standing at Arafah and Tawaf—to illustrate this distinction, ultimately ruling that a Tawaf performed without its own intention (e.g., solely to search for a debtor) is invalid. Understanding this dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) will sharpen your ability to identify when intention is required as a condition for validity.

Guided Path
1
State the Qawida and Scope
Identify the sub-maxim (dabt) from the passage: 'Intention is not necessary where it is not required, but where acquisition is necessary, intention is also necessary.' Note the scope: it applies to acts of worship (Ibadat) where the act is perceived as an independent entity.
The maxim does not apply to acts that are inherently part of a composite worship without independent recognition.
2
Apply to the Furu' of Waqoof Arafah
Examine the case of standing at Arafah: it is an integral part of Hajj but is not perceived as an independent act. When the pilgrim intends Hajj, the intention automatically covers Waqoof. Therefore, no separate intention is required.
The key factor: the act is not considered 'independent' (mustaqil).
3
Apply to the Furu' of Tawaf
Contrast with Tawaf: though it is performed during Ihram, it is considered an independent act (mustaqil bi dhatihi). Hence, a separate intention for Tawaf is required. If one intends only to search for a debtor, the Tawaf is invalid.
The reason given: 'min wajhin mustaqil bi dhatihi' – it is perceived as independent in one aspect.
4
Derive the Ruling and Practical Consequence
Combine the qawida and furu' to state the operative ruling: any act of worship that is viewed as independent in the fiqh tradition requires its own intention, and omission of that intention renders the act invalid (ghayr sahih). The mufta bihi position for fatwa is that Tawaf without specific niyyah is not valid.
This ruling applies irrespective of the original general intention (e.g., intending Hajj).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نیت بھی لازم نہیں ہے، جہاں تحصیل ضروری ہوتی ہے اس میں نیت بھی لازم ہوتی ہے، نیز حج کے افعال میں وقوف عرفہ بھی شامل ہے اور جب حاجی حج کی نیت کرتا ہے تو اس میں وقوف بھی شامل ہو جاتا ہے بخلاف طواف کے اگر چہ طواف اس احرام کے ضمن میں ایک فعل ہے لیکن من وجہ مستقل بذاتہ معلوم ہوتا ہے تو اس میں احتیاط یہی ہے کہ مستقل نیت کو لازم کیا جائے اور طواف میں صرف مقروض کو تلاش کرنے کی نیت تھی نہ کہ طواف کی اس لئے طواف ادا نہ ہو گا۔
Intention is also not necessary. Where acquisition is necessary, intention is also necessary. Similarly, among the acts of Hajj, standing at Arafah is included, and when the pilgrim intends Hajj, standing is also included. Unlike Tawaf, although Tawaf is an act within the state of Ihram, but in one aspect it is perceived as independent in itself, so caution is that independent intention be required. And in Tawaf, the intention was only to search for the debtor, not Tawaf, so Tawaf is not valid.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage discusses the rule of intention (niyyah) in acts of worship. It states that intention is not required in acts that are automatically subsumed under a broader intention, such as standing at Arafah during Hajj. However, if an act is perceived as an independent act, like Tawaf, a separate intention is required. The ruling is that if someone makes Tawaf purely to search for a debtor, without intending the Tawaf itself, the Tawaf is invalid. This is a Hanafi understanding based on the principle that acts are judged by their intentions, and caution demands specifying intention for potentially independent acts.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): The mental intention or purpose to perform a specific act of worship.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba, an act of worship in Hajj and Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
اگر کوئی شخص صرف مقروض کی تلاش کے لیے طواف کرے تو اس کا طواف کیا حکم رکھتا ہے؟
A) درست ہے
B) درست نہیں ہے
C) مکروہ ہے
D) واجب الاعادہ ہے

Key Takeaway
An act of worship that is perceived as independent in fiqh requires its own specific intention; without it, the act is invalid.

Prompting a Non-Imam: Intention Decides Validity
Stating the Hanafi ruling that talqin (prompting) someone other than the imam invalidates prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to the case of talqin (prompting) during prayer and identify when the prayer is invalidated by the intention to teach.

Core Idea
Intent to teach turns speech into worldly talk, invalidating prayer; intent to recite keeps prayer valid.

This lesson unpacks a specific furu' (branch) case from Hanafi fiqh: prompting someone other than the imam during prayer. The ruling hinges on intention – a direct application of the great legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'. Understanding this case sharpens your ability to apply qawaid to real scenarios and to see how intention transforms the legal nature of an act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
Find the act being ruled upon: prompting (al-fatḥ) someone other than the imam during prayer. What is the stated hukm?
The text says 'prayer becomes invalid' (batalat salatuhu).
2
Locate the underlying qawida
What principle justifies this ruling? The passage implies 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'. Identify the explicit link: the intention to teach (qaṣd al-taʿlīm) transforms the speech.
This is a classic example of the major maxim.
3
Analyse how the qawida applies
Explain the legal link: teaching intent makes the recitation resemble worldly speech (kalam al-nas), which is an invalidator of prayer. Without that intent, it remains recitation (tilaawah) and is valid.
The distinction is purely based on niyyah.
4
Note the exception
The text provides an exception: if the person intends recitation rather than teaching, the prayer is not invalidated. Identify this from the text.
This exception confirms the rule depends on intention.
5
Identify the istithna' (if any) from the maxim
For the qawida itself, is there any exception stated? The text does not mention an exception to the maxim, only a different application within it.
The maxim itself is universal; the specific furu' shows its operation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالُوا: لَوْفَتَحَ الْمُصَلَّى عَلَى غَيْرِ إِمَامِهِ بَطَلَتْ صَلَاتُهُ لِقَصْدِ التَّعْلِيمِ. ترجمه: اور فقہاء فرماتے ہیں اگر نمازی اپنے امام کے علاوہ کولقمہ دے تو اس کی نماز باطل ہو جائے گی تعلیم کے ارادہ کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح: اگر کسی شخص نے اپنے امام کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے کو لقمہ دید یا تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی کیونکہ تعلیم کا قصد پائے جانے کی وجہ سے وہ کلام الناس کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور کلام الناس مفسد صلاۃ ہے۔ ولو فتح على غير امامه تفسد الا اذا عنى به التلاوة دون التعليم (هنديه ج ١ ، ص: ٩٩)
And they said: If a praying person prompts someone other than his imam, his prayer becomes invalid due to the intention of teaching. Translation: And the jurists say: If a praying person prompts someone other than his imam, his prayer becomes invalid due to the intention of teaching. Explanation: If a person prompts someone other than his imam, his prayer becomes invalid because due to the presence of the intention of teaching, it resembles the speech of people, and speech of people is an invalidator of prayer. And if he prompts someone other than his imam, it invalidates unless he intends recitation (tilaawah) and not teaching. (Hindiyya vol.1 p.99)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on talqin (prompting) during prayer. According to the Hanafi school, if a praying person corrects or prompts someone other than his own imam with the intention of teaching, his prayer is invalidated. The reason is that the intention of teaching transforms the act of speaking into a human conversation, which breaks the prayer. An exception is noted: if he intends merely to recite (tilaawah) without teaching, the prayer remains valid. This is a direct application of the principle that acts are judged by intentions (al-umur bi maqasidiha).

Key Terms
الفتح على غير الإمام (al-fatḥ ʿalā ghayr al-imām): Prompting or correcting someone other than the imam during prayer.
قصد التعليم (qaṣd al-taʿlīm): Intention to teach, which makes the speech resemble worldly speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does prompting a non-imam with teaching intent invalidate prayer?
A) Because any act of teaching is prohibited in prayer.
B) Because the speech becomes like worldly talk (kalam al-nas), which is an invalidator.
C) Because the imam is the only one allowed to speak.
D) Because the prayer becomes null if any mistake is heard.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, prompting a non-imam during prayer invalidates the prayer only if the intention is to teach; if the intention is recitation, the prayer remains valid, illustrating 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'.

Mixed Intention: Worship and Worldly Purpose
Explores ruling when worship and non-worship intentions are combined

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that mixing worship and non-worship intentions does not invalidate the act but negates reward, and identify the underlying legal maxim.

Core Idea
Mixed intention in worship: the act is valid but the reward is lost.

What happens when a person fasts intending both worship and health benefits? This lesson explores a subtle distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the difference between validity (juz') and reward (thawab). The source passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir examines a case that the original author had not seen explicitly ruled upon, but later commentators like Allama Hamawi provided guidance. Understanding this nuance is essential for a mufti answering questions about intention in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the two questions
The author asks: if a person intends fasting and dieting together, is the worship valid? And if valid, is there any reward? This sets up the problem of mixed intention.
The same principle applies to any act combining worship and non-worship.
2
Distinguish validity from reward
Hanafis separate the legal sufficiency of an act (fulfilling the obligation) from the spiritual reward (which depends on pure intention). Here, the act may be valid in form but reward may be diminished or absent.
This distinction is critical for fatwa: a person may fulfill their duty but gain no reward.
3
Apply the maxim 'reward follows intention'
The underlying legal maxim is that reward is directly tied to the sincerity of intention. When intention is divided, the portion devoted to Allah determines reward.
Hashiyat al-Hamawi confirms: worship is valid with respect to validity (ijza'), but no reward.
4
Derive the fatwa consequence
For a mufti, the operative ruling is: the fast (or similar worship) is valid and the obligation is discharged, but the person does not earn reward for the worldly portion. They should be advised to purify their intention.
This does not mean the act is sinful; it is simply neutral regarding reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمْ از حُكْمَ مَا إِذَا نَوَى الصَّومَ وَالْحِمْيَةَ، وَيَشْمُلُهُمَا مَا إِذَا أَشْرَكَ بَيْنَ عِبَادَةٍ وَ غَيْرِهَا، فَهَلْ تَصِحُ الْعِبَادَةُ، وَ إِذَا صَحْتُ فَهَل يُقربُ بِقَدْرِهِ أَوْ لَا تَوَابَ لَهُ أَصْلاً. :ترجمہ: اور میں نے اس صورت کا حکم نہیں دیکھا جبکہ کوئی روزہ اور پر ہیز کی نیت کرے اور ان دونوں کو وہ صورت بھی شامل ہے کہ جب کوئی عبادت اور غیر عبادت کو شریک کرلے تو کیا عبادت صحیح ہے اور اگر صحیح ہے تو کیا اس کے بقدر ثواب ملے گا یا اس کو بالکلیہ ثواب ہی نہیں ملے گا۔ تشریح صاحب کتاب کہتے ہیں کہ یہ جزئیہ میری نظروں سے نہیں گذرا، فقہاء نے یہ مسئلہ ذکر کیا ہے کہ کسی شخص نے روزہ رکھا اور نیت پر ہیز و علاج کی تھی تو اس کا روزہ صحیح ہو جائے گا کیونکہ پر ہیز اور علاج کا حصول اس عبادت کی ضرورت میں سے ہے۔ اب اس پر یہ مسلہ متفرع ہوتا ہے کہ کسی شخص نے عبادت کےساتھ غیر عبادت کو بھی نبیت میں ملاد یا تو وہ عبادت سیح ہوگی یا نہیں اور اس پر ثواب ملے گا یا نہیں ، علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ عبادت تو صحیح ہو جائے گا لیکن ثواب نہیں ملے گا۔ وما صححوه فى هذه الصورة هو بالنسبة الى الاجزاء واما الثواب فلا (حاشيه الحموي ص:٧٧)
And I have not seen the ruling on when one intends fasting and dieting (for health), and included in this is when one combines between worship and non-worship: Is the worship valid? And if valid, will he be rewarded according to it or will he have no reward at all? Translation: 'And I have not seen the ruling on this case when one intends fasting and dieting, and included in them is that case when one mixes worship and non-worship. So is the worship valid? And if valid, will he be rewarded proportionately or have no reward at all?' Explanation: The author (of the book) says: This case has not passed before my eyes. The jurists have mentioned this issue: If a person kept a fast with the intention of diet and treatment, his fast will be valid because obtaining diet and treatment is part of the need of this worship. Now this case branches out: if a person mixes non-worship with worship in his intention, will the worship be valid or not? And will he get reward? Allama Hamawi says: The worship will be valid, but he will not receive reward. 'And what they have validated in this case is with respect to validity (of the act), but as for reward, no' (Hashiyat al-Hamawi, p. 77).
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a nuanced problem in Hanafi fiqh: what happens when a person's intention in an act of worship is mixed with a worldly purpose? The author quotes an Arabic text (likely from a fiqh reference) saying he has not encountered a specific ruling for the case of intending both fasting (sawm) and dieting (himyah). The same principle extends to any mixing of worship and non-worship in intention. The issue is analyzed in two stages: first, is the worship valid? Second, does it bring reward? The author of the book (the original author of al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir) says he hasn't seen the case explicitly. However, standard Hanafi texts hold that if someone fasts with the intention of diet and treatment, the fast is valid because the worldly benefit is a means to fulfill the worship (strengthening the body for worship). But that is a case of underlying motive, not mixed intention. The branching case (far') is when one actively mixes worship and non-worship in the intention itself. Allama Hamawi (a prominent Hanafi commentator) rules: the worship is valid (in terms of form and legal obligation fulfilled) but there is no reward (thawab) because the intention is not purely for Allah. This distinction between validity (juz') and reward (thawab) is important: acts are valid as long as the essential conditions are met, but reward depends on sincerity. The teacher notes that this reflects the Hanafi principle that niyyah is a condition for reward, not necessarily for the validity of obligatory acts (like fasting Ramadan), but here even for optional worship? The text implies worship is valid but reward is lost. This is a critical refinement for understanding the role of intention in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
پرہیز (parhaiz): Diet or treatment (medical regimen) intended alongside fasting.
ثواب (thawab): Reward from Allah; here differentiated from validity (juz').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Allama Hamawi, if a person fasts with intention of both worship and diet, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is invalid.
B) The fast is valid but there is no reward.
C) The fast is valid and full reward is earned.
D) The fast is valid only if the diet intention is dominant.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, mixing a worldly intention with worship does not invalidate the act, but the reward is lost for the portion intended for other than Allah.

Khushu' and Involuntary Distraction in Prayer: Effect on Reward
Rulings on khushu' in prayer and the effect of involuntary distraction on reward

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on involuntary distraction in prayer to determine when repetition is recommended and when reward is affected.

Core Idea
Khushu' is mustahabb; involuntary distractions do not reduce reward or require repetition.

This lesson clarifies a common concern: do involuntary thoughts during prayer affect its validity or reward? The Hanafi school provides a clear and lenient ruling. We examine the key text from al-Qunyah and the commentaries in Radd al-Muhtar. By the end, you will be able to parse the ruling and apply it in fatwa contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on khushu'
The text states al-khushu' is mustahabb (recommended). Recognize that this means it is not obligatory (wajib or fard).
Mustahabb: performing it earns reward, but leaving it does not incur sin.
2
Distinguish between voluntary and involuntary distraction
The passage discusses distraction during prayer. It distinguishes between distraction due to one's own negligence and distraction that occurs involuntarily.
The key phrase: 'إذا لم يكن من تقصير منه' (if not due to negligence).
3
Apply the ruling on repetition and reward
If distraction is involuntary, repetition is not recommended (la tustahabb al-i'ada) and reward is not decreased. If due to negligence, some scholars say reward decreases.
There is a difference: some say decrease occurs if distraction lasts for the duration of one pillar.
4
Resolve the intra-madhhab difference
The text cites al-Baqqali and another opinion about per-pillar reduction. Recognize that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that reward decreases only if there is negligence, not merely by duration.
Involuntary whispers (waswas) are forgiven (ma'fu anhu).
5
Construct the fatwa
When a mufti is asked about distraction in prayer, he should first ascertain if the person was negligent. If not, the prayer is valid with full reward. If negligent, advise seeking forgiveness but still no repetition required.
This aligns with the general principle that acts of worship are valid as long as essential conditions and pillars are fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْخُشُوعُ فِيْهَا بِظَاهِرِهِ وَ بَاطِنِهِ فَمُسْتَحَبُّ. وَفِي الْقِنْيَةِ : شَرَعَ فِي الْفَرْضِ وَ شَغَلَهُ الفِكْرُ فِي التِّجَارَةِ، أَوِ الْمَسْأَلَةِ حَتَّى أَتَمَّ صَلَا تَهُ لَا تَسْتَحِبُّ إِعَادَتُهُ وَفِي بَعْضٍ الكتبِ : لَا يُعِيدُ، وَفِي بَعْضِهَا : لَمْ يَنْقُصُ أَجْرُهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ تَقْصِيرٍ مِّنْهُ إِنْتَهَى. ترجمه : اور بہر حال نماز میں خشوع اپنے ظاہر و باطن میں تو وہ مستحب ہے اور قنیہ میں ہے کہ کسی نے فرض نماز شروع کی اور وہ تجارت یا کسی اور مسئلہ کی سوچ و چار میں لگ گیا حتی کہ اس نے اپنی نماز پوری کر دی تو اس کا اعادہ منتخب نہیں اور بعض کتابوں میں ہے کہ وہ نہ لوٹائے اور بعض کتابوں میں ہے کہ اگر یہ اس کی کوتاہی سے نہ ہو تو اس کا ثواب کم نہیں : وگا قتیہ کی بات پوری ہوئی۔ تشریح نماز میں خشوع و خضوع مستحب ہے، لہذا اگر کوئی نماز خشوع و خضوع کے بغیر بھی پڑھ لی جائے تو اعادہ مستحب نہیں ہے فلو اشتغل قلبه يتفكر مسئلة مثلاً في اثناء الاركان فلا تستحب الاعادة “
(شامی ج ۱ ص : ۴۱۴)
اگر کسی شخص نے نماز شروع کی اور خیالات ذہن میں اترنا شروع ہو گئے تو اس کے اجر میں کمی ہوگی یا نہیں ؟ شرعی حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر خیالات بالا اختیار آئے ہوں تو اس سے اجر میں کمی نہ ہو گی اگر چہ بعض نے یہ بھی کہا ہے کہ اگر ایک رکن کے برابر خیالات آئیں تو اجر میں کمی ہوگی ورنہ نہیں " و قال البـقـال لـم ينقص اجره الا اذا قصر وقيل
يلزم فى كل ركن ولا يؤاخذ بالسمو لانه معفو عنه " (شمالی جا : ۴۱۷)
As for khushu' (humility) in it, outwardly and inwardly, it is mustahabb (recommended). And in al-Qunyah: One began an obligatory prayer and his mind was occupied with trade or a matter until he completed his prayer; its repetition is not recommended. And in some books: he does not repeat it, and in some: his reward is not decreased if it was not due to negligence on his part. End. Translation: And in any case, khushu' in prayer, outwardly and inwardly, is mustahabb. In al-Qunyah: Someone started an obligatory prayer and became absorbed in thinking about trade or some other issue until he completed his prayer, then its repetition is not recommended. In some books: he does not repeat it, and in some books: his reward does not decrease if it was not due to his negligence. Commentary: Khushu' in prayer is mustahabb, so if someone prays without khushu', repeating it is not recommended. If his heart is occupied thinking about a matter, for example, during the pillars, then repeating it is not recommended. (Shami vol. 1 p. 414) If a person starts prayer and thoughts enter his mind, will his reward decrease? The legal ruling: if the thoughts come involuntarily, his reward does not decrease. Some have said that if thoughts come for the duration of one pillar, reward decreases, otherwise not. And al-Baqqali said: his reward does not decrease unless he is negligent. And it is said: it applies to every pillar, and he is not held accountable for whispers because they are forgiven. (Shami vol. 1 p. 417)
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of khushu' (humility and concentration) in prayer. It first states that khushu' is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. Therefore, if one prays without khushu', it is not necessary to repeat the prayer. The text then cites al-Qunyah on distraction: if a person starts an obligatory prayer and becomes mentally occupied with trade or a matter, but completes the prayer, repeating it is not recommended. There is a difference in books: some say don't repeat, some say reward is not decreased if the distraction was not due to negligence. The commentary adds that if thoughts are involuntary, reward is not decreased. Some scholars distinguish: if the distraction persists for the duration of one pillar (e.g., the time to say Subhanallah three times), reward decreases; otherwise not. Al-Baqqali holds reward decreases only if there is negligence. Involuntary whispers (waswas) are forgiven. This shows that the Hanafi position is lenient: khushu' is recommended, and involuntary distractions do not affect the validity or reward of prayer, as long as the essential actions are performed.

Key Terms
الخُشُوع (al-khushu'): Humility, concentration, and mental presence in prayer, both outwardly (body) and inwardly (heart).
مُسْتَحَبّ (mustahabb): Recommended; performing it earns reward, but omitting it does not incur sin or require compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person prays without khushu' due to involuntary thoughts, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but the person sins for lacking khushu'.
C) The prayer is valid and reward is not decreased if thoughts were involuntary.
D) The prayer is valid but reward is always decreased regardless.

Key Takeaway
Involuntary distractions during prayer do not invalidate it or reduce reward, as khushu' is recommended, not obligatory.
