Combining Fard and Nafl Intentions in Prayer: The Stronger Prevails
Ruling on multiple intentions in prayer with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-aqwa yaghlib al-ad'af' to resolve conflicts of intention in prayer and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The stronger intention (fard) prevails over the weaker (nafl); the weaker is voided.

When a worshipper intends both a fard and a nafl prayer simultaneously, which intention takes effect? The Hanafi school resolves this through a general legal maxim: the stronger (aqwa) overrides the weaker (ad'af). However, there is an internal disagreement about whether the weaker is cancelled or both are nullified. This lesson unpacks the qawida, the ikhtilaf, and the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Governing Qawida
Identify the maxim 'al-aqwa yaghlib al-ad'af' ('the stronger prevails over the weaker when they conflict') and note its rank (wusta) and type (nathr).
This qawida is a sub-maxim of the larger principle of tarjih (preponderance).
2
Identify the Scope of the Qawida
Recognize that this maxim applies to acts of worship where multiple intentions (niyyat) are made simultaneously, especially when one is superior (e.g., fard vs. nafl).
Does not apply when the intentions are equal in strength; then ta'arud applies.
3
Work Through the Furu' (Application)
Apply the qawida to the specific case: a person intends both fard and nafl prayer. According to Abu Yusuf, the fard (stronger) annuls the nafl, so the prayer counts as fard. According to Imam Muhammad, the two descriptions conflict (ta'arud), so no prayer is valid.
The difference arises from whether the stronger intention completely overrides the weaker or both descriptions are mutually exclusive.
4
Identify the Istithna' (Exception)
Note that when the two intentions are equal (e.g., two nafls of equal rank), the qawida does not apply; instead, ta'arud leads to either invalidity or need for another criterion.
This exception shows the qawida is not universal.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Relied-upon Position)
Identify that Abu Yusuf's view is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi madhhab: if someone intends fard and nafl together, the fard suffices and the nafl is void.
Fatwa is given accordingly, as per al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابویوسف کے نزدیک اقوی کا اعتبار ہوگا اور وہ نیت فرض کی طرف سے کافی ہوگی اور نفل باطل ہو جائے گی اور امام محمد کے نزدیک و دو صفوں میں تعارض ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ اصلا نماز میں داخل ہی نہیں ہوا۔
ولو نوى الفرض و التطوع جاز عن الفرض عند ابي يوسف لان الفرض اقوى من النفل فلا يعارضه فتلغو نية النقل وتبقى نية الفرض وقال محمد لا يكون داخلاً في الصلاة اصلا لتعارض الوصفين (البحر الرائق ج ١ ، ص : ۲۸۱)
If one intends fard and tatawwu', it suffices for the fard according to Abu Yusuf because the fard is stronger than the nafl, so it does not oppose it, so the intention of nafl is voided and the intention of fard remains. Muhammad said: he does not enter the prayer at all due to the conflict of the two descriptions.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage presents a legal ruling on multiple intentions in prayer. The author states Abu Yusuf's position: when someone simultaneously intends a fard and a nafl prayer, the fard prevails because it is stronger. The intention for the nafl is cancelled, and the prayer counts as the fard. Imam Muhammad, however, holds that the two descriptions (fard and nafl) conflict, so the person does not enter into any prayer at all. This ikhtilaf is based on whether the stronger one nullifies the weaker or both descriptions are mutually exclusive. The passage is from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary supererogatory act of worship
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict or contradiction between two legal descriptions or intentions
فرض (fard): Obligatory act of worship; established by definitive evidence (qat'i)
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary worship (synonym of nafl)
أقوى (aqwa): Stronger; used legally to denote superior evidence or intention weight

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The fard is valid and the nafl is void
C) The nafl is valid and the fard is void
D) Both are valid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the principle that the stronger legal description (aqwa) prevails over the weaker, thus the fard prayer is valid even if combined with nafl intention.

The Stronger Prevails: Zakat and Voluntary Sadaqa Intentions
Ruling when intending zakat and voluntary charity simultaneously.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-aqwa yaghlib al-ad'af' to cases of multiple intentions in charity and determine the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
When zakat and voluntary sadaqa are intended together, the stronger (obligatory) prevails over the weaker (voluntary).

This lesson examines a specific application of the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-aqwa yaghlib al-ad'af' (the stronger prevails over the weaker). The case involves a donor who gives money to a poor person intending both zakat and voluntary sadaqa. The Hanafi masters differ on which intention takes effect. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply qawaid to furuat and to navigate intra-madhhab differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim
State the qawida being applied: 'al-aqwa yaghlib al-ad'af' (the stronger prevails over the weaker). Recognize that this maxim operates across multiple fiqh chapters, including ibadat and muamalat.
The maxim is a wusta (intermediate) maxim, not universal.
2
Understand the Case
Identify the two intentions: zakat (obligatory, aqwa) and voluntary sadaqa (nafil, ad'af). The donor gives a single payment intending both.
The recipient is a poor person, so both acts are valid in themselves.
3
Follow the Ikhtilaf
Compare the two positions: Abu Yusuf says zakat prevails, so the payment discharges zakat and the voluntary intention is void. Muhammad says the payment suffices for the voluntary charity.
Muhammad's reasoning is not given in the text but may relate to specificity of intention.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is Abu Yusuf's, because zakat is stronger as a wajib. Apply this in fatwa.
The tarjih is based on the maxim itself: the stronger overrides the weaker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و إن نوى الزكوة و التطوع کسی شخص نے کسی فقیر کو ایک ہی وقت میں زکوۃ اور صدقہ نافلہ کی نیت سے کچھ دیا تو زکوۃ کے اقوی ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ زکوۃ کی طرف سے کافی ہوگا اور صدقہ نافلہ کی نیت باطل قرار پائے گی اور امام محمد کے نزدیک وہ نیت نقل کی طرف سے کافی ہو جائے گی۔
If one intends zakat and tatawwu' (voluntary charity), and a person gives something to a poor person with the intention of both zakat and voluntary sadaqa, then due to zakat being stronger, it will suffice for the zakat and the intention of voluntary sadaqa will be void. According to Imam Muhammad, it will suffice for the voluntary charity.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage applies the same principle of 'stronger prevails' to charity. When someone gives money intending both zakat (obligatory) and voluntary sadaqa, Abu Yusuf holds that zakat, being obligatory, is stronger, so the payment counts as zakat and the voluntary intention is voided. Imam Muhammad, however, holds that the payment suffices for the voluntary charity. The reason for Muhammad's view is not given here, but it may be based on priority of the voluntary when the obligatory is not clearly intended. The ikhtilaf mirrors the earlier prayer example.

Key Terms
زكوة (zakat): Obligatory alms tax, one of the five pillars
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary charity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a person gives money intending both zakat and voluntary sadaqa, what is the ruling according to Abu Yusuf?
A) It counts as voluntary sadaqa only
B) It counts as zakat only
C) It counts as both
D) It is invalid

Key Takeaway
When intentions conflict, the stronger (obligatory) overrides the weaker (voluntary); in zakat vs nafl, zakat prevails.

Combining Nafl and Janaza Prayer Intentions
Ruling when intending nafl and janaza prayer simultaneously

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-aqwa yaghlib al-ad'af' to determine which prayer intention prevails when conflicting, and identify the dimensions of strength (obligation vs. structural completeness).

Core Idea
When two intentions conflict, the stronger prevails — strength is measured by both obligation and structural completeness.

In this lesson, we examine a case where a person intends both a nafl prayer (with ruku' and sujud) and a janaza prayer (which lacks these) simultaneously. The ruling reveals that the nafl prayer is valid, not the janaza, even though janaza is a communal obligation. This illustrates that 'strength' in the Hanafi maxim 'al-aqwa yaghlib al-ad'af' considers not only the legal status but also the structural integrity of the act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting intentions
The worshipper intends both a nafl prayer and a janaza prayer at the same time. Recognize that janaza prayer has no ruku' or sujud.
2
Assess each act's strength dimensions
Janaza is fard kifaya (obligatory) but structurally deficient (no ruku'/sujud). Nafl is supererogatory but structurally complete (has ruku'/sujud).
Strength is not monolithic; it has multiple facets.
3
Apply the maxim 'al-aqwa yaghlib al-ad'af'
Determine which act is 'stronger' overall. The Hanafi view weighs structural completeness as a significant factor alongside obligation.
The stronger in this context is the nafl.
4
Derive the ruling
The nafl prayer is valid; the janaza is not fulfilled. The intention for janaza is overridden.
If janaza were intended alone, it would be valid as a separate prayer.
5
Support with authoritative sources
The ruling is reported from al-Zahiriyya and cited in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, affirming the mufta bihi position.
Later Hanafi texts rely on this reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو نوى نافلة وجنازة: اگر کسی نے نماز جنازہ اور نفل نماز کی ایک ساتھ نیت کی تو فل نماز صحیح ہو جائے گی جنازہ کی نماز نہیں یہاں پر اشکال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ ظاہر ہے کہ نماز جناز و قوی ہے لہذ اور صحیح ہونی چاہئے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر چہ فرضیت کے اعتبار سے نماز جنازہ قوی ہے لیکن رکوع وجود کے اعتبار سے یہ ناقص ہے اور نقل نماز کامل، الہذا قوت نقل ہی کو حاصل ہوگی۔
ولو نوى نافلة وصلاة جنازة فهى نافلة كذا فى الظهيرية (البحر الرائق ج ١ ، ص : ٣٨١)
If one intends nafl and janaza prayer: if someone intends both janaza and nafl prayer together, the nafl prayer will be valid, not the janaza. Here, there is a difficulty: apparently janaza prayer is stronger, so it should be valid. The answer is that although janaza is stronger in terms of obligation (fardiyya), it is deficient in terms of ruku' and sujud, while nafl prayer is complete. Therefore, the strength of nafl is realized. And whoever intends nafl and janaza prayer, it is nafl, as in al-Dhahiriyya (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1:381).
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage addresses an interesting case: when someone intends both a nafl prayer (with ruku' and sujud) and a janaza prayer (which has no ruku' or sujud) simultaneously. The author anticipates a question: since janaza is fard kifaya, it is stronger in obligation, so why does the nafl prevail? The answer is that 'strength' here is measured not only by the nature of obligation but also by the completeness of the act. Janaza prayer lacks ruku' and sujud, making it deficient in structure, whereas the nafl is a complete prayer. Hence, the nafl's structural completeness makes it stronger in this context, so the intention of nafl prevails and janaza is not fulfilled. This shows that the principle of 'stronger prevails' considers multiple dimensions of strength.

Key Terms
ركوع (ruku'): Bowing in prayer; janaza lacks ruku'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When someone intends both a nafl prayer and a janaza prayer, which one is valid?
A) Janaza
B) Nafl
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
When two prayer intentions conflict, the one that is stronger in both legal status and structural completeness prevails.

Combining Two Nafl Intentions: The Qawida of Tadakhul
Ruling on combining two nafl intentions (Fajr sunna & tahiyya) and analogy to fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida of tadakhul among nafl acts to determine when one act fulfills multiple intentions and identify when the stronger act prevails.

Core Idea
Nafl intentions can combine: one act fulfills multiple if equal; the stronger prevails if unequal.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi qawida from Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair regarding overlapping nafl acts. The passage confirms that offering the Fajr sunna suffices for both the sunna and tahiyyat al-masjid because both are nafl and tahiyya is subsidiary. The author then extends the principle to fasting. We will unpack the qawida, its conditions, exceptions, and practical applications for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida
Recognize that the core principle is 'النوافل تتداخل وتحصل بواحدة نية النوافل' (Nafl acts interfere and one act suffices for multiple nafl intentions). This is a sughra (minor) qawida, specifically a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim).
2
Condition: equal rank
Understand that tadakhul applies only when the two acts are of equal strength (both nafl). The dabt states: if intentions are of equal strength, interference is allowed; if one is stronger, the stronger prevails.
3
Apply to the first furu'
Analyze the case of intending both Fajr sunna and tahiyyat al-masjid. Since both are nafl and tahiyya is subsidiary, the one prayer suffices for both.
This is the direct ruling from the passage.
4
Apply to the second furu' (tarawih vs tahajjud)
Consider the case where a person intends both tarawih and tahajjud. Tarawih is stronger (sunna mu'akkada vs nafl), so tarawih prevails; only tarawih is fulfilled.
This illustrates the exception: unequal strength.
5
Handle the istithna'
When the two acts have different causes and are of unequal strength, the stronger excludes the weaker. The governing qawida becomes 'الأقوى يغلب الأضعف' (The stronger overcomes the weaker).
This limits the scope of tadakhul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا إِذَانَوَى نَافِلَتَيْنِ، كَمَا إذَانَوى بِرَكْعَتَى الْفَجْرِ التَّحِيَّةَ وَالسُّنَّةَ أَجْزَاتُ عَنْهُمَا، وَلَمْ أَرَحُكْمَ مَا إِذَا نَوى سُنَتَيْنِ كَمَا إِذَا نَوَى فِى يَوْمِ الإِثْنَيْنِ صَوْمَهُ عَنْهُ، وَعَنْ يَوْمٍ عَرْ فَةً إذَا وَافَقَهُ، فَإِنْ مَسْأَلَةَ التَّحِيَّةِ إِنَّمَا كَانَتْ ضِمْناً لِلسُّنَّةِ لِحُصُول الْمَقْصُودِ.
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال جب دو فلوں کی نیت کرے جیسے کوئی فجر کی دورکعتوں یعنی سنتوں میں سنت اور تحیتہ کی نیت کرے تو وہ ان دونوں کی طرف سے کافی ہے اور میں نے اس صورت کا حکم نہیں دیکھا جب کوئی دوسنتوں کی نیت کرے جیسے کوئی پیر کے دن اس کی طرف سے اور یوم عرفہ کی طرف سے روزہ کی نیت کرے جب وہ اس کے موافق ہو جائے ( یوم عرفہ یہ کے دن ہو ) چنانچہ تحیتہ کا مسئلہ سنت کے ضمن میں مقصد کے حاصل ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے ایک ساتھ سے دونوافل کی نیت کی تو اس کی یہ نیت درست ہوگی کیونکہ نوافل میں مداخل ہو سکتا ہے مثلا فجر کی سنت دور کعتوں سے سنت اور تحیۃ المسجد دونوں کی نیت کی تو اس کی یہ نیت درست ہوگی۔ قال في الحلية لو اشتغل داخل المسجد بالفريضة غير ناو للتحية قامت تلك الفريضة مقام تحية المسجد الحصول تعظيم المسجد (شامی ج ۲ : ۱۸) اور اگر دو فل نماز میں ایسی ہوں جن کے اسباب ہی الگ ہوں تو جوان میں قوسی ہوگا وہی راجح ہوگا مثلا نماز تراویح اور تہجد دونوں کی ایک ساتھ نیت کی تو نماز تراویح اتوئی ہے لہذا نماز تراویح ادا ہو گی ۔
ولم أر حكم ما اذا نوى کسی نے پیر کے دن روزہ رکھا اتفاق سے اس دن عرفہ کا قول ہی تھا نا ہو دونوں کے سنت کی نیت کر لی تو اگر چہ اس سلسلہ میں علامہ ابن قیم کو کوئی علم نہیں ملا ہے بیان قواعد کی روتے تو اس کی النوافل ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی نیت صحیح ہو جائے گی اور دونوں کی طرف سے بہت کافی ہو جائے گی۔ فان مسألة التحية اس عبات کا تعلق اجزات عنہا سے ہے ولم ارحکم مانے ممالک کے ہر کاروان کیا ہے یہ فان مسألة التحية والی علت اس پر بھی منطبق ہو سکتی تھی اس لئے اس علمت کو دونوں مستاوں کے پیدا کر فرما کر بتا دیا کہ اگرچہ یہ جزئیہ میں نے صراحی نہیں دیکھا لیکن اشتراک علت کی وجہ سے دونوں جڑ کیوں کافر ایک ہو سکتا ہے۔
As for when one intends two nafls, such as intending with the two rak'ahs of Fajr both the tahiyya and the sunna, it suffices for both. But I have not seen a ruling for when one intends two sunnahs, like fasting on Monday and on the day of Arafah when they coincide. For the tahiyya issue, it is subsumed under the sunna because the purpose is attained. Commentary: If someone intends two nafls together, his intention is valid because interference (madakhala) among nafls is possible. For example, intending both the Fajr sunna and tahiyvat al-masjid with the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunna, it is valid. In al-Hilya: if one engaged in fard in the mosque without intending tahiyya, that fard takes the place of tahiyya because it attains the purpose of honoring the mosque (Shami 2:18). And if there are two nafl prayers with separate causes, then whichever is stronger prevails. For example, if one intends both tarawih and tahajjud together, tarawih is stronger because it is more confirmed. As for the fasting case: if someone fasts on Monday and it coincides with Arafah, and he intends both , although Ibn Qayyim (?) did not come across a ruling, according to the rules, since both are nafl, the intention is valid and suffices for both. For the tahiyya issue, it is related to sufficiency (ijza'), and I have not seen a ruling for when one intends two sunnahs, but the cause of the tahiyya can be applied analogically, so the principle may cover both.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage discusses combining two nafl intentions. The author first confirms that when intending both the Fajr sunna and tahiyyat al-masjid simultaneously, one prayer suffices for both because tahiyya is subsumed under the sunna (both are nafl and the purpose is attained). He then notes that he did not find a specific ruling for combining two sunnahs, such as fasting on Monday and Arafah when they coincide. The commentary extends that since both are nafl, the intention can be combined. The principle is that among nafls, interference (madakhala) is possible, so one act can fulfill multiple nafl intentions if there is no conflict. However, if the two nafls have different causes and unequal strength, the stronger one prevails (e.g., tarawih over tahajjud). This shows the nuanced application of the qawida: when both intentions are of equal rank (both nafl), they can be combined; when one is stronger, it prevails.

Key Terms
مداخل (madakhala): Interference or overlap where one act suffices for multiple intentions
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): Greeting the mosque – a recommended two-rak'ah prayer upon entering the mosque
نافلة (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory act of worship
سنة (sunnah): The confirmed sunna, often used interchangeably with nafl in this context

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone intends both the Fajr sunna prayer and tahiyyat al-masjid with the same two rak'ahs?
A) Only the sunna is valid
B) Only tahiyya is valid
C) Both are fulfilled
D) Neither is valid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, nafl acts can be combined through tadakhul: one act fulfills multiple equal-strength intentions, but when one act is stronger, it prevails over the weaker.

Multiple Intentions in Hajj: The Qawida and Its Furuat
Ruling on multiple Hajj intentions including nadhr and nafl, and two Hajjs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida regarding multiple Hajj intentions to different scenarios (nadhr+nafl, fard+tatawwu', two Hajjs) and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When two Hajj intentions collide, the voluntary overrides the obligatory; if equal, both bind.

This passage from Fath al-Qadir addresses a practical problem: what happens when a person makes multiple intentions for Hajj? The Hanafi school analyzes this through a qawida that weighs the strength of intentions. We will explore the furuat (sub-cases) and the intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the intention combinations
The passage lists three combinations: nadhr+nafl, fard+tatawwu', and two Hajjs (simultaneous or consecutive). Recognize each as a distinct furu'.
Nadhr is a vowed obligation; nafl is voluntary. Fard is obligatory; tatawwu' is voluntary.
2
Apply the qawida of taghalub (overpowering)
For different-category intentions, the voluntary overrides the obligatory: nadhr+nafl becomes nafl; fard+tatawwu' becomes tatawwu'. This is the ruling of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
This shows a qawida that the weaker intention (in terms of obligation level) prevails.
3
Resolve the dispute on two Hajjs
When two similar intentions (both Hajjs) are made, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say both are binding; Muhammad says only one is binding. The text reports that the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) agree one will be dropped later but differ on timing.
The dispute is about whether multiple obligations can be imposed from a single action.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The fatwa is based on the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as it is the zahir al-riwaya. The passage cites al-Mabsut for this.
Mufti should rely on the majority view unless there is a strong counter-evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا التَّعَدُّدُ فِي الْحَجِّ فَقَالَ فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ : مِنْ بَابِ الْإِحْرَامِ لَوْ أَحْرَمَ نَأَرَاوَ المَلَا، كَانَ نَفَلا، أَوْ فَرْضاً وَتَطَوُّعًا، كَانَ تَطَوُّعاً عِنْدَ هُمَا فِي الْأَصَحَ، وَمِنْ بَابِ إِضَافَ الْإِحْرَامِ إِلَى الإِحْرَامِ: وَلَوْأَحْرَمَ بِحَجَّتَيْنِ مَعاً، أَوْ عَلَى التَّعَاقُبِ لَزِمَاهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوْسُفَ، وَعِندَ مُحَمَّدٍ : فِي الْمَعِيَّةِ يَلْزَمُهُ إحْدَاهُمَا، وَفِي التَّعَاقُبِ الْأَوْلَى فَقَط ، وَإِذَ الزمَاهُ عنه، هما إرْتَفَضَتْ إِحْدَاهُمَا بِاتِّفَاقِهِمَا، لَكِنْ إخْتَلَفَا فِي وَقْتِ الرَّفْضِ، فَعِنْدَابِى يُوْسُفَ عِندَ صَيْرُورته مُحْرِماً بَلامُهْلَةٍ، وَعِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ: إِذَاشَرَعَ فِي الْأَعْمَالِ، وَقِيْلَ إِذَا تَوَجَّهَ سَائِراً وَلَصٌ فِي الْمَبْسُوْطِ عَلَى أَنَّهُ ظَاهِرُ الرَّوَايَةِ.
ترجمہ اور ربانج میں تعدد تو فتح القدیر کے باپ احرام میں ہے کہ اگر نذر اور نفل کا احرام باند مانتوان (صاحبین ) کے نزدیک نقلی حج ہوگا اور فرض و تطوع کا باندھا تو ان کے نزدیک اصبح قول یہ ہے کہ حج قطلوع ہوگا اور اضافۃ الاحرام الی الاحرام کے باب میں ہے کہ اگر دونوں کا ایک ساتھ باندھا یا یکے بعد دیگرے تو امام ابی حنیفہ اور امام ابی یوسف کے نزدیک اس پر دونوں لازم ہوں گے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک معیت ایک ساتھ ) کی صورت میں ان میں سے ایک اور تعاقت ( یکے بعد دیگرے) کی صورت میں صرف پہلا لازم ہوگا اور جب شیخین کے نزد یکسال پر وہ دونوں لازم ہوں گے تو متفقہ طور پر دونوں کے درمیان اختلاف ہے چنانچہ امام ابی یوسف کے نزدیک اس کے محرم ہونے کے فورا بعد ہی (ایک چھوٹ جائے گا) اور امام ابی حنیفہ کے نزدیک جب وہ افعال حج شروع کر دے کہا گیا کہ جب وہ (افعال حج کے لئے ) چلنے لگے اور مبسوط میں صراحت ہے کہ ظاہر الروایہ یہی ہے۔
As for multiplicity in Hajj, it is said in Fath al-Qadir: from the chapter of ihram: if he makes ihram with a nadhr and a nafl, it is nafl according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in the most correct view; if with fard and tatawwu', it is tatawwu' according to them in the most correct view. From the chapter of adding ihram to ihram: if he makes ihram for two Hajjs together or consecutively, it is binding upon him according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad: when together, one of them is binding; when consecutive, only the first is binding. And when the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) make both binding, they agree that one of them will be dropped, but they differed over the time of dropping: according to Abu Yusuf, immediately upon becoming muhrim; according to Abu Hanifa, when he begins the actions (of Hajj), and it is said when he sets out traveling. And it is explicitly stated in al-Mabsut that this is the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya).
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage deals with multiple intentions in Hajj. It distinguishes two cases: (1) Combining a nadhr (vowed) Hajj with a nafl Hajj: the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that it counts as nafl because nafl is stronger (or more common) in such combination? Actually, the text says it becomes nafl. (2) Combining a fard Hajj with a voluntary Hajj: it becomes voluntary (tatawwu') according to them in the most correct view. This is similar to the earlier rule that the stronger (fard) is annulled? Actually here the voluntary seems to prevail? That needs careful reading: perhaps the intended distinction is that if one combines a specific obligation (like nadhr) with nafl, the nafl prevails because nadhr is not inherently stronger? The text is ambiguous. Then, when one intends two Hajjs (e.g., two obligatory Hajjs or two voluntary), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say both are binding (the person must perform both), while Muhammad says only one is binding (the first if consecutive, or one if simultaneous). If both are binding according to the first two, they agree that one will eventually be dropped, but differ on when: Abu Yusuf says immediately upon becoming muhrim, Abu Hanifa says after beginning the rites. The correct ruling (zahir al-riwaya) is as in al-Mabsut.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship
احرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah
تغليب (taghalub): Overpowering: the principle that when two intentions conflict, the stronger (in terms of obligation level) gives way to the weaker? Actually, here the voluntary overpowers the obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when a person makes ihram for two Hajjs simultaneously according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?
A) Both are binding
B) Only one is binding
C) Neither is valid
D) It depends on the intention

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, multiple Hajj intentions are legally effective: voluntary overrides obligatory when mixed, and two similar Hajjs bind the person to perform both.

Combining Intentions in Overlapping Supererogatory Acts
Deriving a ruling via shared 'illa for overlapping nafl intentions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of combining intentions in overlapping supererogatory acts and derive rulings for new cases using the shared 'illa method.

Core Idea
One intention suffices for multiple supererogatory acts when they share a common cause or one is stronger.

Sometimes a worshipper intends two supererogatory acts that coincide, such as Tarawih and Tahajjud prayers on a Ramadan night, or fasting on Monday that also falls on Arafah. Does one intention cover both, or must each be intended separately? This lesson explores the Hanafi rule that for supererogatory acts, a single intention can validly cover multiple acts, based on the principle of considering the stronger and shared effective cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida
Extract the underlying maxim from the passage: when two supererogatory acts overlap, one intention suffices for both if they share a common 'illa or if one is stronger (aqwa). The commentator derives this by analogy from the Tahiyyah prayer example.
The text uses the term 'اشتراك علت' (shared cause) to justify the ruling.
2
Apply to the first furu' (Tarawih+Tahajjud)
If someone intends both Tarawih and Tahajjud prayers simultaneously, the Tarawih prayer is valid. The text states 'نماز تراویح ادا ہو گی' (the Tarawih prayer is performed). This indicates that the stronger intention (Tarawih as the specific sunnah of Ramadan) governs.
Tarawih is considered stronger because it is a sunnah mu'akkadah specific to Ramadan.
3
Apply to the second furu' (Monday fast + Arafah fast)
If someone fasts on Monday intending both the Monday sunnah and the Arafah sunnah, the intention is valid and suffices for both, because both are nafl. The principle of 'اعتبار الأقوى' (considering the stronger) is not needed here as they are equal; rather, the shared nafl nature makes one intention sufficient.
The commentator mentions Ibn Qayyim did not find an explicit ruling, but derives it via qiyas from the Tahiyyah prayer case.
4
Note the scope and istithna'
This rule applies to supererogatory (nafl) acts only. For obligatory (fard/wajib) acts, each act requires its own specific intention, unless the acts are the same type and one is a repetition (e.g., repeating a fard prayer with the same intention). The text does not mention this explicitly, but it is a standard Hanafi restriction.
The maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' requires specific intentions for distinct obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور تہجد دونوں کی ایک ساتھ نیت کی تو نماز تراویح اتوئی ہے لہذا نماز تراویح ادا ہو گی ۔ ولم أر حكم ما اذا نوی کسی نے پیر کے دن روزہ رکھا اتفاق سے اس دن عرفہ کا قول ہی تھا نا ہو دونوں کے سنت کی نیت کر لی تو اگر چہ اس سلسلہ میں علامہ ابن قیم کو کوئی علم نہیں ملا ہے بیان قواعد کی روتے تو اس کی النوافل ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی نیت صحیح ہو جائے گی اور دونوں کی طرف سے بہت کافی ہو جائے گی۔ فان مسألة التحية اس عبات کا تعلق اجزات عنہا سے ہے ولم أر حكم مانے ممالک کے ہر کاروان کیا ہے یہ فان مسألة التحية والی علت اس پر بھی منطبق ہو سکتی تھی اس لئے اس علمت کو دونوں مستاوں کے پیدا کر فرما کر بتا دیا کہ اگرچہ یہ جزئیہ میں نے صراحی نہیں دیکھا لیکن اشتراک علت کی وجہ سے دونوں جڑ کیوں کافر ایک ہو سکتا ہے۔
And if one intended both Tarawih and Tahajjud together, then the Tarawih prayer is performed [correctly], so the Tarawih prayer is valid. And I have not seen the ruling when one intended: someone fasted on Monday, coincidentally that day happened to be the day of Arafah, so he intended both supererogatory fasts. Even though Ibn Qayyim did not find any knowledge in this regard, according to the expression of the principles, because they are supererogatory, his intention is valid and it will suffice for both. So the issue of Tahiyyah [prayer] is that this act's relation is to fulfillment from it, and I have not seen the ruling... every caravan of the kingdoms? The issue of Tahiyyah and its cause can also apply to this, so he derived this ruling by combining both equal [aspects?] to inform that although I have not explicitly seen this particular case, due to the shared cause both roots can be one [ruling].
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi rule that when two supererogatory acts of worship coincide, the intention for one can cover both if they share the same cause or are of equal strength. The commentator gives two examples: (1) Intending both Tarawih and Tahajjud prayers simultaneously—the Tarawih is valid because it is the stronger (aqwa) or the one intended. (2) Fasting on Monday that happens to be Arafah—if one intends both the Monday sunnah and the Arafah sunnah, it is valid and suffices for both, as both are nafl. The commentator refers to Ibn Qayyim's lack of explicit knowledge but derives the ruling via shared 'illa (cause). This illustrates the Hanafi principle of 'اعتبار الأقوى' (considering the stronger) in overlapping intentions.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship.
علة (illa): Effective cause or reason that links a ruling to its case.
أقوى (aqwa): Stronger, referring to the act that has a higher legal weight or specific time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone intends both Tarawih and Tahajjud prayers together, what is the ruling according to the text?
A) Neither is valid.
B) Only Tarawih is valid.
C) Both are valid.
D) Only Tahajjud is valid.

Key Takeaway
For supererogatory acts, a single intention can cover multiple coinciding acts if they share a common cause or if one is stronger, based on the Hanafi principle of considering the stronger and shared 'illa.

Combining Two Ihrams: Hanafi Ikhtilaf and Ruling
Parsing the Hanafi ikhtilaf on multiple ihrams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the binding of multiple ihrams, identify the timing of rafd (abandonment) according to each, and apply the resulting dam obligations in case of violations.

Core Idea
Two binding ihrams automatically abandon one—when? Abu Yusuf: immediate; Abu Hanifa: later; the difference changes dam counts.

This passage from Fath al-Qadir and subsequent Hanafi commentaries deals with a specific scenario: a person enters ihram for two Hajj or Umrah intentions simultaneously or consecutively. The Hanafi imams differ on whether both become binding, and if so, when one is automatically abandoned (rafd). Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for a mufti to correctly assess dam obligations and qada requirements for the invalidated Hajj. We will parse the positions and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The passage covers: (a) nadhr and nafl ihrams, (b) fard and nafl ihrams, (c) two Hajjs (both fard or both nafl), and (d) two Umrahs. Note that (a) and (b) involve different categories where one may dominate; (c) and (d) are the core ikhtilaf on identical categories.
The ruling for (a) and (b) is that the weaker (nafl) gives way to the stronger (nadhr/fard) according to the qawida 'al-mu'tabar al-aqwa fa al-aqwa', but the matn in Fath al-Qadir states the opposite.
2
State each imam's ruling on binding
For two Hajjs (both fard or both nafl): Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold both are binding (lazim). Muhammad holds only one is binding: if together, either; if consecutive, only the first. The same applies to two Umrahs.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (ikhtilaf al-madhhab).
3
Explain rafd timing
When both are binding (by the view of the two shaykhs), one is automatically abandoned (rafd) because two cannot be performed simultaneously. The timing differs: Abu Yusuf says immediately upon becoming muhrim without delay; Abu Hanifa has two narrations: (1) when he begins the actions of Hajj, (2) when he sets out traveling. Al-Mabsut states the latter as Zahir al-Riwaya.
Rafd is a technical term—the abandonment is automatic, not requiring intention.
4
Derive the thamarah (practical consequences)
If a violation (jinaya) occurs before the rafd time (e.g., hunting or intercourse before starting actions), the number of dam differs: Under Abu Hanifa (rafd later), two dams for two ihrams; under Abu Yusuf (rafd immediate), one dam for one ihram. Also, the abandoned Hajj requires qada (one Hajj and one Umrah) and a dam.
The thamarah is the key difference in issuing fatwa.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The passage states that al-Mabsut declares the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (both binding) as Zahir al-Riwaya, and the rafd timing according to Abu Hanifa (when setting out) is the relied-upon position.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

نزدیک اصبح قول کے اعتبار سے ج نقل شارہ ہوگا او نوى فرضاً و تطوعاً كان تطوعاً عنده و كذا عند ابي يوسف في الاصح لیکن علامہ موئی کے نزدیک یہاں بھی اقوئی ہونے کی وجہ سے حج فرض ادا ہونا چاہیے ۔ كان ينبغي ان يكون نذراً و فرضاً لانهما اقوى و قد تقدم ان المعتبر الاقوى فالاقوى (حاشيه الحموی ، ص: ۷۹) ولو احرم بحجتين: اولا یہ گھنا چاہئے کہ حج یا عمرہ کے دو احراموں کو جمع کرنا بدعت ہے اور اکبر الکبائر ہونے کی وجہ سے حرام ہے اور مکی کے حق میں جنایت بھی ہے خواہ وہ مکی حقیقتہ ہو یا حکما اور آفاقی کے حق میں مکروہ ہے اور خلاف شرع ہے۔ لیکن اگر کسی نے حج کے احرام پر حج کا احرام باندھ لیا اور دونوں حج ایک ہی درجہ کے ہوں یعنی دونوں فرض ہیں یا نفل ہیں تو اس صورت میں فقہاء کا اختلاف ہے اگر دونوں کا احرام ایک ساتھ باندھا ہے یا یکے بعد دیگرے تو امام محمد کے نزدیک اگر ایک ساتھ باندھا ہے تو دونوں میں سے ایک ہی جج لازم ہوگا کسی ایک کی ادائیگی کافی ہے اور یکے بعد دیگرے باندھا تو جس کا احرام باندھا وہ لازم ہوگا ۔ اور چیخین کے نزدیک اس پر دونوں لازم ہو جائیں گے اور ان دونوں میں سے ایک تو ابھی ادا کرے گا اور ایک کی قضا آئندہ سال کرے گا ، اور اس پر لازم ہوگا کہ آئندہ اس حج کے بدلہ ایک حج اور ایک عمرہ کرے تو امسال ایک حج کرے گا اور ایک چھوٹ جائے گا لیکن ایک جو چھوٹے گاوہ کس وقت چھوٹے گا اس سلسلہ میں شیخین میں اختلاف ہے امام یوسف کے نزدیک اس کے محرم ہونے کے بعد مہلت دیئے بغیر ہی رفض احرام ہو جائے گا۔ امام ابی حنیفہ کے اس میں دو قول ہیں۔ (۱) جب اعمال حج شروع کر دے (۲) جب کسی ایک کی طرف متوجہ ہو جائے گا تو اس وقت دوسرے کو چھوڑنے والا شمار ہوگا ۔ مبسوط میں اسی کو ظاہر الروایہ کہا ہے۔ قال ابو حنيفة اذا توجه إلى احداها يصير رافضاً للأخرى ....... و فى الخانية قبل ان يشتغل بعمل احداهما قال ابويوسف كما فرغ من الاحرامين يصير رافضاً لاحداهما (تارتار خانیه ج ۲، ص: ۵۴۱) وَتَمْرَةُ الْخِلَافِ فِيْمَا إِذَا جَنِّى قَبْلَ الشُّرُوْعِ، فَعَلَيْهِ دَمَانِ لِلْجَنَايَةِ عَلَىٰ إِحْرَامَيْنِ، وَدَمٌ وَاحِدٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ، وَلَوْ جَامَعَ قَبْلَ الشُّرُوْعَ ، فَعَلَيْهِ دَمَانَ لِلْجَمَاعِ، وَدَمٌ ثَالِتْ لِلرَّفْضِ، فَإِنَّهُ يَرْفَضُ أحَدَهُمَا، وَيَمْضِي فِى الْآخَرِ، وَيَقْضِى الَّتِي مَضَىٰ فِيْهَا، وَحَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَةً مَكَانَ الَّتِي رَفَضَهَا، وَلَوْقَتَلَ صَيْداً، فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتَانِ، أَوْ احْصِرَ فَدَمَانِ، وَعَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ إِذَا أَهَلَّ بِعُمْرَ تَيْنِ مَعًا أَوْ عَلَى التَّعَاقُبِ بِلافَضلِ، انتهى.
As for multiplicity in Hajj, it is stated in Fath al-Qadir: from the chapter of ihram: if one enters ihram for a vow and a supererogatory [Hajj], it becomes supererogatory; or for an obligatory and a voluntary, it becomes voluntary according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] in the most correct view. And from the chapter of adding ihram to ihram: if one enters ihram for two Hajjs together or consecutively, both are binding upon him according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; according to Muhammad, if together, only one is binding; if consecutively, only the first. And when both are binding upon him by their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) view, then one of them is abandoned by their agreement, but they differed as to the time of abandonment. According to Abu Yusuf, at the moment he becomes muhrim without delay; according to Abu Hanifa, when he begins the actions, and it is said when he sets out traveling, and in al-Mabsut it is stated that this is the Zahir al-Riwaya. Translation (Urdu)... Explanation: If a person enters ihram for a vowed Hajj and a supererogatory Hajj together, then according to the text of Fath al-Qadir, it becomes supererogatory Hajj, not the vowed one, while al-Hamawi says it should be the vowed Hajj because it is stronger... And if one enters ihram for two Hajjs, first it must be known that combining two ihrams of Hajj or Umrah is a bid'ah and haram being among the major sins, and for a Makkan it is also a jinaya, whether he is actually Makkan or hukman, and for an Afaqi it is makruh and against Shari'ah. But if someone performs two ihrams both of the same category (both fard or both nafl), then there is ikhtilaf among fuqaha... And the fruit of the dispute concerning one who commits a violation before starting: for him two dams for violation of two ihrams, and one dam according to Abu Yusuf; and if he had intercourse before starting, then two dams for intercourse and a third dam for abandonment... and upon this difference if he does talbiyah for two Umrahs together or consecutively without distinction. End.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a detailed presentation of the Hanafi ikhtilaf on combining multiple Hajj or Umrah intentions in one or more ihrams. The author first quotes Fath al-Qadir on the scenario where one intends a nadhr (vow) and a nafl Hajj: the weaker (nafl) gives way to the stronger (nadhr) according to some, but the relied-upon view in the matn is that it becomes nafl. Then it discusses adding an ihram to another ihram: if one performs two Hajjs together or consecutively, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that both are binding (lazim), while Muhammad says only one is binding (if together, either; if consecutive, only the first). When both are binding, one of them is automatically abandoned (rafd), but the time of rafd differs: Abu Yusuf says immediately upon becoming muhrim; Abu Hanifa says when starting the actions or when setting out. The author also mentions al-Hamawi's criticism that the stronger should prevail. The discussion then extends to violations (jinayat) such as hunting or intercourse before starting, and the number of dam (blood sacrifice) required: under Abu Hanifa, two dams for two ihrams; under Abu Yusuf, one dam. The passage ends by noting that the same ikhtilaf applies to combining two Umrahs. This is a classic example of how Hanafi jurists apply the qawida 'al-mu'tabar al-aqwa fa al-aqwa' with ikhtilaf in detail.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, initiated by niyyah and talbiyah.
رفض (rafd): The automatic abandonment of one of two binding ihrams, occurring at a specific time according to each imam.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required as expiation for violations (jinayat) during ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when does one of the two binding ihrams become abandoned (rafd)?
A) Immediately upon entering ihram.
B) When he begins the actions of Hajj.
C) When he sets out traveling.
D) Both B and C are transmitted.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when two ihrams are binding, one is automatically abandoned (rafd) at a time determined by the imam's view, affecting the number of expiation sacrifices.

Combining Intentions in Non-Worship: 'Anti Alayya Haram'
Application of combining intentions in family law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to determine the ruling when a husband says 'anti alayya haram' intending both divorce and zihar.

Core Idea
A single utterance can produce multiple legal effects if the speaker intends them, per 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.

This passage illustrates a vital application of the major legal maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'. It shows that even in non-ibadat contexts, intention can give multiple legal effects to a single utterance. The specific case of 'anti alayya haram' with intentions of both divorce (talaq) and zihar demonstrates how Hanafi fiqh prioritises intention in family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing maxim
Recognize that the ruling is based on the major maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions). This maxim applies across all fiqh chapters.
2
Recall the Hanafi principle on intentions in non-worship
In Hanafi fiqh, intention is considered even in non-worship acts (muamalat) unless specific evidence excludes it. This contrasts with worship, where restrictions on combining intentions sometimes apply.
See the example of combining hajj/umrah in the passage.
3
Apply the maxim to the statement 'anti alayya haram'
When a man says 'anti alayya haram' (you are haram for me), the words are general (kinayah). His intention determines the legal effects: if he intends divorce, it is divorce; if he intends zihar, it is zihar; if he intends both, both may take effect simultaneously.
This is supported by the cited text from al-Muhit.
4
Note the specific furu' case from the passage
The passage explicitly states: if he says it to his wife intending both divorce and zihar, both are applicable. Similarly, if he says it to two wives with different intentions, each intention may affect its target.
This demonstrates the breadth of the maxim.
5
Differentiate from default ruling without intention
Without a specific intention, 'anti alayya haram' is considered a kinayah for zihar by default. With explicit intention for both, the default is overridden and multiple effects are valid.
A mufti must investigate the husband's intention at the time of utterance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اما اذا جمع بين الحجتين او العمرتين ففى المعية والتعاقب لا يتصور عدم الرفض وفي التراخي لا يلزمه الرفض بل يتعين الجمع. (قنية جديدص : ۳۳۸) فائدة : يتفرع على الجمع بين الشيئين في النية، وإن لم يكن من العبادات ما لو قال لزوجته : أنت على حرام ، ناوياً الطلاق والظهار، أو قال لزوجتيه: أنتما علي حرام ناوياً في إحداهما الطلاق، وفي الأخرى الظهار، وقد كتبنا ه في باب الإبلاء من شرح الكنز نقلاً عن المحيط
And as for when one combines between two hajjs or two umrahs, then in the case of simultaneity and succession, absence of refusal is inconceivable, and in the case of delay, refusal is not necessary; rather combination is determined. (Qunyah Jadidah, p. 338) Benefit: It branches from the combining of two things in intention, even if not from acts of worship, such as if one says to his wife: 'You are haram upon me,' intending divorce and zihar, or says to his two wives: 'You both are haram upon me,' intending divorce in one and zihar in the other. We have written this in the chapter of Ila' from Sharh al-Kanz, quoting from al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage provides a benefit (fa'idah) applying the principle of combining intentions to non-worship contexts. It first gives a subsidiary ruling: when someone combines two hajjs or two umrahs in a single ihram, if they are simultaneous or successive, refusal of one is necessary; but if there is a delay (tarakhi), refusal is not necessary and the person must complete both. Then it moves to a separate application: the statement 'anti alayya haram' can combine multiple intentions. If a man says this to his wife intending both divorce and zihar, or to two wives intending different things, the ruling depends on the combination of intentions. This is a classic illustration of the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' and shows that Hanafi fiqh considers the intention even in non-ibadat contexts.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A pre-Islamic divorce-like statement comparing wife to mother; in Hanafi fiqh, it is a specific form of divorce requiring expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a man says to his wife 'anti alayya haram' intending both divorce and zihar?
A) Only divorce applies
B) Only zihar applies
C) Both may apply based on his intention
D) The statement is invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a single utterance can produce multiple legal effects if the speaker intends them, as per the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.

Thamarah al-Khilaf: Applying the Principle to Combined Ihrams
This passage applies the principle of thamarah al-khilaf to the specific case of combining two ihrams and committing violations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the practical difference (thamarah) between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf in cases of combining two ihrams, and evaluate which opinion is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on combined ihrams results in double or single penalties for violations.

This passage from the Ashbah wa al-Nazair illustrates the principle of thamarah al-khilaf — the practical consequence of a legal disagreement. It applies a fundamental ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the validity of combining two ihrams to specific scenarios of violations (jinayat). By examining these applications, you will learn how theoretical differences impact actual rulings in Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ikhtilaf
Determine the root disagreement: Does combining two ihrams (e.g., for two Hajjs or Umrahs) result in both being valid, or does the second reject the first?
This is the foundational usul difference that drives all derived rulings.
2
State Each Imam's Position
Abu Hanifa holds both ihrams valid and independent; therefore violations incur separate expiations for each. Abu Yusuf holds that the second ihram rejects the first, so only one remains and violations incur a single set of expiations.
The position of each imam is based on their view of the possibility of performing two Hajjs or Umrahs simultaneously.
3
Apply to Specific Violations
Work through the three scenarios in the text: janabah, intercourse, and hunting. For each, calculate the number of dam/hady required according to each imam.
For janabah: Abu Hanifa = 2 dam, Abu Yusuf = 1 dam. For intercourse: Abu Hanifa = 3 dam (2 for intercourse + 1 for abandonment), Abu Yusuf = 2 dam (1+1). For hunting: Abu Hanifa = 2 hady, Abu Yusuf = 1 hady.
4
Note the Thamarah for Each Scenario
Observe how the core ikhtilaf manifests in concrete numbers of expiations. This is the thamarah — the practical consequence of the legal disagreement.
The difference is consistent across all scenarios: double or single penalties.
5
Consider the Mufta Bihi
Evaluate which position is relied upon in later Hanafi fatwa works (e.g., Fatawa Hindiyya). The position of Abu Yusuf is often preferred for practicality, as it avoids unnecessary doubling of penalties.
Tarjih is based on the soundness of the dalil and ease of practice (taysir).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: اور اختلاف کا ثمرہ اس صورت میں ظاہر ہوگا جب شروع کرنے سے پہلے جنابت کرے تو اس پر دوا حراموں پر جنایت کی وجہ سے دودم لازم ہوں کے اور امام ابی یوسف کے نزدیک ایک دم لازم ہوگا۔ اور اگر شروع کرنے سے پہلے جماع کیا تو جماع کی وجہ سے اس پر دودم لازم ہوں گے اور تیسر ادم چھوڑ دینے کی وجہ سے کیونکہ ان میں سے ایک کو چھوڑے گا اور دوسرے کو کرے گا اور جسے جاری رکھے گا اس کو پورا کرے گا اور ایک حج اور ایک عمر د اس کی جگہ کرے جس کو چھوڑا ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے کوئی شکار کیا تواس پر و قیمتیں لازم ہوں گی یا اسے اصرار کیا گیا تو وہ ہوں گے اور وہ صورت بھی اسی اختلاف پر محمول ہے جب دو عمروں کا ایک ساتھ یا آگے پیچھے احرام باند ھے حج والی صورت اور عمرہ والی صورت کی تفصیل میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے فتح القدیر کا کام مکمل ہوا۔ تشریح : اختلاف کا ثمرہ چیخین کے مابین اس وقت ظاہر ہو گا اگر ایسا کوئی محرم احترام مکمل کرنے کے بعد افعال حج کی طرف چلنے یا افعال حج شروع کرنے سے پہلے کوئی جنایت کر دے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دو احراموں پر جنایت کی وجہ سے دو دم لازم ہوں گے اور امام یوسف کے نزدیک ایک دم لازم ہوگا۔ اور اگر افعال حج شروع کرنے سے پہلے جماع کر لیا تو امام ابی حنیفہ کے نزدیک دورم جماع کی وجہ سے واجب ہوں گے اور تیسر ادم حج کو چھوڑ دینے کی وجہ سے، جبکہ امام یوسف کے نزدیک ایک دم جماع کی وجہ سے اور دوسرا حج کو چھوڑ دینے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوگا اور جس حج میں اس نے یہ عمل کیا ہے اس کی قضا کرے گا اور جسے چھوڑا ہے اس کی جگہ ایک حج اور عمرہ کی قضا کرے گا۔ اگر افعال شروع کرنے سے پہلے شکار کر لیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک حلال ہونے کے لئے اسے دو ہدی کی ضرورت ہے اور امام ابی یوسف کے نزدیک ایک ہی ہدی اسے کافی ہوگی۔ و على هذا الخلاف اگر کسی شخص نے ایک ساتھ یا پے در پے دو عمروں کا احرام باندھ لیا تو تعدد احرام حج کی شکل میں جو تفصیل گذری ہے بلا کسی فرق کے وہی ساری تفصیل اس صورت میں بھی ہوگی۔ و اما اذا جمع بين الحجتين او العمرتين ففى المعية والتعاقب لا يتصور عدم الرفض وفي التراخي لا يلزمه الرفض بل يتعين الجمع. (قنية جديدص : ۳۳۸)
Translation: The fruit of the difference will appear in this case: if he commits janabah before starting (the actions), then upon him, due to the violation (jinaya) on two ihrams, two dam become obligatory according to Abu Hanifa, and according to Imam Abu Yusuf one dam becomes obligatory. And if he had intercourse before starting, then due to intercourse two dam are obligatory upon him, and a third dam due to abandoning (the Hajj), because he will leave one and do the other; whatever he continues, he will complete it, and he will perform one Hajj and one Umrah in place of what he left. And if he hunted something, then upon him are the values (fidyah) or if he was urged, then they will be. And that case is also based on this difference when he assumes ihram for two Umrahs together or consecutively; there is no difference in detail between the Hajj case and the Umrah case. (Fath al-Qadir is completed). Explanation: The fruit of the difference between the two shaykhs will appear if a muhrim, after completing the ihram and before proceeding to or starting the actions of Hajj, commits a violation. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, due to the violation on two ihrams, two dam are obligatory; according to Imam Abu Yusuf, one dam is obligatory. And if he had intercourse before starting the actions of Hajj, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa two dam are obligatory due to intercourse and a third dam due to abandoning Hajj, while according to Imam Abu Yusuf one dam is obligatory due to intercourse and a second due to abandoning Hajj. And he will make up the Hajj in which he did this act, and in place of what he left, he will perform one Hajj and one Umrah. If he hunted before starting the actions, then according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) he needs two hady for becoming halal; according to Imam Abu Yusuf, one hady suffices. And based on this difference: if a person assumes ihram for two Umrahs together or consecutively, then the same detail that passed in the form of multiple ihrams for Hajj applies here without any difference. And as for when he combines two Hajj or two Umrahs: in the cases of simultaneity and consecutiveness, non-rejection is inconceivable; in the case of delay, rejection is not obligatory upon him, rather combination is determined. (Qunya jadid, p. 338)
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the principle of thamarah al-khilaf (the practical consequence of legal disagreement). It demonstrates how the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the effect of combining two ihrams manifests in concrete rulings. The core dispute is whether a person who assumes ihram for two Hajjs or two Umrahs simultaneously or consecutively has effectively rejected one of them (and thus only one remains) or both remain valid. According to Abu Hanifa, both ihrams are valid and separate, leading to separate violations for each. According to Abu Yusuf, the second ihram rejects the first, so only one ihram remains. This difference affects the number of dam (blood penalty) required for violations such as janabah, intercourse, and hunting committed after the ihram but before starting the actions of Hajj. The passage details each scenario: for janabah, Abu Hanifa requires two dam (one for each ihram), Abu Yusuf requires one; for intercourse, Abu Hanifa requires two for the act plus one for abandoning Hajj (three total), Abu Yusuf requires one for intercourse and one for abandonment (two total). For hunting, Abu Hanifa requires two hady, Abu Yusuf one. These differences are consistent across variations of combining two Hajjs or two Umrahs, whether simultaneous or consecutive. The quote from Qunya clarifies that in cases of delay (tarakhi), rejection is not obligatory because the two acts can be performed sequentially without conflict.

Key Terms
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement between scholars
جنایت (jinaya): A violation of the rules of ihram, such as janabah, intercourse, or hunting
دم (dam): A blood penalty (slaughter of an animal) required as expiation for certain violations in ihram

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, how many dam are required if a muhrim combining two Hajjs commits janabah before starting the actions?
A) One dam
B) Two dam
C) Three dam
D) None

Key Takeaway
The thamarah al-khilaf on combined ihrams dictates whether double or single expiations apply; in practice, Abu Yusuf's view is typically followed to minimize hardship.

Transfer Between Worships and Combining Intentions in Marriage
Ruling on transfer with takbir and combining intentions in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that exiting a worship requires a physical action (takbir) alongside intention, and construct the fatwa for a husband who says a single ambiguous statement intending two different legal effects.

Core Idea
Intention alone does not exit a prayer; a physical action is required. A single ambiguous word cannot bear two contradictory legal meanings.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents two distinct but structurally related rules. The first governs the transition between acts of worship: mere intention is insufficient without a physical act (takbir). The second applies to non-worship contexts, specifically when a husband uses a single ambiguous expression (e.g., 'anti alayya haram') intending both talaq and zihar, or addressing two wives with differing intentions. The Hanafi school's treatment of these cases reveals how intention and verbal expression interact across different legal domains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for valid transfer in worship
In the first part, the text states that to exit a current prayer and enter another, one must not only intend the transfer but also utter the takbir with that intention. If the takbir is said with the intention of renewing the first prayer, no transfer occurs.
2
Understand the role of takbir as a physical action
Takbir is not merely a verbal means to enter prayer; it is the action that manifests the intention. Without it, the intention remains internal and does not break the existing ritual state. This is based on the principle that worship acts require an opening action (tahrimah).
3
Contrast the worship ruling with non-worship cases
The text then branches to a benefit (fa'idah): combining two intentions in non-worship matters. Here, intention plays a more flexible role because the acts (talaq, zihar, ila') are not rituals but legal declarations. The ambiguity of the word 'haram' allows the husband to choose which effect he meant, according to one opinion.
4
Analyze the madhhab dispute on a single expression to two wives
When the same phrase is said to two wives with different intentions (talaq for one, ila' for the other), Abu Hanifa rules that both wives are divorced because a single utterance cannot carry two distinct legal effects. The Sahibayn follow the intention, differentiating the ruling per wife.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and apply to a modern scenario
In fatwa practice, Abu Hanifa's position is preferred for caution in talaq matters. You must apply this to a contemporary case: a husband texts 'You are haram' to his two wives, intending talaq for one and ila' for the other. The mufta bihi is that both are divorced.

علی حرام کہا اور ایک بیوی میں طلاق کی اور دوسری میں ایلاء کی نیت کی تو ان دونوں کو طلاق پڑ جائے گی کیونکہ ایک لفظ کو دو معنی پر محمول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور اگر کسی ایک کومراد لے تو پھر الفاظ پرمحمول کیا جائے گا صاحبین کے نزدیک بہر حال اس کی نیت کے مطابق معاملہ ہوگا۔ واذا قال لامراتيه انتما على حرام ينوى في احداهما الطلاق و في الاخرى الايلاء كانتا طالقين جميعاً لان اللفظ الواحد لا يحمل على امرين فاذا اراد احدها حمل على الاغلظ منهما. (الجوهرة ج ۳، ص: ۵۳)
Translation: In any case, when he intends one worship, then during it he intends to transfer from it to another: if he says takbir with the intention of transferring from it to another, then he exits from the first worship. But if he intended and did not say takbir, then he does not exit from the first worship, just as if he intends to renew the first worship and says takbir. The full detail is in our commentary on al-Kanz in the chapter on nullifiers of prayer. Benefit: Branching from combining two things in intention, even if they are not worship: this issue: someone says to his wife 'you are haram upon me' intending talaq and zihar, or says to his two wives 'you both are haram upon me' intending talaq for one and zihar for the other. We have written this in the chapter on ila' from our commentary on al-Kanz, transmitted from al-Muhit. Explanation: Someone intended prayer, then during the prayer he intended to transfer to another prayer. If he said takbir with the intention of transfer, he exits the first prayer. If he did not say takbir but only intended, he does not exit, just as if he intended renewal of the first and said takbir, that takbir is not contradictory to that prayer, so he does not exit. (Quote: 'Opening with Asr or supererogatory, not Zuhr, after one rak'ah of Zuhr: i.e., his transfer from one prayer to another different from the first invalidates the first' (al-Bahr al-Raiq 2:16). Benefit: The author was discussing combining two things in intention among acts of worship. Now he branches from that to issues of combining two things in intention that are not worship. The first issue: a person says to his wife 'anti alayya haram' intending talaq and zihar. In that case, he has a choice; whichever he chooses, it becomes effective. Another opinion: talaq becomes effective due to its strength. Another: zihar becomes effective because the original is the continuity of marriage. In Fath al-Qadir: If he says to his wife 'anti alayya haram' intending talaq and zihar, then he is given a choice between them; what he chooses becomes established. It is also said talaq is established due to its strength; it is said zihar is established because the original is the continuity of marriage. (Hawashi al-Maw?, p. 80). Or if someone had two wives and said 'antuma alayya haram' intending talaq for one and ila' for the other, then both are divorced because one word cannot be applied to two meanings. If he intends one, it is applied to the harsher of them. According to the Sahibayn, in any case, the matter proceeds according to his intention. (Al-Jawhara 3:53)
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage discusses two distinct but related topics. First, it establishes the principle that mere intention (niyyah) does not suffice to exit an act of worship; a physical action consistent with the new intention is required. In prayer, the takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) is the action that, when combined with the intention to transfer to another prayer, effects the exit from the first prayer. If the takbir is said with the intention to renew the current prayer, it does not exit. This is based on the Hadith 'Actions are by intentions' but also requires a manifest action. The quote from al-Bahr al-Raiq illustrates this: opening a new prayer (e.g., Asr or supererogatory) while still in Zuhr invalidates Zuhr because the takbir for the new prayer constitutes an action that exits the previous one. Second, the passage presents a benefit (fa'idah) branching from the concept of combining two things in intention, but now applying to non-worship matters like marriage. If a husband says to his wife 'you are haram upon me' (a phrase that can signify both talaq and zihar), and he intends both, the Hanafi ruling gives him a choice to select which one he meant, because the word 'haram' is ambiguous and can be applied to multiple legal effects. There are three opinions: (1) he chooses; (2) talaq is given priority due to its strength; (3) zihar is given priority because the default is continuity of marriage. The text notes from Fath al-Qadir that the relied-upon position is that he chooses. If the husband says the same phrase to two wives, intending talaq for one and ila' (vow of abstinence) for the other, the ruling differs: according to Abu Hanifa, both wives are divorced because one utterance cannot bear two different meanings. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the intention is followed. This demonstrates how the principle of combining intentions applies differently in worship and non-worship contexts.

Key Terms
الانتقال (al-intiqal): Transferring from one worship to another while in the act of the first
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar', the opening phrase of prayer
الجمع بين الشيئين في النية (al-jam' bayna al-shay'ayn fi al-niyyah): Combining two different intentions (e.g., talaq and zihar) in a single statement

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his two wives 'antuma alayya haram' intending talaq for one and ila' for the other, what is the mufta bihi ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) Each wife receives the effect intended (talaq for one, ila' for the other)
B) Both wives are divorced
C) Both wives are subject to ila'
D) The statement is void because it is ambiguous

Key Takeaway
To exit a worship, intention alone is insufficient; a physical action (takbir) must accompany it. In marriage, a single ambiguous expression cannot produce two different legal effects for two addressees, following Abu Hanifa's cautionary position.

The Recommended Time for Intention in Purification
Explaining the recommended time for intention in purification acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'Mahall al-niyyah 'inda awwal al-fard' to determine the recommended time for intention in wudu, ghusl, and tayammum, and advise a mufti on the best practice to gain reward for sunan.

Core Idea
Intention at the first fard suffices, but earlier intention at the sunan gains reward.

This passage from al-Jawharah clarifies when a person should make their intention for purification. While the intention is valid when made at the first obligatory act, it is recommended to make it earlier, at the start of the sunan, to include those acts in the reward. As a mufti, you need to guide questioners on this subtle but rewarding difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida
State the maxim: 'Mahall al-niyyah 'inda awwal al-fard'. Note its rank (sughra) and scope (purification acts).
The qawida is a minor principle governing the recommended timing of intention.
2
Parse the dabt (constraining rule)
Identify the additional rule: 'Yanbaghi taqdimuha 'ala al-sunan linayl al-thawab' – it is recommended to precede intention before the sunan to gain reward.
This shows the Hanafi emphasis on maximizing reward through proper timing.
3
Apply to wudu
The first fard is washing the face. The recommended time for intention is at the first sunan (washing hands up to wrists). Intention at face washing is sufficient but loses sunan reward.
4
Apply to ghusl
Same as wudu: intention at the first sunan (washing hands or rinsing mouth) is recommended; intention at the first fard suffices.
Scholars agree ghusl mirrors wudu in this ruling.
5
Apply to tayammum
Tayammum has no preceding sunan. The first obligatory act is placing hands on earth. Intention must be made at that moment.
No recommendation for earlier intention since no sunan exist.
6
Formulate fatwa advice
For a questioner asking when to intend, confirm validity if made at the first fard, but advise making intention earlier (at the first sunan) to gain reward for those sunan.
Mufti should explain the fiqh hierarchy: valid vs. recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما النية في الوضوء: فقال في الجوهرة إن محلها عند غسل الوجه، وينبغي أن تكون في أول السنن عند غسل اليدين إلى الرسغين لينال ثواب السنن المتقدمة على غسل الوجه. وقالوا الغسل كالوضوء في السنن. وفي التيمم ينوي عند الوضع على الصعيد.
And as for intention in wudu: He said in al-Jawharah that its place is at the washing of the face, and it is recommended that it be at the beginning of the sunan, at the washing of the hands up to the wrists, so that one may attain the reward of the sunan preceding the washing of the face. And they said that ghusl is like wudu regarding the sunan. And in tayammum, one intends at the placing (of hands) on the earth.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rulings on the recommended time for making intention in purification acts. For wudu, the proper time for the intention is at the moment of washing the face, which is the first obligatory act of wudu. However, it is better to make the intention earlier, at the beginning of the sunan (i.e., when washing the hands up to the wrists), so that one also gains reward for those preparatory sunan. This is because the intention should ideally cover the entire act from the start. The same rule applies to ghusl: the intention is made at the beginning of the sunan (washing hands) or at the time of rinsing the mouth, as clarified by later Hanafi scholars. For tayammum, the intention is made at the moment of placing the hands on the clean earth (sa'id). This is because tayammum has no sunan preceding the obligatory act.

Key Terms
محل النية (mahall al-niyyah): The recommended time or moment when intention should be made for an act of worship.
السنن (al-sunan): The recommended acts that precede the obligatory part in wudu, such as washing hands and rinsing the mouth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the recommended (mustahabb) time for intention in wudu?
A) At the washing of the face
B) At the first sunan, i.e., washing the hands
C) At the rinsing of the mouth
D) At the beginning of the wudu, before washing hands

Key Takeaway
Intention at the first fard (washing face) is valid; making it earlier at the sunan is recommended for extra reward.

Timing of Intention for Imamate and Following
Qawida with furuat on timing of niyyah for imamate and iqtida'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida on timing of niyyah for imamate and iqtida' to determine valid scenarios for congregational prayer and issue a fatwa on the follower's intention when mistaken about the imam's start.

Core Idea
Imamate intention for reward only when followed; iqtida' intention must coincide with imam's actual start.

In Hanafi fiqh, the timing of intention (niyyah) for leading prayer (imamate) versus following (iqtida') differs. The imam's intention for reward is only effective when someone actually follows him, not before. For the follower, the intention to join the congregation must align with the imam's commencement. This lesson unpacks a key qawida from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair and a ruling from Fath al-Qadir, helping you navigate common scenarios and intra-madhhab disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contexts
Distinguish between niyyat al-imamah (for reward) and niyyat al-iqtida' (for validity). The qawida addresses the former; the passage from Fath al-Qadir addresses the latter.
Reward (thawab) vs. validity (sihhah) is a key distinction.
2
State the qawida and its furuat
Formulate the qawida: 'The intention for imamate is at the time of following, not before.' Apply it to the five furuat listed in the qawida panel, noting which scenarios are valid for reward.
The dabt emphasises that intending before followers gives no reward.
3
Analyse the follower's intention for validity
From Fath al-Qadir, three timings: (a) at the imam's opening takbir (best); (b) while standing knowing imam hasn't started (valid); (c) mistakenly thinking imam has started (disputed). Determine the mufta bihi.
The preferred view (qila la yajuz) is that the mistaken intention is invalid.
4
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute
Use the madhhab dispute map to understand the basis of the disagreement. The tarjih favours invalidity based on Fath al-Qadir.
The thamarah al-khilaf: follower should renew intention if he realises his mistake.
5
Apply to fatwa scenarios
Given a real case (e.g., follower joins late, or imam intends early), apply the qawida and the Fath al-Qadir ruling to issue a mufta bihi opinion.
Remember the adab: avoid confusing reward with validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم أر وقت نية الإمامة للثواب، وينبغي أن تكون وقت اقتداء أحد به لا قبله، كما أنه ينبغي أن يكون وقت نية الجماعة أول صلاة المأموم، وإن كان في أثناء صلاة الإمام. هذا للقواب. وأما لصحة الاقتداء بالإمام، فقال في فتح القدير والأفضل أن ينوي الاقتداء عند افتتاح الإمام، فإن نوى حين وقف عالما بأنه لم يشرع جاز، وإن نوى ذلك على ظن أنه شرع ولم يشرع، اختلف فيه، قيل: لا يجوز انتهى.
And I have not seen (a text on) the time of intention of imamate for reward, and it is recommended that it be at the time when someone follows him, not before, just as it is recommended that the time of intention for congregation (by the follower) be at the beginning of the follower's prayer, even if (the follower starts) during the imam's prayer. This pertains to the maxims. And as for the validity of following the imam, it is said in Fath al-Qadir: It is best that one intends (to follow the imam) at the moment the imam opens (the prayer). If he intends standing (waiting), knowing that the imam has not started, it is permissible. But if he intends under the impression that the imam has started while he has not, there is a difference of opinion; it is said it is not permissible. End.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage addresses the timing of intention for two contexts: imamate (leading) and iqtida' (following). For the imam, the intention to lead for reward (thawab) is recommended at the time when someone actually follows him—not before, because the reward of imamate depends on actual followers. The intention for the follower to be part of a congregation (niyyat al-jama'ah) is made at the start of his own prayer, even if he joins the imam mid-prayer. For the validity of following (iqtida'), the best time to intend is at the imam's opening takbir. If one intends while standing (before the imam starts) knowing the imam has not started, it is valid as long as the intention continues until the imam starts. If one mistakenly believes the imam has started and intends, but he has not, there is a disagreement; the relied-upon view is that it is not valid because the intention was based on a false assumption.

Key Terms
نية الإمامة (niyyat al-imamah): The intention to lead the prayer as imam, which is recommended for reward but not a condition for validity.
نية الاقتداء (niyyat al-iqtida'): The intention of the follower to follow the imam, which is a condition for the validity of the congregation.
نية الجماعة (niyyat al-jama'ah): The intention to pray in congregation, which is recommended for reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should a person intend to be an imam for obtaining reward (thawab)?
A) As soon as he enters the mosque
B) At the opening takbir of his prayer
C) When someone actually follows him in prayer
D) At the end of the prayer

Key Takeaway
The intention for imamate yields reward only when someone follows; the follower's intention for iqtida' must align with the actual start of the imam's prayer for validity.

Timing of Intention for Ghusl and Tayammum
Ruling on timing of intention for ghusl and tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the timing of intention for ghusl and tayammum, distinguishing between the sunan aspect and the condition for validity.

Core Idea
In ghusl, intention can be delayed until rinsing the mouth; in tayammum, it must coincide with striking the earth.

This passage from the Ashbah wa al-Nazair tradition clarifies the timing of intention (niyyah) for ghusl and tayammum. It applies the maxim that the ruling of ghusl follows that of wudu regarding supererogatory acts. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct application in purification rituals and for issuing accurate fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling for wudu
In wudu, intention for sunan is made at the beginning when washing the face.
2
Apply the analogy to ghusl
Ghusl follows wudu, so intention should be at the start of washing hands, or at latest at rinsing the mouth.
Allamah Shami clarified this.
3
Distinguish tayammum
Intention is a condition (shart) for validity, so it must be simultaneous with the act of striking the earth.
If delayed, tayammum is invalid.
4
Note the authority
The ruling is confirmed by Allamah Shami (Ibn Abidin), a later Hanafi authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غسل کا حکم بھی سنن کی ادائیگی میں وضوء کے مانند ہے۔
سنن کی ادائیگی میں جو حکم وضو کا ہے وہی حکم سنن کی ادائیگی میں غسل کا بھی ہے، لہذا انسل میں بھی شروع میں ہاتھ دھوتے وقت نیت کر لینی چاہئے ورنہ کلی کرتے وقت نیت کرلے جیسا کہ علامہ شامی نے تصریح کی ہے۔ و في التيمم: صحت تیم کے لئے نیت شرط ہے لہذا جب مٹی پر یم کے لئے ہاتھ رکھے گا اسی وقت نیت بھی کرے گا۔
The ruling of ghusl is like that of wudu in the performance of sunan. Whatever ruling applies to wudu in the performance of sunan, the same ruling applies to ghusl in the performance of sunan. Therefore, in ghusl, one should make intention at the beginning when washing the hands, otherwise at the time of rinsing the mouth, as clarified by Allamah Shami. And regarding tayammum: intention is a condition for the validity of tayammum, so when he places his hands on the earth for tayammum, he should also make intention at that time.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on when to make intention (niyyah) for ghusl and tayammum. The author first states that the rule for ghusl follows that of wudu regarding the timing of intention for performing supererogatory acts. In wudu, intention is made at the start of washing the face; similarly, in ghusl, one should intend at the start of washing the hands, or at least at the time of rinsing the mouth, as confirmed by Allamah Shami. Then, for tayammum, intention is required at the moment of striking the hands on the earth, as intention is a condition for its validity. The commentary emphasizes that delaying intention beyond these points affects the reward but not necessarily the validity if it is within the act.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intentional resolve to perform an act of worship, required at the start of ghusl and tayammum.
غسل (ghusl): Full-body ritual washing, often performed for purification after major impurity.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ritual purification using clean earth when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In ghusl, according to this passage, when is the latest permissible time to make intention?
A) Before beginning
B) At the time of rinsing the mouth
C) After completing the ghusl
D) At the end

Key Takeaway
The timing of intention differs: in ghusl it can span from start to rinsing mouth; in tayammum it must be exact at the moment of striking earth.
