Timing of Intention for Reward in Imamate and Congregation
Qawida on timing of reward intention in imamate and congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct timing of intention for reward in imamate and congregation, and apply it to a mufti's advisory scenario.

Core Idea
Intention for reward in imamate is made when someone follows, not before; for congregation, at start of follower's prayer.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair addresses a subtle point: the timing of intention for reward when leading or joining congregation. While intention for validity may not be required, the desire for reward requires proper timing. Ibn Nujaym explains that the imam should intend for reward precisely when someone follows him, and the follower should intend congregation at the start of his own prayer, even if the imam is already in progress.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the discussion is about intention for reward (nip for thawab), not intention for validity. The validity of imamate and congregation does not require this intention.
This distinction is crucial: intention for validity is a condition, but for reward it is about following the sunnah of making intent.
2
Isolate the two rulings
The matn gives two separate timings: (1) the imam's intention for imamate for reward should be at the time someone follows him, not before; (2) the follower's intention for congregation for reward should be at the beginning of his own prayer, even if the imam is already in the middle of his prayer.
Note the asymmetry: the imam's intention is triggered by another's action, while the follower's intention is at his own start.
3
Understand the reason
Intention for reward should accompany the action that generates reward. For the imam, the reward comes from being followed, so intention should coincide with that moment. For the follower, the reward comes from joining the congregation, so intention should be at the start of his prayer.
This aligns with the broader qawida: al-umur bi-maqasidiha (matters are judged by intentions), but here the maqsad (reward) requires the intention to join the act.
4
Apply to mufti advisory
When advising a mufti, clarify that the imam need not pre-intend imamate; he should simply begin his prayer and intend for reward when someone joins. The follower should intend congregation at the start of his own prayer, regardless of the imam's stage.
This prevents confusion, especially when followers join late.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَمْ أَرَوَقْتَ نِيَّةِ الْإِمَامَةِ لِلتَّوَابِ، وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ تَكُونَ وَقْتَ إِقْتِدَاءِ أَحَدٍ بِهِ لَا قَبْلَهُ، كَمَا أَنَّهُ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ تَكُوْنَ وَقْتَ نِيَّةِ الْجَمَاعَةِ أَوَّلَ صَلَاةِ الْمَامُوْمِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي أَثْنَاءِ صَلوةِ الإمام. هذا للقواب.
ترجمہ اور ثواب کے لئے امامت کی نیت کا وقت میں نے نہیں دیکھا اور مناسب ہے کہ وہ کسی کی اقتدار کے وقت ہو نہ کہ اس سے پہلے جیسا کہ مناسب ہے کہ جماعت کی نیت کا وقت مقتدی کی نماز کا شروع ہو اگر چیدو لام کی نماز کے درمیان ہو یہ تو ثواب کے لئے ہے۔ تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ صحت امامت کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے جیسا کہ ماسبق میں گذر چکا البتہ امام است کے ثواب کے حصول کے لئے امامت کی نیت کب کرے علامہ ابن نجیم فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے یہ مسئلہ نہیں دیکھا تو نہیں ہاں مناسب یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ جب کوئی شخص اس کی اقتداء کرے گا اسی وقت وہ حصول ثواب کے لئے امامت کی نیت بھی کرے گا اس سے پہلے نہیں۔
And I have not seen a time for the intention of imamate for reward, and it is appropriate that it be at the time of someone following him, not before, just as it is appropriate that the time of intention for congregation is the beginning of the follower's prayer, even if during the imam's prayer. This is for reward. Translation: And for the reward, I have not seen the time of the intention for imamate, and it is appropriate that it be at the time of someone's following him, not before, just as it is appropriate that the time of intention for congregation is the beginning of the follower's prayer, even if it is during the imam's prayer. This is for reward. Commentary: The issue is that intention is not a condition for the validity of imamate, as has passed earlier. However, when should the imam make intention for the attainment of reward? Allamah Ibn Nujaym says: I have not seen this issue; it is appropriate that when someone follows him, at that time he should make intention for imamate for reward, not before.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from the matn of al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair discusses the timing of intention for reward in imamate and congregation. The author, Ibn Nujaym, states he did not find a specified time for intending imamate for reward, but logically it should be when someone follows him, not earlier. Similarly, for intending to pray in congregation, the follower should intend at the start of his own prayer, even if the imam has already begun. The commentary explains that intention is not a condition for the validity of the imamate itself, but for reward, it should coincide with the follower's action. This is an application of the general principle that intention should accompany the act for reward.

Key Terms
إمامة (imamah): Leading the congregation in prayer; here the focus is on the intention for reward, not validity.
نية (niyyah): Intention to perform an act for the sake of Allah, here specifically for imamate and congregation.
جماعة (jama'ah): Congregational prayer; intention to join the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida, when should the imam intend imamate for reward?
A) Before the prayer starts
B) At the time someone follows him
C) At the beginning of his prayer
D) It is not required

Key Takeaway
Intention for reward in imamate is made when someone follows; for congregation, at follower's prayer start.

Certainty in Intention for Following the Imam
Refining timing and certainty of intention for iqtida

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of certainty (jazm) in intention to determine the validity of following the imam, and distinguish between cases of knowledge and presumption.

Core Idea
Intention for following the imam requires certainty; presumption invalidates it.

In Hanafi law, the validity of acts of worship often hinges on the quality of intention. This passage from Fath al-Qadir refines the timing of intention for following the imam (iqtida), highlighting that intention must be certain—not based on mere presumption. We will examine the two scenarios and the underlying principle that governs the fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Condition
Recognize that the act under discussion is following the imam (iqtida) in prayer, and the condition for its validity is the presence of intention with certainty (jazm).
Intention itself is a pillar, but certainty is an additional requirement for this condition.
2
Distinguish the Two Cases
The passage presents two scenarios: (a) intending while knowing the imam has not started (valid), and (b) intending while presuming the imam has started, but he has not (disputed, with the relied-upon view being invalid).
In both cases the intention is made before the imam starts; the difference is the state of knowledge.
3
Apply the Qāʿidah of Certainty
Apply the principle that intention requires certainty (jazm). In the first case, certainty exists (knowledge); in the second, only presumption (ẓann) exists, so intention is deficient.
The broader qāʿidah is 'al-umūr bi-maqāṣidihā', but this is a specific application requiring decisive intention.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafī Dispute
Some Hanafīs held the second case valid if the intention remains until the imam starts, but the stronger view (referenced as 'qīla lā yajūz') is that it is invalid due to lack of certainty.
This illustrates a legitimate ikhtilāf within the school, resolved by tarjīḥ based on the principle of jazm.
5
Determine the Muftā Bihi
In fatwa, the operative ruling is that the iqtida is invalid. This is the position taken in Fath al-Qadir and supported by later scholars like Allamah Hamawi.
The mufti must apply the stricter view to avoid doubt in worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا لِصحة الإقْعِدَاءِ بِالْإِمَامِ، فَقَالَ فِي فَتح الْقَدِير وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يُنْوِيَ الَّا أَبَدَاء عِنْدَ إِفْتِتَاحِ الْإِمَامِ، فَإِنْ نَوَى حِيْنَ وَقَفَ عَالِماً بِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَشْرَعْ جَازَ، وَإِنْ نَوَى ذَلِكَ عَلَىٰ ظُنُّ أَنَّهُ شَرَعَ وَلَمْ يَشْرَعْ ، أَخْتُلِفَ فِيْهِ، قِيْلَ: لَا يَجُوْزُ انْتَهى. ترجمه اور بہر حال امام کی اقتداء کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے تو فتح القدیر میں کہا ہے کہ افضل یہ ہے کہ اتقاء کی نیت اقتداء کو شروع کرنے کے وقت کرے اور اگر کھڑے ہوتے ہی یہ معلوم ہوتے ہوئے نیت کر لی کہ امام نے نماز شروع نہیں کی تو بھی جائز ہے اور اگر اس وقت نیت کر لی یہ گمان کرتے ہوئے کہ اس نے نماز شروع کر دی حالانکہ اس نے شروع نہیں کی تھی تو اس میں اختلاف ہے کہا گیا ہے کہ جائز نہیں ہے کلام پورا ہوا۔ تشریح اقتداء کی صحت کے لئے نیت اقتداء شرط ہے، جس وقت امام نماز شروع کرے اس وقت اقتداء کی نیت کر لینی چاہئے اگر امام کے شروع کرنے سے پہلے ہی اقتداء کی نیت کر لی اور وہ نیت امام کے نماز شروع کرنے تک باقی رہی تو بھی حکما وہ نیت امام کی نماز کے شروع میں ہوئی اس لئے درست ہے اور اگر اس نے کھڑے ہوتے ہی اقتداء کی نیت کرلی اور اس کا گمان یہ تھا کہ امام نے نماز شروع کر دی ہے حالانکہ امام نے نماز شروع نہیں کی تھی اس کے درست ہونے میں اختلاف ہے ایک قول ہے کہ اقتداء درست نہ ہو گی ان دونوں شکلوں میں علامہ حموی نے فرق یہ کیا ہے کہ نیت کے اندر جزم مطلوب ہے اور وہ موجود ہے جبکہ دوسری شکل میں اس نے ظن اور گمان پر نیت کی ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں جزم نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کی اقتداء درست نہ ہوئی کیونکہ فقہاء نے نیت کے اندر جزم کی شرط لگائی ہے۔ (تفصیل کے لئے دیکھئے تارتارخانیہ نا ہی ۳۲ و کذائی البند سیتا ہی (۹۹)
And as for validity of following the imam, it is said in Fath al-Qadir: The best is that he intend following at the imam's opening. If he intends while standing, knowing that he (the imam) has not started, it is permissible. And if he intends based on presumption that he has started while he hasn't, there is difference: it is said it is not permissible. Translation: And for the correctness of following the imam, in Fath al-Qadir it is said: The best is that the intention of following be made at the time of beginning the following. If he intends while standing, knowing that the imam has not started, it is permissible. And if he intends at that time presuming that he has started while he had not, there is difference; it is said it is not permissible. Commentary: Intention of following is a condition for validity, it should be made at the time the imam starts. If made before the imam starts and remains until he starts, it is valid. If he intends while standing assuming the imam has started but he hasn't, there is difference; one opinion says invalid. Allamah Hamawi distinguished: intention requires certainty (jazm); in the first case certainty exists; in the second case it is based on presumption, so invalid.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage refines the timing of intention for validly following the imam (iqtida). The best is to intend when the imam begins. If one intends while standing knowing the imam hasn't started, it's permissible because the intention continues until the imam starts. But if one intends based on the presumption that the imam started and he hadn't, there is a dispute. The relied-upon position is that it is invalid because intention requires certainty (jazm), which is lacking. This distinction is attributed to Allamah Hamawi. The text thus provides a nuanced application of the principle that intention must be certain and concurrent with the act.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida): Following the imam in prayer; intention is a condition for its validity.
جزم (jazm): Certainty in intention; absence makes the intention invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a follower intends to follow the imam while standing, wrongly presuming the imam has started, his following is:
A) Valid because his intention remains
B) Invalid due to lack of certainty
C) Valid if he is knowledgeable
D) Valid only for supererogatory prayers

Key Takeaway
Intention for following the imam must be certain (jazm); presumption invalidates the following, and this is the operative position in fatwa.

Timing of Intention for Water to Become Musta'mal
Timing of intention for musta'mal water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct timing of intention for making water musta'mal and explain why intention is required according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The intention to draw near to Allah must be present at the moment of scooping water for it to become musta'mal.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational rule in Hanafi fiqh regarding the status of water used for purification. The key distinction is that water becomes musta'mal only when used with the intention of devotion (qurbah), and this intention must be present at the time of scooping the water. Understanding this timing is crucial for determining whether water can be reused for wudu or ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The passage states that the time for making intention (niyyat al-taqarrub) for water to become musta'mal is at the moment of scooping (al-ightiraf). Identify this as the core legal ruling.
2
Recognize the condition
The intention must be for devotion (taqarrub), not mere use. This condition transforms pure water into musta'mal water, which is no longer purifying.
Without this intention, water remains pure even after use.
3
Understand Imam Muhammad's principle
Imam Muhammad states that water becomes musta'mal by one thing only: use with the intention of performing an act of closeness (qurbah). This principle is relied upon in the Hanafi school.
Example: performing wudu while already in wudu with the intention of devotion makes the water musta'mal.
4
Apply the rule in practice
In real-life scenarios, the mufti must inquire about the user's intention at the time of scooping water. If the intention was devotion, the water is musta'mal; otherwise, it remains pure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا نِيَّةُ التَّقَرُّبِ لِصَيْرُوْرَةِ الْمَاءِ مُسْتَعْمَلًا فَوَقْتُهَا عِنْدَ الْاِغْتِرَافِ.
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال پانی کے مستعمل ہونے کے لئے تقریب کی نیت؟ تو اس کا وقت پانی لیتے وقت ہے۔ تشریح ما مستعمل ہونے کے لئے استعمال کرتے وقت اگر قربت کا اراد کیا گیا ہے تو وہ مستعمل ہو جائے گا لہذا استعمال کرتے وقت کی نیت قربت معیار ہے۔
أو باستعماله على قصد القربة بان يتوضأ وهو متوضئ ناويا للوضوء و على اصل محمد رحمه الله الماء انما يصير مستعملا بشئ واحد وهو الاستعمال على قصد اقامة القربة. تار تار خانية ج ا ص : (۲۱۳)
And as for the intention of devotion (taqarrub) for making water musta'mal, its time is at the time of scooping (taking water). Translation: And as for the intention for making water used, its time is at the time of taking water. Commentary: When using water, if one intends closeness, it becomes musta'mal; the intention of closeness at the time of use is the criterion. Or by using it with the intention of closeness, like one who performs wudu while already in wudu, intending wudu. According to the principle of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), water becomes musta'mal by one thing: use with the intention of performing an act of closeness. (Tatarkhaniya, vol. 1, p. 213)
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage gives the timing for the intention that makes water musta'mal (used water that cannot be used for purification again). When scooping water for an act of worship, if one intends devotion (qurbah), the water becomes musta'mal at that moment. The time of intention is when one takes the water, not later. The commentary adds that according to Imam Muhammad, water becomes musta'mal only through use with the intention of performing an act of closeness, such as performing wudu while already in wudu, intending wudu again. This clarifies that the intention must accompany the act of taking water.

Key Terms
نية التقرّب (niyyat al-taqarrub): Intention to draw near to Allah through an act of worship.
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used for purification and is no longer pure enough for similar use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should one intend devotion to make water musta'mal?
A) After using the water
B) At the time of scooping the water
C) Before starting wudu
D) Only if water is scarce

Key Takeaway
The intention of devotion must be at the moment of scooping water for it to become musta'mal.

Timing of Intention for Zakat and Sadaqat al-Fitr
Timing of intention for zakat and sadaqat al-fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida on the timing of intention for zakat and sadaqat al-fitr to scenarios of payment, setting aside, and delayed intention, and identify the exceptions.

Core Idea
Zakat intention must accompany payment or setting aside; delayed intention is valid if wealth is still with the recipient.

The timing of intention in obligatory charities is a key area where the Hanafi school balances principle and practicality. While intention must generally accompany the act, exceptions are made to ease the obligation. This passage from al-Hidayah and Sharh al-Majma lays out the rules and their limits, showing how the school accommodates real-world payment difficulties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base qawida
Read the passage and extract the core legal maxim: payment of zakat is not valid without an intention concurrent with payment or concurrent with setting aside the obligatory amount.
The qawida is explicitly stated from al-Hidayah.
2
Understand the underlying reason (talil)
The passage gives the reason: zakat is an act of worship, so intention is a condition. The default is concurrency, but since payment is often spread over time, the law eases by allowing intention at setting aside, analogous to advancing intention for fasting.
This talil shows the qiyas with fasting.
3
Recognize the exception for installment payments
When zakat is paid in multiple installments, intention at the time of setting aside the total amount suffices for all subsequent payments. This is the practical application of the qawida.
This is the furu' of the qawida.
4
Analyze the delayed intention scenario
The passage from Sharh al-Majma discusses a case where payment occurs without intention, but the intention is formed later while the money is still in the poor's hand. The ruling is that it is valid; otherwise invalid. This is an istithna' (exception) to the requirement of concurrency.
The condition is that the wealth must still be in the recipient's possession.
5
Apply to sadaqat al-fitr
The passage states that sadaqat al-fitr follows the same rules for intention and disbursement, except that its disbursement is specific to fitr, not general zakat.
This extends the qawida to another obligatory charity.

رَأَمَّا وَقْتُهَا فِي الزَّكَاةِ، فَقَالَ فِي الْهِدَايَةِ لَا يَجُوْزُ أَدَاءُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَّا بِنِيَّةٍ مَقَارِنَةٍ لِلْأَدَاءِ، أَوْ مُقَارِنَةٍ لِعَزْلِ مِقْدَارِ مَا وَجَبَ ؛ لأنَّ الزَّكَاةَ عِبَادَةٌ، فَكَانَتْ مِنْ شَرْطِهَا النِّيَّةُ. وَالْأَصْلُ فِيْهَا الإقتران إلا أن الدَّفَعَ يَتَفَرَّقَ ، فَاكْتُفِي بِوُجُوْدِهَا حَالَةَ الْعَزْلِ تَيْسِيراً كَتَقْدِيمِ النِّيَّةِ فِي الصَّوْمِ إنْتَهى وَقَدْ جَوَّزُوْا التَّقْدِيمَ عَلَى الأَدَاءِ لَكِنْ عِنْدَ الْعَزْلِ وَهَلْ يَجُوزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مُتَاخِرَةِ عَنِ الْأَدَاءِ. فَقَالَ فِي شَرْحِ الْمَجْمَعِ : لَوْدَفَعَهَا بِلَا نِيَّةٍ، ثُمَّ نَوَى بَعْدَهُ، فَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَالُ قَائِمًا فِي يَدِ الْفَقِيْرِ جَازَ وَإِلَّا فَلَا. إنْتَهى وَأَمَّا صَدَقَةُ الْفِطْرِ : فَكَالزَّكَاةِ نِيَّةٌ وَمَصْرِفاً، فالو إلا اللهى، فَإِنَّهُ مَصْرَت لِلْفِطْرِدُونَ الزَّكَاةِ.
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال زکوۃ میں اس کا وقت تو ہدایہ میں کہا ہے کہ اداء ز کوۃ جائز نہیں بغیر اس نیت کے جو ادا ت ملی ہوئی ہو یا مقدار واجب کو علیحدہ کرنے سے ملی ہوئی ہو اس لئے کہ زکوۃ ایک عبادت ہے تو نیت اس کے لئے شرط ہے جس میں اصل اقتران ہے لیکن مال دینا بار بار ہوتا ہے اس لئے آسانی کے لئے علیحدہ کرنے کے وقت اس کے پائے جانے پر اکتفا کر لیا گیا جیسے روزہ میں نیت کو مقدم کر دینا، ہدایہ کی بات پوری ہوگئی اور فقہا ء نے ادا پر مقدم کرنے کو جائز فرمایا ہے لیکن مال علیحدہ کرتے وقت اور کیا وہ اس نیت سے بھی جائز ہے جو اداء سے بھی مئوخر ہو تو شرح مجمع میں ہے کہ اگر وہ بغیر نیت کے دیدی پھر اس کے بعد نیت کی تو اگر مال فقیر کے قبضہ میں موجود ہو تو جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں شرح مجمع کا کلام پورا ہوا ر ہا صدقہ فطر تو وہ نیت اور مصرف کے اعتبار سے زکوۃ کے مانند ہے فقہاء یہ فرماتے ہیں
And as for its time in zakat, it is said in al-Hidayah: Payment of zakat is not permissible except with an intention concurrent with the payment, or concurrent with setting aside the obligatory amount, because zakat is an act of worship, so intention is a condition. The principle is concurrency, but since payment may be gradual, its existence at the time of setting aside is deemed sufficient for ease, like advancing intention in fasting. End of quote. They (jurists) have permitted advancing the intention over payment, but at the time of setting aside. And is it permissible with an intention delayed after payment? It is said in Sharh al-Majma: If he paid without intention, then intended afterwards, if the wealth is still in the hand of the poor, it is permissible; otherwise not. End. And as for sadaqat al-fitr: it is like zakat in intention and disbursement, except that its disbursement is for fitr not zakat. Translation: And as for its time in zakat, al-Hidayah said: Payment of zakat is not permissible without a intention concurrent with payment or concurrent with setting aside the obligatory amount, because zakat is an act of worship, so intention is a condition. The principle is concurrency, but since payment is spread, it is sufficient to have it at the time of setting aside for ease, like advancing intention in fasting. The jurists have permitted advancing the intention over payment, but at the time of setting aside. And is it permissible with an intention delayed after payment? In Sharh al-Majma: If he paid without intention, then intended afterwards, if the wealth is still in the possession of the poor, it is permissible; otherwise not. End. And sadaqat al-fitr is like zakat in intention and disbursement, except that its disbursement is for fitr, not zakat. The jurists say...
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage details the timing of intention for zakat and sadaqat al-fitr. For zakat, intention must accompany the payment or the act of setting aside the amount. Since zakat is a worship, intention is a condition. Usually it must be concurrent, but due to practical difficulty when paying in installments, it is sufficient to intend when setting aside the money, similar to advancing intention for fasting. Jurists allow intention before payment, but at the time of setting aside. For a delayed intention after payment, if the money is still with the poor, it is valid; otherwise not. Sadaqat al-fitr follows the same rule for intention and disbursement, except its specific purpose. The passage ends abruptly, likely continuing on the next page.

Key Terms
نية مقارنة (niyyah muqarinah): Intention that accompanies the act of payment or setting aside.
عزل (azl): Setting aside the obligatory amount of zakat from one's wealth.
صدقہ فطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Compulsory charity given at the end of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person pays zakat without intention and later intends while the money is still in the poor's hand, the payment is:
A) Invalid always
B) Valid according to Sharh al-Majma
C) Valid only if setting aside was done
D) Requires repeating

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accommodates practical difficulty in zakat by allowing intention at setting aside and delayed intention while the property is with the poor.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
beginner
6 min
Requirement of Determination (Jism) in Niyyah for Following an Imam
Analyzes the validity of following an imam based on the certainty of intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of jism (determination) in niyyah for following an imam and identify when a follower's intention is insufficient due to lack of certainty.

Core Idea
Intention in following an imam must be certain (jism); assumption alone invalidates the prayer following.

This lesson unpacks a specific condition of niyyah in congregational prayer: the requirement that the follower's intention be definitive, not conjectural. Allamah Hamawi’s analysis clarifies why mere guesswork fails to satisfy the condition of jism, a key term in Hanafi jurisprudence. Mastering this rule sharpens your understanding of how niyyah operates in worship.

Guided Path
1
Define the act and the condition
Identify the act as following the imam (iqtida) in prayer. The condition is that the follower's niyyah must be certain (jism) as stipulated by jurists.
2
Identify the basis for the condition
The passage cites the consensus of jurists that niyyah requires jism. This is a general principle applied to iqtida.
No explicit Quran or hadith dalil is given; it is an established rule.
3
Analyze the distinction by Allamah Hamawi
He differentiates two forms: one with definite intention (valid) and one with conjectural intention (invalid). The difference lies in the presence/absence of jism.
Form 1: certain internal intention. Form 2: intention based on assumption.
4
Apply the rule
If the follower intends based on assumption (ظن), jism is absent, so the iqtida is invalid. If the intention is certain, it is valid.
Certainty is a heart-based state, not necessarily verbalized.
5
Note the implication for prayer validity
The validity of the follower's prayer depends on this condition. Lack of jism means the prayer following is void and must be repeated.

الله الماء انما يصير مستعملا بشئ واحد وهو الاستعمال على قصد اقامة القربة. تار تار خانية ج ا ص : (۲۱۳) رَأَمَّا وَقْتُهَا فِي الزَّكَاةِ، فَقَالَ فِي الْهِدَايَةِ لَا يَجُوْزُ أَدَاءُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَّا اداء ز کوۃ جائز نہیں بغیر اس نیت کے جو ادا ت ملی ہوئی ہو یا مقدار واجب کو علیحدہ کرنے سے ملی ہوئی ہو اس لئے کہ زکوۃ ایک عبادت ہے تو نیت اس کے لئے شرط ہے جس میں اصل اقتران ہے لیکن مال دینا بار بار ہوتا علیحدہ کرتے وقت اور کیا وہ اس نیت سے بھی جائز ہے جو اداء سے بھی مئوخر ہو تو شرح مجمع میں ہے کہ اگر وہ بغیر نیت کے دیدی پھر اس کے بعد نیت کی تو اگر مال فقیر کے قبضہ میں موجود ہو تو جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں اندر نیت کا ہونا ضروری ہے اصل تو یہی ہے کہ یہ نیت ادا ئیگلی کے وقت جڑی ہوئی ہونی چاہئے لیکن اگر کسی نے زکوۃ کی واجب مقدار کو علیحدہ کرتے وقت نیت کر لی تو لوگوں کی آسانی کو مد نظر رکھتے ہوئے یہ نیت بھی معتبر ہوگی۔ و اما شرط ادائها فنية مقارنة للاداء او الفرضما وجب هكذا في الكنز (بند برج اص: ۷۰) اور اگر بلانیت زکوۃ فقیر کو مال دیدیا تو ایسی صورت میں کب تک زکوة کی نیت معتبر ہوئی تو اگر فقیر کے قبضہ اجزاء والا فلا هندیه ج ۱، ص ۱۷۱) و أما صدقة الفطر : نیت اور مصرف کے اعتبار سے صدقہ فطر کا حکم زکوۃ کے قریب قریب ہے ورنہ ہر ایک کے لئے چند ایسی شرائط ہیں جو دوسرے کے لئے ہیں جیسا کہ زکوۃ کے اندر حولان حول وغیرہ شرط ہے۔ و صدقۃ الفطر كالزكاة في المصارف و في كل حال و تحته في رد المحتار بل المراد في احوال الدفع الى المصارف من اشتراط النية واشتراط التمليك فلا الا حاجة كما في البدائع (شامی زکریا ج ۳ ص: ۳۲۵) قالوا الا الذمی : ذمی یعنی غیر مسلم کو صدقہ فطر دیا جا سکتا ہے یا نہیں اس میں فقہاء کی رائے یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے صدقہ فطر زمی کو دید یا تو جائز تو ہو جائے گا لیکن مکروہ ہوگا جبکہ امام شافعی اور امام ابی یوسف کی ایک روایت کے مطابقی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ولو اعطى ذميا جاز و فى الخانية جاز و يكره وعند الشافعي واحدى الروايتين عن ابي يوسف لايجوز ( تار تار خانیه ج ۲، ص: ۴۲۴) وَأَمَا الصَّوْمُ فَلَا يَخْلُوْا إِمَّا أَيَّكُوْنَ فَرْضاً أَوْ نَفْلًا، فَإِنْ كَانَ فَرْضاً، فَلَايَخْلُوْا إِمَّا أَيَّكُونَ أَدَاءَ رَمَضَانَ أَوْ غَيْرَهُ. فَإِنْ كَانَ أَدَاءَ رَمَضَانَ جَازَ بِنِيَّةٍ مُتَقَدِّمَةٍ مِنْ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَبِمُقَارِنَةٍ، وَهُوَ الْأَصْلُ، وَبِمُتَأَخْرَةِ عَنِ الشَّرُوْعِ إِلَى مَاقَبْلَ نَصْفِ النَّهَارِ الشَّرِي تَيْسِيراً عَلَى الصَّائِمِينَ. وَإِنْ كَانَ غَيْرِ أَدَاءِ رَمَضَانَ مِنْ قَضَاءِ، أَوْ نَذْرٍ، أَوْ كَفَّارَةٍ، فَيَجُوْزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مُتَقَدِّمَةٍ مِنْ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ إِلى طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ، وَيَجُوْزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مَقَارِنَةٍ لِطُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ لأنَّ الْأَصْلَ الْقِرَانُ، كَمَا فِي فَتَاوَى قَاضِي حَانْ وَإِنْ كَانَ نَفْلًا، فَكَرَ مَضَانَ أَدَاءً. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال روز و تو وہ دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو وہ فرض ہوگا یا نفل اگر وہ فرض ہوتو وہ خالی ایک بار وہ اداء رمضان ہوگا یا اس کے علاوہ ہو گا اگر وہ اداء رمضان ہو تو وہ اس نیت سے بھی جائز ہے جو غروب شمس سے مقدم
There is disagreement about its validity. One opinion: following is not valid in both forms. Allamah Hamawi distinguished: in niyyah, determination (jism) is required and it exists, while in the second form he intended based on assumption and conjecture; obviously there is no determination, so his following is not valid because jurists have stipulated determination in niyyah. As for the intention of seeking nearness for water becoming used (musta'mal), its time is at the time of scooping. Explanation: When using water for it to become used, if one intends nearness, it becomes used; hence the intention of nearness at the time of use is the criterion. Or by using it with the intention of nearness, e.g., one performs wudu while already in wudu intending wudu. According to the principle of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), water becomes used by only one thing: using it with the intention of performing worship. As for its time in zakat, Al-Hidayah says: Payment of zakat is not valid except with a niyyah concurrent with the payment or concurrent with setting aside the amount due, because zakat is an act of worship, so niyyah is a condition of it. The principle is concurrency, but since payment may be distributed, its presence at the time of setting aside is deemed sufficient for ease, like advancing the niyyah in fasting. They have permitted advancement before payment, but at the time of setting aside. Is it valid with a niyyah delayed after payment? In Sharh al-Majma': If he paid without niyyah, then intended afterward, if the wealth still exists in the poor person's hand, it is valid; otherwise not. As for Sadaqat al-Fitr: it is like zakat in niyyah and channels of expenditure, except the dhimmi: the dhimmi is a channel for Sadaqat al-Fitr but not for zakat. Explanation: Zakat is an act of worship, so niyyah is necessary. The principle is that this niyyah should be attached at the time of payment, but if one makes niyyah at the time of setting aside the wajib amount, considering people's ease, this niyyah is also valid. If one gave wealth to a poor person without niyyah, then when is delayed niyyah valid? If the wealth still exists in the poor person's possession, delayed niyyah is valid; if he has spent it, then delayed niyyah is not valid. As for Sadaqat al-Fitr: its ruling is close to zakat in niyyah and channels, but each has some conditions not found in the other, e.g., the passing of a year is a condition in zakat. Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat in channels and in every case; the meaning in conditions of payment to channels is the stipulation of niyyah and stipulation of ownership. They said except the dhimmi: whether Sadaqat al-Fitr can be given to a dhimmi? The jurists' opinion: if one gives Sadaqat al-Fitr to a dhimmi, it is valid but disliked, while according to Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf, it is not valid. As for fasting: it is either obligatory or supererogatory. If obligatory, it is either Ramadan or other. If it is Ramadan fasting, it is valid with a niyyah advanced from sunset, with a concurrent niyyah (which is the principle), and with a delayed niyyah from the start up to before midday as a concession for the fasting people. If it is other than Ramadan, such as make-up, vow, or expiation, it is valid with a niyyah advanced from sunset to dawn, and valid with a concurrent niyyah at dawn because the principle is concurrency. If supererogatory, it is like Ramadan.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the timing rules for niyyah (intention) in various acts of worship, drawn from Hanafi sources. It opens with a discussion on the requirement of determination (jism) in niyyah for the validity of following an imam in prayer. Allamah Hamawi distinguishes between two forms: one where the follower has definite intention, and another where he intends based on assumption; only the former is valid because scholars have mandated certainty in niyyah.

The passage then addresses the timing of niyyah for making water 'musta'mal' (used). For water to become musta'mal, the intention of seeking nearness (qurbah) must be present at the moment of scooping the water. This is based on Imam Muhammad's principle that water becomes used solely through use with the intention of worship.

Moving to zakat, Al-Hidayah is quoted: niyyah must be concurrent with payment or at the time of setting aside the due amount. Since zakat is a form of worship, niyyah is a condition. The default is temporal concurrency, but because payment may be staggered, scholars allowed the niyyah at the time of setting aside for ease, analogous to advancing niyyah in fasting. Furthermore, if one pays without niyyah, a delayed niyyah is accepted only if the wealth still exists in the recipient's hand; otherwise not.

Sadaqat al-Fitr follows the same rules as zakat regarding niyyah and expenditure channels, except that it may be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen), though it is disliked. Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf prohibit it.

Finally, the passage details the timing of niyyah for fasting. For Ramadan, niyyah can be made from sunset the previous night up to before midday of the same day. For other obligatory fasts (qada', nadhr, kaffarah), the window is from sunset to dawn. For voluntary fasts, the same leniency as Ramadan applies. The underlying principle is that while concurrency is the original requirement, concessions (taysir) are granted for these acts.

Throughout, the passage emphasizes that niyyah is a condition for worship, and the timing rules reflect a balance between the general principle of concurrency and the need for ease in specific circumstances.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; a condition for the validity of worship, requiring determination (jism) and concurrency with the act unless ease allows otherwise.
جزم (jism): Certainty and determination in intention, as opposed to mere assumption or probability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what invalidates a follower's iqtida in prayer?
A) Lack of verbal intention.
B) Intention based on assumption rather than certainty.
C) Not facing the qibla.
D) Following an imam who has broken wudu.

Key Takeaway
The follower's intention must be certain (jism); assumption invalidates the prayer following.

Timing of Niyyah for Water Becoming Musta'mal
Explains when water becomes musta'mal based on the timing of niyyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct timing of niyyah for making water musta'mal according to the Hanafi school and apply the rule to scenarios of water use.

Core Idea
Water becomes musta'mal only when used with intention of worship at the moment of scooping.

This lesson examines a specific rule regarding water that has been used for worship: when does it become 'musta'mal' (used water)? The passage clarifies that the key is the intention of seeking nearness (qurbah) at the time of scooping the water, not later. Understanding this timing helps distinguish between pure and used water in practical fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using water for worship with the intention of nearness. The ruling is that water becomes musta'mal (used) and loses its purifying quality.
2
Locate the timing condition
The passage states that the time for the niyyah is at the moment of scooping (عند الاغتراف). This is when the intention must be present.
Scooping is the beginning of the act of using water.
3
Understand the basis in Imam Muhammad's principle
Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) held that water becomes musta'mal by one thing: using it with the intention of performing worship. The conjunction of use and intention is essential.
This is from the principle of Imam Muhammad, a foundational Hanafi authority.
4
Apply to a scenario
If someone scoops water intending to perform wudu for worship, the water becomes musta'mal. If they scoop without intention, it does not become musta'mal until they actually use it with intention.
The intention must be present at the start of the act.

There is disagreement about its validity. One opinion: following is not valid in both forms. Allamah Hamawi distinguished: in niyyah, determination (jism) is required and it exists, while in the second form he intended based on assumption and conjecture; obviously there is no determination, so his following is not valid because jurists have stipulated determination in niyyah. As for the intention of seeking nearness for water becoming used (musta'mal), its time is at the time of scooping. Explanation: When using water for it to become used, if one intends nearness, it becomes used; hence the intention of nearness at the time of use is the criterion. Or by using it with the intention of nearness, e.g., one performs wudu while already in wudu intending wudu. According to the principle of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), water becomes used by only one thing: using it with the intention of performing worship. As for its time in zakat, Al-Hidayah says: Payment of zakat is not valid except with a niyyah concurrent with the payment or concurrent with setting aside the amount due, because zakat is an act of worship, so niyyah is a condition of it. The principle is concurrency, but since payment may be distributed, its presence at the time of setting aside is deemed sufficient for ease, like advancing the niyyah in fasting. They have permitted advancement before payment, but at the time of setting aside. Is it valid with a niyyah delayed after payment? In Sharh al-Majma': If he paid without niyyah, then intended afterward, if the wealth still exists in the poor person's hand, it is valid; otherwise not. As for Sadaqat al-Fitr: it is like zakat in niyyah and channels of expenditure, except the dhimmi: the dhimmi is a channel for Sadaqat al-Fitr but not for zakat. Explanation: Zakat is an act of worship, so niyyah is necessary. The principle is that this niyyah should be attached at the time of payment, but if one makes niyyah at the time of setting aside the wajib amount, considering people's ease, this niyyah is also valid. If one gave wealth to a poor person without niyyah, then when is delayed niyyah valid? If the wealth still exists in the poor person's possession, delayed niyyah is valid; if he has spent it, then delayed niyyah is not valid. As for Sadaqat al-Fitr: its ruling is close to zakat in niyyah and channels, but each has some conditions not found in the other, e.g., the passing of a year is a condition in zakat. Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat in channels and in every case; the meaning in conditions of payment to channels is the stipulation of niyyah and stipulation of ownership. They said except the dhimmi: whether Sadaqat al-Fitr can be given to a dhimmi? The jurists' opinion: if one gives Sadaqat al-Fitr to a dhimmi, it is valid but disliked, while according to Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf, it is not valid. As for fasting: it is either obligatory or supererogatory. If obligatory, it is either Ramadan or other. If it is Ramadan fasting, it is valid with a niyyah advanced from sunset, with a concurrent niyyah (which is the principle), and with a delayed niyyah from the start up to before midday as a concession for the fasting people. If it is other than Ramadan, such as make-up, vow, or expiation, it is valid with a niyyah advanced from sunset to dawn, and valid with a concurrent niyyah at dawn because the principle is concurrency. If supererogatory, it is like Ramadan.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the timing rules for niyyah (intention) in various acts of worship, drawn from Hanafi sources. It opens with a discussion on the requirement of determination (jism) in niyyah for the validity of following an imam in prayer. Allamah Hamawi distinguishes between two forms: one where the follower has definite intention, and another where he intends based on assumption; only the former is valid because scholars have mandated certainty in niyyah.

The passage then addresses the timing of niyyah for making water 'musta'mal' (used). For water to become musta'mal, the intention of seeking nearness (qurbah) must be present at the moment of scooping the water. This is based on Imam Muhammad's principle that water becomes used solely through use with the intention of worship.

Moving to zakat, Al-Hidayah is quoted: niyyah must be concurrent with payment or at the time of setting aside the due amount. Since zakat is a form of worship, niyyah is a condition. The default is temporal concurrency, but because payment may be staggered, scholars allowed the niyyah at the time of setting aside for ease, analogous to advancing niyyah in fasting. Furthermore, if one pays without niyyah, a delayed niyyah is accepted only if the wealth still exists in the recipient's hand; otherwise not.

Sadaqat al-Fitr follows the same rules as zakat regarding niyyah and expenditure channels, except that it may be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen), though it is disliked. Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf prohibit it.

Finally, the passage details the timing of niyyah for fasting. For Ramadan, niyyah can be made from sunset the previous night up to before midday of the same day. For other obligatory fasts (qada', nadhr, kaffarah), the window is from sunset to dawn. For voluntary fasts, the same leniency as Ramadan applies. The underlying principle is that while concurrency is the original requirement, concessions (taysir) are granted for these acts.

Throughout, the passage emphasizes that niyyah is a condition for worship, and the timing rules reflect a balance between the general principle of concurrency and the need for ease in specific circumstances.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; a condition for the validity of worship, requiring determination (jism) and concurrency with the act unless ease allows otherwise.
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used for worship and thus loses its purifying quality; it becomes musta'mal when used with the intention of worship.

Timing of Niyyah in Zakat
Explains the timing rules for niyyah in zakat payment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on the timing of niyyah for zakat, including concurrent, advanced (at setting aside), and delayed niyyah scenarios.

Core Idea
Zakat niyyah can be concurrent, advanced at setting aside, or even delayed if the wealth still exists in the recipient's hand.

This lesson focuses on the timing of niyyah for zakat, as explained in Al-Hidayah. Since zakat is an act of worship, niyyah is required. The general principle is concurrency with payment, but ease is granted by allowing niyyah at the time of setting aside the due amount. Additionally, an unintentional payment can be rectified by a delayed niyyah if the wealth is still with the poor person. Understanding these taysir (ease) rules helps muftis handle real-world cases where payments are made without immediate intention.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Zakat payment is not valid except with a niyyah concurrent with the payment (مقارنة للأداء). This is the default rule because zakat is an act of worship requiring niyyah.
The principle is from Al-Hidayah.
2
Recognize the concession for setting aside
If one sets aside a specific amount of wealth for zakat with the intention, that niyyah is sufficient even if the actual distribution occurs later. This is a concession for ease (taysir) because payment may be staggered.
The niyyah at the time of setting aside (عزل) is valid.
3
Understand the delayed niyyah scenario
If one pays zakat without any niyyah, then later intends it as zakat, it is valid only if the wealth still exists in the poor person's hand (قائماً في يد الفقير). If the recipient has spent it, the delayed niyyah does not make it count as zakat.
This is from Sharh al-Majma'.
4
Apply to a case
Example: A person gives money to a poor person without zakat intention. Later he remembers and intends it as zakat. If the poor person still has the money, it counts as zakat. Otherwise not.

مِنْ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَبِمُقَارِنَةٍ، وَهُوَ الْأَصْلُ، وَبِمُتَأَخْرَةِ عَنِ الشَّرُوْعِ إِلَى مَاقَبْلَ نَصْفِ النَّهَارِ الشَّرِي تَيْسِيراً عَلَى الصَّائِمِينَ. وَإِنْ كَانَ غَيْرِ أَدَاءِ رَمَضَانَ مِنْ قَضَاءِ، أَوْ نَذْرٍ، أَوْ كَفَّارَةٍ، فَيَجُوْزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مُتَقَدِّمَةٍ مِنْ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ إِلى طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ، وَيَجُوْزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مَقَارِنَةٍ لِطُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ لأنَّ الْأَصْلَ الْقِرَانُ، كَمَا فِي فَتَاوَى قَاضِي حَانْ وَإِنْ كَانَ نَفْلًا، فَكَرَ مَضَانَ أَدَاءً. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال روز و تو وہ دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو وہ فرض ہوگا یا نفل اگر وہ فرض ہوتو وہ خالی ایک بار وہ اداء رمضان ہوگا یا اس کے علاوہ ہو گا اگر وہ اداء رمضان ہو تو وہ اس نیت سے بھی جائز ہے جو غروب شمس سے مقدم
There is disagreement about its validity. One opinion: following is not valid in both forms. Allamah Hamawi distinguished: in niyyah, determination (jism) is required and it exists, while in the second form he intended based on assumption and conjecture; obviously there is no determination, so his following is not valid because jurists have stipulated determination in niyyah. As for the intention of seeking nearness for water becoming used (musta'mal), its time is at the time of scooping. Explanation: When using water for it to become used, if one intends nearness, it becomes used; hence the intention of nearness at the time of use is the criterion. Or by using it with the intention of nearness, e.g., one performs wudu while already in wudu intending wudu. According to the principle of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), water becomes used by only one thing: using it with the intention of performing worship. As for its time in zakat, Al-Hidayah says: Payment of zakat is not valid except with a niyyah concurrent with the payment or concurrent with setting aside the amount due, because zakat is an act of worship, so niyyah is a condition of it. The principle is concurrency, but since payment may be distributed, its presence at the time of setting aside is deemed sufficient for ease, like advancing the niyyah in fasting. They have permitted advancement before payment, but at the time of setting aside. Is it valid with a niyyah delayed after payment? In Sharh al-Majma': If he paid without niyyah, then intended afterward, if the wealth still exists in the poor person's hand, it is valid; otherwise not. As for Sadaqat al-Fitr: it is like zakat in niyyah and channels of expenditure, except the dhimmi: the dhimmi is a channel for Sadaqat al-Fitr but not for zakat. Explanation: Zakat is an act of worship, so niyyah is necessary. The principle is that this niyyah should be attached at the time of payment, but if one makes niyyah at the time of setting aside the wajib amount, considering people's ease, this niyyah is also valid. If one gave wealth to a poor person without niyyah, then when is delayed niyyah valid? If the wealth still exists in the poor person's possession, delayed niyyah is valid; if he has spent it, then delayed niyyah is not valid. As for Sadaqat al-Fitr: its ruling is close to zakat in niyyah and channels, but each has some conditions not found in the other, e.g., the passing of a year is a condition in zakat. Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat in channels and in every case; the meaning in conditions of payment to channels is the stipulation of niyyah and stipulation of ownership. They said except the dhimmi: whether Sadaqat al-Fitr can be given to a dhimmi? The jurists' opinion: if one gives Sadaqat al-Fitr to a dhimmi, it is valid but disliked, while according to Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf, it is not valid. As for fasting: it is either obligatory or supererogatory. If obligatory, it is either Ramadan or other. If it is Ramadan fasting, it is valid with a niyyah advanced from sunset, with a concurrent niyyah (which is the principle), and with a delayed niyyah from the start up to before midday as a concession for the fasting people. If it is other than Ramadan, such as make-up, vow, or expiation, it is valid with a niyyah advanced from sunset to dawn, and valid with a concurrent niyyah at dawn because the principle is concurrency. If supererogatory, it is like Ramadan.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the timing rules for niyyah (intention) in various acts of worship, drawn from Hanafi sources. It opens with a discussion on the requirement of determination (jism) in niyyah for the validity of following an imam in prayer. Allamah Hamawi distinguishes between two forms: one where the follower has definite intention, and another where he intends based on assumption; only the former is valid because scholars have mandated certainty in niyyah.

The passage then addresses the timing of niyyah for making water 'musta'mal' (used). For water to become musta'mal, the intention of seeking nearness (qurbah) must be present at the moment of scooping the water. This is based on Imam Muhammad's principle that water becomes used solely through use with the intention of worship.

Moving to zakat, Al-Hidayah is quoted: niyyah must be concurrent with payment or at the time of setting aside the due amount. Since zakat is a form of worship, niyyah is a condition. The default is temporal concurrency, but because payment may be staggered, scholars allowed the niyyah at the time of setting aside for ease, analogous to advancing niyyah in fasting. Furthermore, if one pays without niyyah, a delayed niyyah is accepted only if the wealth still exists in the recipient's hand; otherwise not.

Sadaqat al-Fitr follows the same rules as zakat regarding niyyah and expenditure channels, except that it may be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen), though it is disliked. Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf prohibit it.

Finally, the passage details the timing of niyyah for fasting. For Ramadan, niyyah can be made from sunset the previous night up to before midday of the same day. For other obligatory fasts (qada', nadhr, kaffarah), the window is from sunset to dawn. For voluntary fasts, the same leniency as Ramadan applies. The underlying principle is that while concurrency is the original requirement, concessions (taysir) are granted for these acts.

Throughout, the passage emphasizes that niyyah is a condition for worship, and the timing rules reflect a balance between the general principle of concurrency and the need for ease in specific circumstances.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; a condition for the validity of worship, requiring determination (jism) and concurrency with the act unless ease allows otherwise.
عزل (azl): Setting aside or separating a specific amount of wealth for the purpose of zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary requirement for zakat niyyah according to Al-Hidayah?
A) Niyyah must be made every time a portion of zakat is distributed.
B) Niyyah can only be made at the time of payment.
C) Niyyah must be concurrent with payment OR concurrent with setting aside the due amount.
D) Niyyah is not required for zakat.

Key Takeaway
Zakat niyyah can be concurrent, at setting aside, or even delayed if wealth is still with the poor.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
7 min
Timing of Niyyah in Sadaqat al-Fitr
Applies zakat niyyah rules to Sadaqat al-Fitr with a special exception for dhimmi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on niyyah for Sadaqat al-Fitr and identify the difference regarding giving to a dhimmi.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-Fitr shares the same niyyah rules as zakat, but giving to a dhimmi is disliked (makruh) and impermissible according to some.

This lesson extends the niyyah rules from zakat to Sadaqat al-Fitr (fitrana). The passage states that Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat in terms of niyyah and channels of expenditure, except for the dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen). While the Hanafi school permits giving Sadaqat al-Fitr to a dhimmi, it is considered makruh (disliked), and Imam Shafi'i together with one narration from Abu Yusuf deem it invalid. Understanding this exceptional case is important for correct fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Establish the rule of analogy
Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat in the requirement of niyyah and the channels of expenditure. Thus, the same timing rules apply (concurrent, setting aside, delayed).
The phrase 'كَالزَّكَاةِ نِيَّةً وَمَصْرِفاً' establishes the analogy.
2
Identify the exception: the dhimmi
The exception is that a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state) may receive Sadaqat al-Fitr, but not zakat. Giving to a dhimmi is disliked (makruh).
3
Note the ikhtilaf on the dhimmi
Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf prohibit giving Sadaqat al-Fitr to a dhimmi altogether. The Hanafi relied-upon position is that it is valid but disliked.
This is an intra/inter-school difference.
4
Apply the niyyah rule
For Sadaqat al-Fitr, niyyah is required in the same manner as zakat. The timing flexibility applies.

لئے استعمال کرتے وقت اگر قربت کا اراد کیا گیا ہے تو وہ مستعمل ہو جائے گا لہذا استعمال کرتے وقت کی نیت قربت معیار ہے۔ أو باستعماله على قصد القربة بان يتوضأ وهو متوضئ ناويا للوضوء و على اصل محمد رحمه الله الماء انما يصير مستعملا بشئ واحد وهو الاستعمال على قصد اقامة القربة. تار تار خانية ج ا ص : (۲۱۳) رَأَمَّا وَقْتُهَا فِي الزَّكَاةِ، فَقَالَ فِي الْهِدَايَةِ لَا يَجُوْزُ أَدَاءُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَّا بِنِيَّةٍ مَقَارِنَةٍ لِلْأَدَاءِ، أَوْ مُقَارِنَةٍ لِعَزْلِ مِقْدَارِ مَا وَجَبَ ؛ لأنَّ الزَّكَاةَ عِبَادَةٌ، فَكَانَتْ مِنْ شَرْطِهَا النِّيَّةُ. وَالْأَصْلُ فِيْهَا الإقتران إلا أن الدَّفَعَ يَتَفَرَّقَ ، فَاكْتُفِي بِوُجُوْدِهَا حَالَةَ الْعَزْلِ تَيْسِيراً كَتَقْدِيمِ النِّيَّةِ فِي الصَّوْمِ إنْتَهى وَقَدْ جَوَّزُوْا التَّقْدِيمَ عَلَى الأَدَاءِ لَكِنْ عِنْدَ الْعَزْلِ وَهَلْ يَجُوزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مُتَاخِرَةِ عَنِ الْأَدَاءِ. فَقَالَ فِي شَرْحِ الْمَجْمَعِ : لَوْدَفَعَهَا بِلَا نِيَّةٍ، ثُمَّ نَوَى بَعْدَهُ، فَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَالُ قَائِمًا فِي يَدِ الْفَقِيْرِ جَازَ وَإِلَّا فَلَا. إنْتَهى وَأَمَّا صَدَقَةُ الْفِطْرِ : فَكَالزَّكَاةِ نِيَّةٌ وَمَصْرِفاً، فالو إلا اللهى، فَإِنَّهُ مَصْرَت لِلْفِطْرِدُونَ الزَّكَاةِ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال زکوۃ میں اس کا وقت تو ہدایہ میں کہا ہے کہ اداء ز کوۃ جائز نہیں بغیر اس نیت کے جو ادا ت ملی ہوئی ہو یا مقدار واجب کو علیحدہ کرنے سے ملی ہوئی ہو اس لئے کہ زکوۃ ایک عبادت ہے تو نیت اس کے لئے شرط ہے جس میں اصل اقتران ہے لیکن مال دینا بار بار ہوتا ہے اس لئے آسانی کے لئے علیحدہ کرنے کے وقت اس کے پائے جانے پر اکتفا کر لیا گیا جیسے روزہ میں نیت کو مقدم کر دینا، ہدایہ کی بات پوری ہوگئی اور فقہا ء نے ادا پر مقدم کرنے کو جائز فرمایا ہے لیکن مال علیحدہ کرتے وقت اور کیا وہ اس نیت سے بھی جائز ہے جو اداء سے بھی مئوخر ہو تو شرح مجمع میں ہے کہ اگر وہ بغیر نیت کے دیدی پھر اس کے بعد نیت کی تو اگر مال فقیر کے قبضہ میں موجود ہو تو جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں شرح مجمع کا کلام پورا ہوا ر ہا صدقہ فطر تو وہ نیت اور مصرف کے اعتبار سے زکوۃ کے مانند ہے فقہاء یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بجز ذمی کے کہ وہ صدقہ فطر کا مصرف ہے زکوۃ کا نہیں۔ تشریح: زکوۃ ایک عبادت ہے لہذا اس کے معتبر ہوگی۔ و اما شرط ادائها فنية مقارنة للاداء او الفرضما وجب هكذا في الكنز (بند برج اص: ۷۰) اور اگر بلانیت زکوۃ فقیر کو مال دیدیا تو ایسی صورت میں کب تک زکوة کی نیت معتبر ہوئی تو اگر فقیر کے قبضہ میں ال موجود ہے بے تو زکوۃ کے اندر نیت متاخرہ معتبر ہوگی اور اگر اس نے مال خرچ کر دیا ہو تو پھر نیت متاخر معبر نہ ہوگی۔ و اذا دفع الى الفقير بلانية ثم نواه عن الزكاة فان كان المال قائما في يد الفقير اجزاء والا فلا هندیه ج ۱، ص ۱۷۱) و أما صدقة الفطر : نیت اور مصرف کے اعتبار سے صدقہ فطر کا حکم زکوۃ کے قریب قریب ہے ورنہ ہر ایک کے لئے چند ایسی شرائط ہیں جو دوسرے کے لئے ہیں جیسا کہ زکوۃ کے اندر حولان حول وغیرہ شرط ہے۔ و صدقۃ الفطر كالزكاة في المصارف و في كل حال و تحته في رد المحتار بل المراد في احوال الدفع الى المصارف من اشتراط النية واشتراط التمليك فلا الا حاجة كما في البدائع (شامی زکریا ج ۳ ص: ۳۲۵) قالوا الا الذمی : ذمی یعنی غیر مسلم کو صدقہ فطر دیا جا سکتا ہے یا نہیں اس میں فقہاء کی رائے یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے صدقہ فطر زمی کو دید یا تو جائز تو ہو جائے گا لیکن مکروہ ہوگا جبکہ امام شافعی اور امام ابی یوسف کی ایک روایت کے مطابقی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ولو اعطى ذميا جاز و فى الخانية جاز و يكره وعند الشافعي واحدى الروايتين عن ابي يوسف لايجوز ( تار تار خانیه ج ۲، ص: ۴۲۴) وَأَمَا الصَّوْمُ فَلَا يَخْلُوْا إِمَّا أَيَّكُوْنَ فَرْضاً أَوْ نَفْلًا، فَإِنْ كَانَ فَرْضاً، فَلَايَخْلُوْا إِمَّا أَيَّكُونَ أَدَاءَ رَمَضَانَ أَوْ غَيْرَهُ. فَإِنْ كَانَ أَدَاءَ رَمَضَانَ جَازَ بِنِيَّةٍ مُتَقَدِّمَةٍ مِنْ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَبِمُقَارِنَةٍ، وَهُوَ الْأَصْلُ، وَبِمُتَأَخْرَةِ عَنِ الشَّرُوْعِ إِلَى مَاقَبْلَ نَصْفِ النَّهَارِ الشَّرِي تَيْسِيراً عَلَى الصَّائِمِينَ. وَإِنْ كَانَ غَيْرِ أَدَاءِ رَمَضَانَ مِنْ قَضَاءِ، أَوْ نَذْرٍ، أَوْ كَفَّارَةٍ، فَيَجُوْزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مُتَقَدِّمَةٍ مِنْ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ إِلى طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ، وَيَجُوْزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مَقَارِنَةٍ لِطُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ لأنَّ الْأَصْلَ الْقِرَانُ، كَمَا فِي فَتَاوَى قَاضِي حَانْ وَإِنْ كَانَ نَفْلًا، فَكَرَ مَضَانَ أَدَاءً. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال روز و تو وہ دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو وہ فرض ہوگا یا نفل اگر وہ فرض ہوتو وہ خالی ایک بار وہ اداء رمضان ہوگا یا اس کے علاوہ ہو گا اگر وہ اداء رمضان ہو تو وہ اس نیت سے بھی جائز ہے جو غروب شمس سے مقدم
There is disagreement about its validity. One opinion: following is not valid in both forms. Allamah Hamawi distinguished: in niyyah, determination (jism) is required and it exists, while in the second form he intended based on assumption and conjecture; obviously there is no determination, so his following is not valid because jurists have stipulated determination in niyyah. As for the intention of seeking nearness for water becoming used (musta'mal), its time is at the time of scooping. Explanation: When using water for it to become used, if one intends nearness, it becomes used; hence the intention of nearness at the time of use is the criterion. Or by using it with the intention of nearness, e.g., one performs wudu while already in wudu intending wudu. According to the principle of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), water becomes used by only one thing: using it with the intention of performing worship. As for its time in zakat, Al-Hidayah says: Payment of zakat is not valid except with a niyyah concurrent with the payment or concurrent with setting aside the amount due, because zakat is an act of worship, so niyyah is a condition of it. The principle is concurrency, but since payment may be distributed, its presence at the time of setting aside is deemed sufficient for ease, like advancing the niyyah in fasting. They have permitted advancement before payment, but at the time of setting aside. Is it valid with a niyyah delayed after payment? In Sharh al-Majma': If he paid without niyyah, then intended afterward, if the wealth still exists in the poor person's hand, it is valid; otherwise not. As for Sadaqat al-Fitr: it is like zakat in niyyah and channels of expenditure, except the dhimmi: the dhimmi is a channel for Sadaqat al-Fitr but not for zakat. Explanation: Zakat is an act of worship, so niyyah is necessary. The principle is that this niyyah should be attached at the time of payment, but if one makes niyyah at the time of setting aside the wajib amount, considering people's ease, this niyyah is also valid. If one gave wealth to a poor person without niyyah, then when is delayed niyyah valid? If the wealth still exists in the poor person's possession, delayed niyyah is valid; if he has spent it, then delayed niyyah is not valid. As for Sadaqat al-Fitr: its ruling is close to zakat in niyyah and channels, but each has some conditions not found in the other, e.g., the passing of a year is a condition in zakat. Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat in channels and in every case; the meaning in conditions of payment to channels is the stipulation of niyyah and stipulation of ownership. They said except the dhimmi: whether Sadaqat al-Fitr can be given to a dhimmi? The jurists' opinion: if one gives Sadaqat al-Fitr to a dhimmi, it is valid but disliked, while according to Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf, it is not valid. As for fasting: it is either obligatory or supererogatory. If obligatory, it is either Ramadan or other. If it is Ramadan fasting, it is valid with a niyyah advanced from sunset, with a concurrent niyyah (which is the principle), and with a delayed niyyah from the start up to before midday as a concession for the fasting people. If it is other than Ramadan, such as make-up, vow, or expiation, it is valid with a niyyah advanced from sunset to dawn, and valid with a concurrent niyyah at dawn because the principle is concurrency. If supererogatory, it is like Ramadan.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the timing rules for niyyah (intention) in various acts of worship, drawn from Hanafi sources. It opens with a discussion on the requirement of determination (jism) in niyyah for the validity of following an imam in prayer. Allamah Hamawi distinguishes between two forms: one where the follower has definite intention, and another where he intends based on assumption; only the former is valid because scholars have mandated certainty in niyyah.

The passage then addresses the timing of niyyah for making water 'musta'mal' (used). For water to become musta'mal, the intention of seeking nearness (qurbah) must be present at the moment of scooping the water. This is based on Imam Muhammad's principle that water becomes used solely through use with the intention of worship.

Moving to zakat, Al-Hidayah is quoted: niyyah must be concurrent with payment or at the time of setting aside the due amount. Since zakat is a form of worship, niyyah is a condition. The default is temporal concurrency, but because payment may be staggered, scholars allowed the niyyah at the time of setting aside for ease, analogous to advancing niyyah in fasting. Furthermore, if one pays without niyyah, a delayed niyyah is accepted only if the wealth still exists in the recipient's hand; otherwise not.

Sadaqat al-Fitr follows the same rules as zakat regarding niyyah and expenditure channels, except that it may be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen), though it is disliked. Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf prohibit it.

Finally, the passage details the timing of niyyah for fasting. For Ramadan, niyyah can be made from sunset the previous night up to before midday of the same day. For other obligatory fasts (qada', nadhr, kaffarah), the window is from sunset to dawn. For voluntary fasts, the same leniency as Ramadan applies. The underlying principle is that while concurrency is the original requirement, concessions (taysir) are granted for these acts.

Throughout, the passage emphasizes that niyyah is a condition for worship, and the timing rules reflect a balance between the general principle of concurrency and the need for ease in specific circumstances.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; a condition for the validity of worship, requiring determination (jism) and concurrency with the act unless ease allows otherwise.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on giving Sadaqat al-Fitr to a dhimmi?
A) Impermissible (haram).
B) Valid but disliked (makruh).
C) Valid and recommended.
D) Invalid (batil).

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-Fitr follows zakat's niyyah rules, but giving to a dhimmi is valid though disliked.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Timing of Niyyah in Fasting
Explains timing of niyyah for different types of fasts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible times for niyyah in various types of fasting (Ramadan, qada', nadhr, kaffarah, supererogatory) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ramadan fast niyyah can be made from sunset until before midday; other obligatory fasts require niyyah before dawn; supererogatory fasts are like Ramadan.

This lesson details the timing rules for niyyah in fasting, distinguishing between types: Ramadan (obligatory as performance), other obligatory (qada', vow, expiation), and supererogatory. The default principle is concurrency at dawn, but concessions are given. For Ramadan, niyyah can be advanced from the previous sunset and even delayed up to before midday. For other obligatory fasts, the window is from sunset to dawn. Supererogatory fasts follow the same leniency as Ramadan. These rules reflect the Hanafi commitment to ease (taysir) in worship.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the fast
Determine whether the fast is obligatory (فرض) or supererogatory (نفل). If obligatory, decide if it is Ramadan (أداء رمضان) or other (qada', nadhr, kaffarah).
2
Apply the rule for Ramadan
Ramadan fast is valid with niyyah from sunset (previous day) to pre-midday of the current day. This is a concession (تيسيراً).
The phrase 'نصف النهار الشري' means the middle of the day (zawal).
3
Apply the rule for other obligatory fasts
For qada', vow, or expiation, niyyah must be made from sunset to dawn (fajr). It can be advanced or concurrent at dawn. The default is concurrency.
No concession for delayed niyyah after dawn for these types.
4
Apply the rule for supererogatory fasts
Supererogatory fasts are like Ramadan: niyyah can be made from sunset to pre-midday.
This allows greater flexibility for voluntary fasts.

بِنِيَّةٍ مَقَارِنَةٍ لِلْأَدَاءِ، أَوْ مُقَارِنَةٍ لِعَزْلِ مِقْدَارِ مَا وَجَبَ ؛ لأنَّ الزَّكَاةَ عِبَادَةٌ، فَكَانَتْ مِنْ شَرْطِهَا النِّيَّةُ. وَالْأَصْلُ فِيْهَا الإقتران إلا أن الدَّفَعَ يَتَفَرَّقَ ، فَاكْتُفِي بِوُجُوْدِهَا حَالَةَ الْعَزْلِ تَيْسِيراً كَتَقْدِيمِ النِّيَّةِ فِي الصَّوْمِ إنْتَهى وَقَدْ جَوَّزُوْا التَّقْدِيمَ عَلَى الأَدَاءِ لَكِنْ عِنْدَ الْعَزْلِ وَهَلْ يَجُوزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مُتَاخِرَةِ عَنِ الْأَدَاءِ. فَقَالَ فِي شَرْحِ الْمَجْمَعِ : لَوْدَفَعَهَا بِلَا نِيَّةٍ، ثُمَّ نَوَى بَعْدَهُ، فَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَالُ قَائِمًا فِي يَدِ الْفَقِيْرِ جَازَ وَإِلَّا فَلَا. إنْتَهى وَأَمَّا صَدَقَةُ الْفِطْرِ : فَكَالزَّكَاةِ نِيَّةٌ وَمَصْرِفاً، فالو إلا اللهى، فَإِنَّهُ مَصْرَت لِلْفِطْرِدُونَ الزَّكَاةِ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال زکوۃ میں اس کا وقت تو ہدایہ میں کہا ہے کہ اداء ز کوۃ جائز نہیں بغیر اس نیت کے جو ادا ت ملی ہوئی ہو یا مقدار واجب کو علیحدہ کرنے سے ملی ہوئی ہو اس لئے کہ زکوۃ ایک عبادت ہے تو نیت اس کے لئے شرط ہے جس میں اصل اقتران ہے لیکن مال دینا بار بار ہوتا علیحدہ کرتے وقت اور کیا وہ اس نیت سے بھی جائز ہے جو اداء سے بھی مئوخر ہو تو شرح مجمع میں ہے کہ اگر وہ بغیر نیت کے دیدی پھر اس کے بعد نیت کی تو اگر مال فقیر کے قبضہ میں موجود ہو تو جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں اندر نیت کا ہونا ضروری ہے اصل تو یہی ہے کہ یہ نیت ادا ئیگلی کے وقت جڑی ہوئی ہونی چاہئے لیکن اگر کسی نے زکوۃ کی واجب مقدار کو علیحدہ کرتے وقت نیت کر لی تو لوگوں کی آسانی کو مد نظر رکھتے ہوئے یہ نیت بھی معتبر ہوگی۔ و اما شرط ادائها فنية مقارنة للاداء او الفرضما وجب هكذا في الكنز (بند برج اص: ۷۰) اور اگر بلانیت زکوۃ فقیر کو مال دیدیا تو ایسی صورت میں کب تک زکوة کی نیت معتبر ہوئی تو اگر فقیر کے قبضہ میں ال موجود ہے بے تو زکوۃ کے اندر نیت متاخرہ معتبر ہوگی اور اگر اس نے مال خرچ کر دیا ہو تو پھر نیت متاخر معبر نہ ہوگی۔ و اذا دفع الى الفقير بلانية ثم نواه عن الزكاة فان كان المال قائما في يد الفقير اجزاء والا فلا هندیه ج ۱، ص ۱۷۱) و أما صدقة الفطر : نیت اور مصرف کے اعتبار سے صدقہ فطر کا حکم زکوۃ کے قریب قریب ہے ورنہ ہر ایک کے لئے چند ایسی شرائط ہیں جو دوسرے کے لئے ہیں جیسا کہ زکوۃ کے اندر حولان حول وغیرہ شرط ہے۔ و صدقۃ الفطر كالزكاة في المصارف و في كل حال و تحته في رد المحتار بل المراد في احوال الدفع الى المصارف من اشتراط النية واشتراط التمليك فلا الا حاجة كما في البدائع (شامی زکریا ج ۳ ص: ۳۲۵) قالوا الا الذمی : ذمی یعنی غیر مسلم کو صدقہ فطر دیا جا سکتا ہے یا نہیں اس میں فقہاء کی رائے یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے صدقہ فطر زمی کو دید یا تو جائز تو ہو جائے گا لیکن مکروہ ہوگا جبکہ امام شافعی اور امام ابی یوسف کی ایک روایت کے مطابقی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ولو اعطى ذميا جاز و فى الخانية جاز و يكره وعند الشافعي واحدى الروايتين عن ابي يوسف لايجوز ( تار تار خانیه ج ۲، ص: ۴۲۴) وَأَمَا الصَّوْمُ فَلَا يَخْلُوْا إِمَّا أَيَّكُوْنَ فَرْضاً أَوْ نَفْلًا، فَإِنْ كَانَ فَرْضاً، فَلَايَخْلُوْا إِمَّا أَيَّكُونَ أَدَاءَ رَمَضَانَ أَوْ غَيْرَهُ. فَإِنْ كَانَ أَدَاءَ رَمَضَانَ جَازَ بِنِيَّةٍ مُتَقَدِّمَةٍ مِنْ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَبِمُقَارِنَةٍ، وَهُوَ الْأَصْلُ، وَبِمُتَأَخْرَةِ عَنِ الشَّرُوْعِ إِلَى مَاقَبْلَ نَصْفِ النَّهَارِ الشَّرِي تَيْسِيراً عَلَى الصَّائِمِينَ. وَإِنْ كَانَ غَيْرِ أَدَاءِ رَمَضَانَ مِنْ قَضَاءِ، أَوْ نَذْرٍ، أَوْ كَفَّارَةٍ، فَيَجُوْزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مُتَقَدِّمَةٍ مِنْ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ إِلى طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ، وَيَجُوْزُ بِنِيَّةٍ مَقَارِنَةٍ لِطُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ لأنَّ الْأَصْلَ الْقِرَانُ، كَمَا فِي فَتَاوَى قَاضِي حَانْ وَإِنْ كَانَ نَفْلًا، فَكَرَ مَضَانَ أَدَاءً. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال روز و تو وہ دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو وہ فرض ہوگا یا نفل اگر وہ فرض ہوتو وہ خالی ایک بار وہ اداء رمضان ہوگا یا اس کے علاوہ ہو گا اگر وہ اداء رمضان ہو تو وہ اس نیت سے بھی جائز ہے جو غروب شمس سے مقدم
There is disagreement about its validity. One opinion: following is not valid in both forms. Allamah Hamawi distinguished: in niyyah, determination (jism) is required and it exists, while in the second form he intended based on assumption and conjecture; obviously there is no determination, so his following is not valid because jurists have stipulated determination in niyyah. As for the intention of seeking nearness for water becoming used (musta'mal), its time is at the time of scooping. Explanation: When using water for it to become used, if one intends nearness, it becomes used; hence the intention of nearness at the time of use is the criterion. Or by using it with the intention of nearness, e.g., one performs wudu while already in wudu intending wudu. According to the principle of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), water becomes used by only one thing: using it with the intention of performing worship. As for its time in zakat, Al-Hidayah says: Payment of zakat is not valid except with a niyyah concurrent with the payment or concurrent with setting aside the amount due, because zakat is an act of worship, so niyyah is a condition of it. The principle is concurrency, but since payment may be distributed, its presence at the time of setting aside is deemed sufficient for ease, like advancing the niyyah in fasting. They have permitted advancement before payment, but at the time of setting aside. Is it valid with a niyyah delayed after payment? In Sharh al-Majma': If he paid without niyyah, then intended afterward, if the wealth still exists in the poor person's hand, it is valid; otherwise not. As for Sadaqat al-Fitr: it is like zakat in niyyah and channels of expenditure, except the dhimmi: the dhimmi is a channel for Sadaqat al-Fitr but not for zakat. Explanation: Zakat is an act of worship, so niyyah is necessary. The principle is that this niyyah should be attached at the time of payment, but if one makes niyyah at the time of setting aside the wajib amount, considering people's ease, this niyyah is also valid. If one gave wealth to a poor person without niyyah, then when is delayed niyyah valid? If the wealth still exists in the poor person's possession, delayed niyyah is valid; if he has spent it, then delayed niyyah is not valid. As for Sadaqat al-Fitr: its ruling is close to zakat in niyyah and channels, but each has some conditions not found in the other, e.g., the passing of a year is a condition in zakat. Sadaqat al-Fitr is like zakat in channels and in every case; the meaning in conditions of payment to channels is the stipulation of niyyah and stipulation of ownership. They said except the dhimmi: whether Sadaqat al-Fitr can be given to a dhimmi? The jurists' opinion: if one gives Sadaqat al-Fitr to a dhimmi, it is valid but disliked, while according to Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf, it is not valid. As for fasting: it is either obligatory or supererogatory. If obligatory, it is either Ramadan or other. If it is Ramadan fasting, it is valid with a niyyah advanced from sunset, with a concurrent niyyah (which is the principle), and with a delayed niyyah from the start up to before midday as a concession for the fasting people. If it is other than Ramadan, such as make-up, vow, or expiation, it is valid with a niyyah advanced from sunset to dawn, and valid with a concurrent niyyah at dawn because the principle is concurrency. If supererogatory, it is like Ramadan.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the timing rules for niyyah (intention) in various acts of worship, drawn from Hanafi sources. It opens with a discussion on the requirement of determination (jism) in niyyah for the validity of following an imam in prayer. Allamah Hamawi distinguishes between two forms: one where the follower has definite intention, and another where he intends based on assumption; only the former is valid because scholars have mandated certainty in niyyah.

The passage then addresses the timing of niyyah for making water 'musta'mal' (used). For water to become musta'mal, the intention of seeking nearness (qurbah) must be present at the moment of scooping the water. This is based on Imam Muhammad's principle that water becomes used solely through use with the intention of worship.

Moving to zakat, Al-Hidayah is quoted: niyyah must be concurrent with payment or at the time of setting aside the due amount. Since zakat is a form of worship, niyyah is a condition. The default is temporal concurrency, but because payment may be staggered, scholars allowed the niyyah at the time of setting aside for ease, analogous to advancing niyyah in fasting. Furthermore, if one pays without niyyah, a delayed niyyah is accepted only if the wealth still exists in the recipient's hand; otherwise not.

Sadaqat al-Fitr follows the same rules as zakat regarding niyyah and expenditure channels, except that it may be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen), though it is disliked. Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Abu Yusuf prohibit it.

Finally, the passage details the timing of niyyah for fasting. For Ramadan, niyyah can be made from sunset the previous night up to before midday of the same day. For other obligatory fasts (qada', nadhr, kaffarah), the window is from sunset to dawn. For voluntary fasts, the same leniency as Ramadan applies. The underlying principle is that while concurrency is the original requirement, concessions (taysir) are granted for these acts.

Throughout, the passage emphasizes that niyyah is a condition for worship, and the timing rules reflect a balance between the general principle of concurrency and the need for ease in specific circumstances.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; a condition for the validity of worship, requiring determination (jism) and concurrency with the act unless ease allows otherwise.
صوم (sawm): Fasting; an act of worship requiring niyyah with specific timing rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Until what time can a niyyah be made for a Ramadan fast?
A) Only until dawn.
B) Only until sunrise.
C) Up to before midday (zawal).
D) Any time during the day.

Key Takeaway
Ramadan fasting allows niyyah up to before midday; other obligatory fasts require niyyah before dawn.
