Intention Times for Fasts and the Maxim of Hardship
Ruling on intention timing for fasts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir' to determine the valid time of intention for different types of fasts and identify which fasts require tabyit.

Core Idea
Hardship permits postponing intention for Ramadan and nafl fasts until noon, but qada, kaffarah, and absolute nazr require intention from the night.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition details when intention (niyyah) must be made for different categories of fasts. The key principle is that to avoid undue hardship, intention for fasts that are either fixed (Ramadan) or light (nafl) may be delayed until before noon. However, for fasts that are obligatory repayments or expiations, a more precise intention from the night (tabyit) is required. This distinction is grounded in the major legal maxim 'hardship attracts facility'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of fast
Distinguish between Ramadan, nafl, fixed nazr, qada, kaffarah, and absolute nazr. Each has different rules for intention timing.
Fixed nazr (e.g., vowing to fast on a specific day) is treated like Ramadan; absolute nazr (e.g., vowing to fast without specifying a day) is treated like qada.
2
Apply the maxim 'al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir'
For fasts that are repeated daily (Ramadan) or are voluntary (nafl), requiring intention from the night every day would cause hardship. Therefore, intention is valid if made from dawn until before noon. This is the facility granted by the maxim.
This includes fixed nazr, as it is determined like Ramadan.
3
Identify the exception to the maxim
For fasts that are obligations of a certain nature (qada, kaffarah, absolute nazr), the same hardship argument does not apply because the obligation is more exacting. These fasts require intention to be made from the night (tabyit) and must specify the type of fast.
The exception is supported by analogy to prayer, where obligatory acts require intention before commencement.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi position is as stated in the sources: tabyit is required only for qada, kaffarah, and absolute nazr; for Ramadan, fixed nazr, and nafl, intention until noon suffices.
This is consistently found in later authoritative texts like al-Hindiyya and Fatawa Qadikhan.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Given a question from a layperson, identify the fast type and determine whether intention can be made after dawn. If the fast is qada, rule that intention must have been made at night; otherwise, it is valid until noon.
Always ask if the fast is an obligatory make-up or expiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہوا اور اسی نیت سے کی جو ( طلوع صبح صادق سے ) ملی ہوئی ہو اور یہی اصل ہے اور روزہ داروں کی سہولت کے لئے ائی لیت سے بھی درست ہے جو شروع سے شرعی دن کے نصف سے پہلے تک مؤخر ہو اور اگر وہ ادا در مضان کے علاوہ ی اٹھایا نذر یا کفارہ کا روزہ ہوتو وہ اس نیت سے جائز ہے جو غروب شمس سے پہلے سے طلوع فجر تک ہو اور اس نیت سے بھی جائز ہے جو طلوع فجر سے ملی ہوئی ہو اس لئے کہ اصل ملی ہوئی ہونا ہی ہے، فتاوی قاضیخان میں ایسا ہی ہے اور اگر دو قل ہو تو ایسا ہی ہے جیسے اداء رمضان ہے ۔ تشریح: روزہ ہیں نیت کے وقت کے بارے میں تحصیل ۔ اس سلسلہ میں قدرے تفصیل اس طرح ہے کہ رمضان کا اداروزہ اور نفل میں تو پیشگی نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ رمضان من اللہ متعین ہے اور نفل کے بارے میں حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے ثابت ہے کہ جس روز آپ کے پاس کھانے کو کچھ نہ ہوتا تھا تو آپ اس روز روزہ کی نیت فرما لیتے تھے البتہ نذر غیر معین قضاء اور کفارہ میں حویت نیست شرط ہے یعنی شورہ کبری سے پہلے نیت کر لینی چاہئے۔
جاز صوم رمضان والنذر المعين والنفل بنية ذلك اليوم او بنية مطلق الصوم أو بنية لنفل من الليل الى ماقبل نصف النهار (هندیه ج ۱ ص: ۱۹۵) وشرط القضاء والكفارات ان يبيت و يعين كذا فى الثقاية و كذا النذر المطلق هكذا في السراج الوهاج (بندي ج ١ ص : ١٩٢)
And intention made at dawn (true dawn) is valid and this is the principle. For the ease of fasting persons, intention made from the beginning up to before half of the shar'i day is also valid. If it is a fast other than Ramadan, such as a specific nazr or kaffarah, it is valid with intention made from before sunset to dawn, and also with intention made at dawn, because the principle is intention at dawn. In Fatawa Qadikhan, it is like this. And if it is a makeup fast, it is like the Ramadan fast. Explanation: Regarding the times of intention for fasts, detail is as follows: For Ramadan fast and nafl fast, prior intention is not required because Ramadan is determined by Allah, and for nafl it is proven from the Prophet (SAW) that when he had nothing to eat, he would intend fasting that day. However, for non-specific nazr, qada, and kaffarah, intention is necessary, meaning intention must be made before the beginning of the legal day (i.e., before dawn with certainty). The fast of Ramadan, fixed nazr, and nafl are valid with intention of that day or absolute intention to fast or intention of nafl from night to before midday (Hindiyya, vol. 1, p. 195). For qada and kaffarah, it is conditional to intend from the night and to specify, as in al-Thaqafiyya, similarly for absolute nazr, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj (Bandi vol. 1, p. 192).
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the requirement of intention for fasting. It distinguishes between different types of fasts based on ease and certainty. For Ramadan and voluntary fasts, intention can be made later in the day, before noon, due to the hardship of requiring a nightly intention for every day. This is derived from the practice of the Prophet (SAW). For obligatory fasts like qada and kaffarah, a more precise intention is required: it must be made at night and specify the type of fast. The passage cites standard Hanafi references: Hindiyya, Thaqafiyya, and Siraj al-Wahhaj. The underlying legal maxim is that intention is a condition for the validity of acts of worship, but its timing varies with the type of worship to avoid undue hardship.

Key Terms
نیة (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship
تبییت (tabyit): Making intention at night, specifically for obligatory fasts
شرعي دن (shar'i yawm): The legal day in Islamic law, from true dawn (fajr sadiq) to sunset

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following fasts requires intention to be made at night (tabyit)?
A) Ramadan fast
B) Voluntary (nafl) fast
C) Qada (makeup) fast
D) Fixed nazr fast

Key Takeaway
The timing of intention for fasting depends on the type of fast: facility (noon deadline) for Ramadan, fixed nazr, and nafl; strictness (tabyit) for qada, kaffarah, and absolute nazr.

Combining Intentions: When a New Intention Does Not Invalidate the Current Worship
Ruling on the validity of intending another worship while already engaged in one

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qa'ida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to determine the validity of intending a different type of worship while engaged in another, and identify the exception for same-type intentions.

Core Idea
Intending a different genus of worship (e.g., fasting during prayer) is valid and does not invalidate the first; only same-genus intentions conflict.

In Hanafi jurisprudence, the principle 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions) governs the validity of intentions. However, that principle is qualified by the distinction between types (jins) of worship. This lesson examines the ruling when a person intends another worship while in the midst of one—a common scenario for the mufti dealing with unintended intentions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Acts of Worship
First, determine the two acts involved: the act currently being performed and the one intended. For example, prayer and fasting.
The acts must be from the category of ibadat (worship).
2
Determine Their Genus (Jins)
Classify each act by its genus: prayer, fasting, Hajj, etc. If they are of the same genus, the new intention is invalid unless the first act is properly terminated. If different, the intention is valid.
For instance, all prayers (fard, nafl) belong to the same jins.
3
Apply the Rule
If the jins differ, the new intention is valid and does not affect the ongoing act. If the jins match, the new intention is invalid (unless the first act is ended), but the ongoing act remains valid.
The ongoing act is not invalidated even if the new intention is invalid.
4
Recognize the Underlying Qa'ida and Istithna'
The rule derives from 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha', but the istithna' (exception) for same jins prevents conflict. Understand how the major maxim is restricted.
The exception is based on the need for exclusive intention per act of the same genus.
5
Practice with New Furu'
Apply the rule to other cases like combining tawaf with sa'i, or salah with sajdat al-tilawah. The mufti must quickly identify jins.
Different jins: prayer and fasting, prayer and Umrah, tawaf and sajdat al-tilawah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَلْ تَصِحُ لِيا عِبَادَةِ، وَهُوَ فِى عِبَادَةٍ أخرى، قَالَ فِى الفنيةِ : نَوَى فِي صَلَاةٍ مكتوبة أوْ نَافِلَة الصَّوْم ، تَصِحُ بَيْتَهُ، وَلَا تَفْسَا صَلَاتُهُ، انتهى.
:ترجمه: کیا اس حال میں کسی عبادت کی نیت درست ہے جبکہ وہ کسی دوسری عبادت میں مشغول ہوانہ میں ہے کہ فرض یا نفل نماز میں کسی نے روزہ کی نیت کر لی تو اس کی نیت درست ہے اور اس کی نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی قنیہ کا کلام مکمل ہوا۔ تشریح: ایک عبادت کے درمیان دوسری عبادت کی نیت ہو سکتی ہے یا نہیں اس سلسلہ میں ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ ایک عبادت میں اسی جنس کی عبادت کی نیت صحیح نہ ہو گی جب تک کہ پہلی عبادت کے لئے کوئی قاطع اور مالی محل پایا جائے اور اگر دوسری جنس کی عبادت کی نیت کی تو نیت میں ہو جائے گی اور عبادت فاسد نہ ہوگی۔
Is it valid to intend a worship while in another worship? Al-Funiyya said: One intended in an obligatory or voluntary prayer to fast, his intention is valid and his prayer is not invalidated, end. Translation: Is the intention for one worship valid while engaged in another? For example, in an obligatory or voluntary prayer, one intends to fast — his intention is valid and his prayer does not become invalid. The statement of Quniyya is complete. Explanation: Regarding whether one can intend another worship during a worship, the rule is: Intending a worship of the same type is not valid unless there is something to terminate the first worship and a valid place for it. But if a different type of worship is intended, the intention is valid and the first worship is not invalidated.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific issue in the chapter on intention: can one intend a different act of worship while already performing another? The answer is yes, if the second is of a different genus (jins). For example, if while praying an obligatory prayer, one intends to start a fast, that intention is valid and does not ruin the prayer. The rule is based on the principle that actions are judged by intentions, but different types of worship do not conflict. However, intending another prayer during a prayer would invalidate the first unless it is terminated properly.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Type or genus of worship (e.g., prayer, fasting, Hajj).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If during a voluntary prayer, one intends to perform Umrah, what is the ruling on the prayer?
A) The prayer is invalidated
B) The intention for Umrah is invalid
C) The prayer remains valid and the intention for Umrah is valid
D) Both become invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intending a different genus of worship during an act is valid and does not invalidate the ongoing act; only same-genus intentions require termination of the first.

Ruling on Intention for Another Worship While Engaged in One
Ruling on intention for one worship while in another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that intending a worship of a different genre during another worship is valid and does not invalidate the current worship.

Core Idea
Intention for a different genre of worship during salah is valid; same genre requires a disconnect.

This passage from Al-Qunyah presents a key ruling on the validity of making an intention for one act of worship while already engaged in another. The text gives a specific case and then a general principle that distinguishes between same and different genres. This principle is a valuable tool for a mufti when assessing such scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific case
Read the quote from Al-Qunyah: what is the scenario described?
A person in salah (fard or nafl) intends to fast.
2
Extract the ruling
What is the hukm on the intention and the original salah?
The intention is valid, and the salah does not become invalid.
3
Derive the general principle
From the commentary, what rule is extracted about the genre of the intended worship?
Same genre not valid unless disconnector; different genre valid.
4
Apply the principle
Consider a related scenario: intending zuhr salah while in fajr. Is it valid?
Same genre (salah) – not valid unless there is a disconnector or the first salah is terminable.
5
Note the source hierarchy
Al-Qunyah is a well-known Hanafi text. What is its authority level?
It is from the later authoritative works, reliable for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَلْ تَصِحُ نِيَّةُ عِبَادَةٍ وَهُوَ فِي عِبَادَةٍ أُخْرَى، قَالَ فِي القُنْيَةِ: نَوَى فِي صَلَاةٍ مَكْتُوبَةٍ أَوْ نَافِلَةٍ الصَّوْمَ، تَصِحُ نِيَّتُهُ، وَلَا تَفْسُدُ صَلَاتُهُ، انتهى.

ترجمه: کیا اس حال میں کسی عبادت کی نیت درست ہے جبکہ وہ کسی دوسری عبادت میں مشغول ہو۔ قنیہ میں ہے کہ فرض یا نفل نماز میں کسی نے روزہ کی نیت کر لی تو اس کی نیت درست ہے اور اس کی نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔

قنیہ کا کلام مکمل ہوا۔ تشریح: ایک عبادت کے درمیان دوسری عبادت کی نیت ہو سکتی ہے یا نہیں اس سلسلہ میں ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ ایک عبادت میں اسی جنس کی عبادت کی نیت صحیح نہ ہو گی جب تک کہ پہلی عبادت کے لئے کوئی قاطع اور مالی محل پایا جائے اور اگر دوسری جنس کی عبادت کی نیت کی تو نیت میں ہو جائے گی اور عبادت فاسد نہ ہوگی۔
Is the intention of an act of worship valid while one is in another act of worship? He said in Al-Qunyah: He intended in an obligatory or supererogatory prayer the fast – his intention is valid, and his prayer does not become invalid. End. Translation: Whether the intention of an act of worship is correct while he is engaged in another act of worship. In Al-Qunyah it is stated: If someone in an obligatory or supererogatory prayer intended fasting, his intention is valid and his prayer does not become invalid. The speech of Al-Qunyah is complete. Commentary: The rule in this matter is that intending an act of worship of the same type during another worship is not valid unless there is a disconnector or a place of impermissibility for the first worship; but if he intends a different type, his intention is valid and the worship does not become invalid.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling on validity of intention for one worship while engaged in another. The text presents a rule from Al-Qunyah: If someone in prayer (obligatory or supererogatory) makes the intention for fasting, that intention is valid and the prayer remains valid. The commentator then extracts the general principle: If the intended worship is of the same genre as the current one (e.g., intending another prayer while in prayer), it is not valid unless there is a clear disconnect or the first worship is already terminable. If it is a different genre (e.g., intending fast while in prayer), it is valid and does not ruin the current worship. This is based on the fact that the current worship is not nullified by a mere different intention; rather, continuity of intention is not required for every moment.

Key Terms
نیة (niyyah): The intention of the heart to perform a specific act of worship
قنیہ (Al-Qunyah): A Hanafi fiqh reference work by Imam al-Qunyah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone is performing the fajr prayer and in the middle of it intends to observe a nafl fast, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer becomes invalid because of the new intention.
B) The intention for fasting is valid and the prayer remains valid.
C) The intention for fasting is invalid and the prayer becomes invalid.
D) The prayer becomes nafl instead of fard.

Key Takeaway
Intention for a different genre of worship during another worship is valid and does not invalidate the current act.

Intention Not Required for the Remainder of Worship
Explaining the non-requirement of intention for the remainder of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that intention is not required for the remainder of worship and apply it to scenarios involving mid-prayer intention changes.

Core Idea
Intention at start governs the whole; requiring it continuously would cause undue hardship.

This lesson explores a key maxim from Hanafi fiqh: the non-requirement of intention (niyyah) for the continuation (baqa') of worship. While intention is essential at the beginning, demanding it for every subsequent moment would create hardship (haraj). The text cites Al-Binayah and Al-Qunyah to illustrate the rule and its practical application, including the case where a person mistakenly changes their intention mid-prayer yet the original obligation is fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its basis
The text states that intention is not required for the remainder of prayer due to hardship. Recognize the underlying principle: المشقة تجلب التيسير (hardship brings ease). This is a general rule for all acts of worship.
The basis is talil (reasoning) by hardship, not a direct textual proof.
2
Understand the scope: all acts of worship
The text explicitly extends the rule from prayer to all acts of worship ('بقيّة العبادات'). Note that this applies as long as the act is continuous and the initial intention remains valid.
Exceptions exist if the act is clearly disconnected (e.g., breaking prayer entirely).
3
Analyze the Al-Binayah example
A person starts fard prayer with proper intention, then mistakenly thinks it is nafl and completes it with nafl intention. The ruling: it fulfills the fard because the initial intention governs the whole act.
This shows that the initial intention 'carries through' the entire act; a mere mental shift does not nullify it.
4
Contrast with other schools
This Hanafi position differs from other madhabs (e.g., Shafi'i) that require continuity of intention for validity. Recognize the ikhtilaf and the Hanafi justification: necessity and ease.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in the Hanafi school, a mid-prayer intention change to nafl does not invalidate the fard; in Shafi'i school it might.
5
Apply as a mufti
When issuing a fatwa, use this rule to answer questions about niyyah continuity. For example, if someone asks whether their prayer is valid after doubting their intention, the initial valid intention suffices unless there is a clear break.
Remember: the rule is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school and is relied upon in later fatwa collections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامن : في بَيَانِ عَدَم إِشْتِرَاطهَا فِي الْبَقَاءِ، وَحُكْمِهَا مَعَ كُلِّ رُكْنِ. قَالُوا : فِي الصَّلَاةِ لَا تُشْتَرَطُ النِّيَّةُ فِى الْبَقَاءِ لِلْحَرَج، كَذَا فِي " البنَايَةِ فَكَذَا فِي بَقِيَّةِ الْعِبَادَاتِ، وَفِي القِنْيَةِ لَا تَلْزَمُ نِيَّةُ العِبَادَةِ فِي كُلّ جُزءِ، إِنَّمَا تَلْزَمُ في جُمْلَةِ مَا يَفْعَلُهُ فِي كُلّ حَالٍ، إنتهى . وَفِي الْبِنَايَةِ لَوِ افْتَتَحَ الْمَكْتُوبَةُ، ثُمَّ ظَنَّ أَنَّهَا تَطَوُّع فَأَتَمْهَا عَلَى نِيَّةِ التطوع أَجْزَاتُهُ عَنِ الْمَكْتُوبَةِ.

ترجمه: آٹھویں بحث بقاء میں اس کے شرط نہ ہونے اور ہر رکن میں اس کے حکم کے بیان میں ہے چنانچہ نماز کے متعلق فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ بقاء میں نیت شرط نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ حرج ہے بنایہ میں ایساہی ہے تو بقیہ عبادات کا بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ اور قنیہ میں ہے کہ ہر جز میں عبادت کی نیت لازم نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں منجملہ ضروری ہے جسے بہر حال وہ انجام دے رہا ہو قنیہ کی بات پوری ہوئی۔ بنایہ میں ہے کہ اگر کسی نے فرض نماز شروع کی پھر یہ سمجھا کہ یہ نفل ہے اور اسے نفل کی نیت پر ہی پوری کر دی تو وہ اس کے لئے فرض کی طرف سے کافی ہے۔

تشریح: آٹھویں بحث کا ماحصل یہ ہے کہ عبادت کے آخر تک بقاء نیت ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ جو نیت شروع میں کی گئی ہے اس کا رکن کے ہر جز میں باقی رہنا ضروری نہیں ہے مجموعی اعتبار سے نیت کافی ہے حرج کی وجہ سے آخر تک بقاء نیت کو ضروری قرار نہیں دیا گیا۔

 قالوا في الصلواة لاتشترط النية فى البقاء للحرج كذا فى البناية وشرطت في ابتدائها (البنايه ج ۳، ص : ۱۳۸)

ولو افتتح المكتوبة فظن انها تطوع فاتمها على نية التطوع فالصلوة هي المكتوبة لان الشرط قران العزيمة باول العبادة اذ قرانها بجميعها متعذر. (البناية ٣، ص: ۴۲)
The eighth: Concerning the explanation of its non-requirement in the remainder, and its ruling with every pillar. They said: In prayer, intention is not required for the remainder due to hardship. Likewise in Al-Binayah, and likewise in the rest of the acts of worship. And in Al-Qunyah: The intention of worship is not binding in every part; rather it is binding in the entirety of what he does in every state. End. And in Al-Binayah: If he started the obligatory prayer, then thought it was supererogatory and completed it with the intention of supererogatory, it suffices him for the obligatory. Translation: The eighth discussion regarding it not being a condition in the remainder and its ruling with every pillar. Therefore, concerning prayer, the jurists say that intention is not a condition in the remainder because of hardship. Likewise in Al-Binayah, and likewise for the rest of acts of worship. And in Al-Qunyah: Intention of worship is not necessary in every part; rather it is necessary in the totality of what he does in every state. The speech of Al-Qunyah is complete. In Al-Binayah: If someone started an obligatory prayer, then thought it was supererogatory and completed it with the intention of supererogatory, it suffices for the obligatory. Commentary: The summary of the eighth discussion is that continuity of intention until the end of worship is not necessary; rather the intention made at the beginning, its persistence in every part of the pillar is not required; collectively the intention is sufficient. Due to hardship, continuity of intention till the end is not deemed necessary.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling on the non-requirement of intention for the remainder of worship. The text opens with the eighth discussion: intention is not required for the remainder of prayer (and by extension all acts of worship) due to hardship. Two sources are cited: Al-Binayah and Al-Qunyah. Al-Binayah's example illustrates that if a person starts a fard prayer, later mistakenly changes intention to nafl, yet completes it, it counts as the fard because the initial valid intention governs the whole act. The rule is based on the principle that requiring intention for every moment would be burdensome; rather, the initial intention suffices. This applies across all acts of worship (salat, sawm, etc.) unless there is a clear disconnection.

Key Terms
بقاء (baqa'): The remaining/continuation of the act of worship after its commencement
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty that justifies leniency in legal rulings
افتتح (iftataha): To begin/commence an act of worship, especially prayer with takbirat al-ihram

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the eighth discussion, why is intention not required for the remainder of prayer?
A) Because prayer is not valid without continuous intention.
B) Because hardship would result from requiring it at every moment.
C) Because intention is never required in worship.
D) Because the sahaba did not do it.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the initial intention at the start of worship suffices for the entire act; requiring its continuity at every moment is not necessary due to hardship.

Comprehensive Components of Niyyah from Al-Mujtaba
Definition of detailed niyyah components from rare transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four components of niyyah mentioned in Al-Mujtaba and distinguish their authority level (nawadir vs. zahir al-riwayah).

Core Idea
The rare transmission from Al-Mujtaba prescribes four intentions, but only the simple niyyah is obligatory in the relied-upon position.

This passage from Al-Mujtaba presents a detailed definition of intention (niyyah) that includes humility, obedience, seeking reward, and religious reform. The author flags it as 'gharib' (rare), indicating it is not the standard Hanafi position. In this lesson, you will learn the components and understand their limited authority in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four components
List the four types of intention mentioned: niyyat al-‘ibadah (utmost humility and submission), niyyat al-ta‘ah (doing what Allah commands), niyyat al-qurbah (seeking reward through hardship), and intention of religious reform (doing what is rationally closest to obligation and farthest from sin).
Each component has a distinct focus: humility, obedience, reward, and moral improvement.
2
Classify the authority level
Recognize that the text introduces this as 'min al-gharib' (from the strange/rare). In Hanafi usul, this source belongs to the nawadir (rare transmissions) of Imam Muhammad, not the six core books of zahir al-riwayah.
Nawadir have lower authority than zahir al-riwayah and are generally not mufta bihi when they conflict.
3
Contrast with the standard Hanafi position
The standard Hanafi position only requires the simple intention of the specific act (e.g., 'I intend to pray fajr'). The detailed components from Al-Mujtaba are not obligatory but may be recommended for deeper mindfulness.
This distinction is crucial for fatwa: the mufta bihi is the simple niyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنَ الْغَرِيْبِ مَا فِي الْمُجْتَبى : وَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ نِيَّةِ الْعِبَادَةِ، وَهِيَ التَّذَلُّلُ وَالْحُضُوْعُ عَلَى أَبْلَغَ الْوَجُوْهِ، وَنِيَّةِ الطَّاعَةِ، وَهِي فِعْلُ مَا أَرَادَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَىٰ مِنْهُ وَنِيَّةُ الْقُرْبَةِ وَهِيَ طَلَبُ الثَّوَابِ بِالْمُشَقَّةِ فِي فِعْلِهَا ، وَيَنْوِيَ أَنَّهُ يَفْعَلُهَا مَصْلِحَةً لَهُ فِي دِينِهِ، بِأَنْ يَكُونَ أَقْرَبَ إِلَى مَا وَجَبَ عِنْدَهُ عَقْلًا مِنَ الْفِعْلِ وَأَدَاءِ الْأَمَانَةِ، وَأَبْعَدَ عَمَّا حَرُمَ عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الظُّلْمِ وَكُفْرَانِ النِّعْمَةِ.

ترجمہ: اور مجتبی میں ایک نادر مسئلہ ہے کہ عبادت کی نیت ضروری ہے اور وہ پورے طور پر کمتری و عاجزی کا اظہار ہے اور طاعت کی نیت ضروری ہے اور وہ اس امر کو انجام دیتا ہے جس کا اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس سے مطالبہ کیا ہے اور قربت کی نیت ضروری ہے اور وہ اس کو انجام دینے میں مشقت پر ثواب طلب کرنا ہے نیز یہ نیت کرے کہ وہ اس عبادت کو دین میں اپنی اصلاح کے لئے کر رہا ہے۔ اور یہ کہ وہ اس کے بہت قریب ہو جائے جو اس کے نزدیک عقلاً واجب ہے یعنی فعل اور اداء امانت اور اس سے کافی دور ہو جائے جو اس پر حرام ہے یعنی ظلم اور نعمت کی ناشکری ۔

تشریح: بعض لوگوں نے ایک عجیب و غریب نیت بتلائی ہے اس نیت کو مجتبی میں نقل کیا گیا ہے عبادت کی نیت کرنا لازم ہے اور عبادت نام ہے آخری درجہ کا خضوع اور ذلت اختیار کرنے کا۔ اطاعت کی نیت کرے اور اطاعت کا مفہوم یہ ہے کہ جس فعل کو اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس سے چاہا وہ اسے انجام دے قربت کی نیت کرے اور اس کا مفہوم یہ ہے کہ اس کو انجام دینے میں پیش آنے والی مشقت پر ثواب کا طالب رہے اور یہ بھی نیت ہو کہ وہ اس عبادت کو دینی مصلحت و فائدہ کے لئے کر رہا ہے اور یہ بھی نیت ہو کہ عقلاً اس کے اوپر اس وقت وجوب کے اعتبار سے جو فعل اقرب ہے وہ اسے کر رہا ہے اور ظلم و کفران نعمت سے دور رہنے کی نیت کرے۔
And among the strange things is what is in Al-Mujtaba: The intention of worship is necessary, and it is utmost humility and submissiveness; and the intention of obedience, which is doing what Allah Ta'ala wants from him; and the intention of closeness, which is seeking reward with hardship in performing it; and he intends that he does it as a reform for himself in his religion, such that it becomes closer to what is rationally obligatory for him of action and fulfillment of trust, and farther from what is forbidden to him of oppression and ingratitude for blessings. Translation: And in Al-Mujtaba there is a rare issue: Intention of worship is necessary, and it is utmost expression of humility and lowliness; and intention of obedience is necessary, and it is to perform the action that Allah required from him; and intention of closeness is necessary, and it is seeking reward for the hardship in performing it; also he should intend that he is performing this worship for the reform of his religion. And that he becomes very close to what is rationally obligatory for him, i.e., action and fulfillment of trust, and becomes far from what is forbidden to him, i.e., oppression and ingratitude. Commentary: Some people have described a strange intention; this intention is narrated in Al-Mujtaba. Intending the worship is necessary, and worship is the name for adopting the utmost humility and lowliness. Intending obedience is necessary, and the meaning of obedience is that he performs the action that Allah wanted from him. Intending closeness is necessary, and its meaning is that he seeks reward for the hardship encountered in doing it. Also, he should intend that he is doing this worship for religious benefit and advantage, and that he is doing what is rationally closest to obligation, and intends to stay away from oppression and ingratitude.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
Passage type: Definition and expansion of the components of niyyah. This passage from Al-Mujtaba (a rare or 'strange' transmission) provides a detailed prescription for intention in worship. It lists four necessary elements: (1) intention of worship (niyyat al-‘ibadah), which is utmost humility and submission; (2) intention of obedience (niyyat al-ta‘ah), i.e., performing what Allah commands; (3) intention of closeness (niyyat al-qurbah), i.e., seeking reward through hardship; (4) intention of personal religious reform, i.e., doing the action that is closest to what is rationally obligatory and farthest from sin. This level of detail is 'strange' because the standard Hanafi position only requires the simple intention of the specific act (e.g., 'I intend to pray fajr'). The commentator explains that some scholars transmitted this detailed intention, but it is not required for validity; it is a recommended depth of mindfulness. The authority weight here is Nawadir, as indicated by 'gharib' (rare).

Key Terms
نیة العبادة (niyyat al-‘ibadah): Intention of worship defined as utmost humility and submission
نیة الطاعة (niyyat al-ta‘ah): Intention of obedience: doing what Allah wills from the person
نیة القربة (niyyat al-qurbah): Intention of closeness: seeking reward through hardship in the act
الغريب (al-gharib): Rare or strange transmission

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from Al-Mujtaba, which of the following is NOT a component of intention?
A) Intention of worship (humility)
B) Intention of obedience (doing what Allah wants)
C) Intention of closeness (seeking reward)
D) Intention of worldly benefit (dunyanawi)

Key Takeaway
The rare transmission from Al-Mujtaba lists four detailed intentions, but the mufta bihi only requires the simple specific intention; the detailed components are not obligatory.

Initial Intention Suffices for Prayer: The Maxim of Niyyah and Hardship
Ruling that intention is required only at start of prayer, not continuously

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim that intention is required only at the beginning of worship due to hardship, and identify the scope of this ruling in multi-part acts of worship.

Core Idea
Intention at the start of prayer suffices because requiring it throughout would cause hardship.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling on intention (niyyah) in prayer: the intention is only required at the beginning, not continuously. This is based on the principle that maintaining intention for every moment would cause undue hardship (haraj). The passage from al-Binaya illustrates this with a practical example: if someone starts an obligatory prayer with the correct intention but later mistakenly thinks it is a supererogatory prayer, the prayer remains valid as obligatory. This ruling eases the worship experience and prevents invalidations due to fleeting thoughts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the ruling: intention is required at the beginning of prayer, but not for the duration. The text explicitly says 'latishtarti al-niyyah fi al-baqa' li al-haraj' — intention is not required for the remainder due to hardship.
This is the core of the lesson.
2
Understand the 'illa (legal cause)
The reason for not requiring continuous intention is hardship (haraj). The Shariah lightens obligations when maintaining them would be excessively difficult. This connects to the major maxim 'al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir' (hardship brings ease).
Haraj includes the natural distraction of the mind during a lengthy act.
3
Apply the example from al-Binaya
Consider the scenario: a person begins an obligatory prayer (e.g., Fajr) with the correct intention, but during the prayer he mistakenly thinks he is praying a supererogatory prayer and completes it with that belief. The prayer remains valid as obligatory because the initial intention governs the entire act as long as no contradictory action is performed.
This demonstrates the practical effect of the ruling.
4
Identify the exception
The ruling holds as long as the worshiper does not perform an action that explicitly breaks the original intention, such as deliberately intending to leave the prayer or performing an act that nullifies it (e.g., talking, eating). In such cases, the initial intention no longer suffices.
The exception preserves the requirement of intention for valid worship.
5
Extend to other acts of worship
This ruling applies to any multi-part act of worship, such as Hajj or Umrah. For example, if someone starts Tawaf with the intention of a specific type (e.g., ifrad) but later thinks it is another, the original intention holds if no contradictory action is taken.
The principle is general beyond prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا في الصلواة لاتشترط النية فى البقاء للحرج كذا فى البناية وشرطت في ابتدائها (البنايه ج ۳، ص : ١٣٨) بنایہ میں ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے فرض کی نیت سے نماز شروع کی تھی جب نماز شروع کر دی تو دل میں اسے نفل سمجھ لیا تو اس سے کوئی حرج نہیں یہ نماز فرض ہی ادا ہوگی اس کی شروع کی ہی نیست معتبر ہوگی اور درمیان میں دل میں ادھر ادھر کے خیال آنے سے کوئی فرق نہیں پڑے گا جب تک اس کی طرف سے کوئی ایسا فعل نہ پایا جائے جس کے ذریعہ وہ پہلی نماز سے نکل جائے۔ ولو افتتح المكتوبة فظن انها تطوع فاتمها على نية التطوع فالصلوة هي المكتوبة لان الشرط قران العزيمة باول العبادة اذ قرانها بجميعها متعذر. (البناية ٣، ص: ۴۲)
They said regarding prayer: intention is not required for the duration due to hardship, as in al-Binaya, and it is required at its beginning. In al-Binaya it is mentioned: if a person begins prayer with the intention of an obligatory prayer, then during the prayer he thinks it is a supererogatory prayer, there is no harm; the prayer is still considered obligatory. His initial intention is valid, and thoughts that come to mind in between do not matter as long as he does not perform an action that would take him out of the first prayer. And if he begins an obligatory prayer but thinks it is supererogatory and completes it with the intention of supererogatory prayer, the prayer is still obligatory because the condition is that the resolve is linked to the beginning of the worship, since linking it to the entire worship is impossible (al-Binaya 3:42).
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi madhhab regarding the scope of intention (niyyah) in prayer. The key principle is that intention is only required at the commencement of the prayer, not continuously throughout, due to the difficulty (haraj) of maintaining it. The text from al-Binaya illustrates this with an example: if one starts an obligatory prayer with the correct intention but later mistakenly thinks it is a supererogatory prayer, the prayer remains valid as obligatory because the original intention suffices. The legal reasoning ('illa) is that it is impracticable to require intention for every part of the prayer. Therefore, the intention at the beginning is deemed to accompany the entire act as long as no contradictory action is performed that would break the prayer.

Key Terms
نیة (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship.
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty that is accommodated by the Shariah to lighten obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling regarding intention in a multi-act worship like prayer?
A) Intention must be renewed for every act
B) Intention at the beginning suffices for the entire prayer
C) Intention is not required at all
D) Intention is only required for the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Intention is only required at the start of prayer; the initial resolve governs the entire act, easing the burden on the worshiper.

Niyyah Extension: The Hanafi Rule that One Intention Suffices for Multi-Act Worship
Presentation of a rare view and the relied-upon rule on niyyah extension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that initial niyyah extends to all subsequent actions in a multi-act worship and identify when a new intention is needed.

Core Idea
One intention at the start covers the whole prayer; renew only if you intend a different act.

This passage presents a rare view requiring intention in every rukn, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that a single intention at the beginning suffices. This is a key qa'ida in Hanafi fiqh that facilitates worship. We will analyze the rule, its evidence, and its application to tawaf and wuquf to understand when a new intention is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rare view
Read the first part: al-Mujtaba requires intention of worship, obedience, closeness, and reform, and states that these intentions must be present from start to end, especially at each pillar (rukn).
This view is labeled 'gharib' (strange/rare).
2
State the relied-upon rule
Note the phrase 'al-madhab al-mu'tamad' – the relied-upon madhhab is that for worship consisting of multiple actions, a single intention at the beginning suffices and extends to all subsequent actions.
This is based on the principle of ease (haraj).
3
Determine the exception
Check the condition 'illa idha nawa bi ba'd al-af'al ghayr ma wudi'a lahu' – the extension fails if one intends something other than what the action is prescribed for.
Example: if during prayer, one intends to wave as a greeting, that action requires a separate intention.
4
Apply to tawaf and wuquf
Compare: tawaf seeking a debtor is invalid because it requires a specific intention of worship; wuquf at 'Arafat with the same worldly intention is valid because the intention of ihram covers it.
Al-Zayla'i's distinction: tawaf occurs after partial tahlul (exit from ihram) so it needs its own intention, while wuquf is within the ihram state.
5
Extract the qa'ida
Formulate the rule in Arabic: يُكتَفَى بالنِّيَّةِ في أوَّلِ العِبادةِ ذاتِ الأفعالِ وتنسحبُ على بقيَّتِها إلا إذا نوى ببعضِ الأفعالِ غيرَ ما وُضِعَ له.
This qa'ida applies to all multi-act worships (prayer, hajj, etc.).

Source Text

ہے کہ وہ عبادت جو افعال پر مشتمل ہو اس کے شروع میں نیت کافی ہے ہر فعل میں اس کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس کے اس پر پھیل جانے پر اکتفا کرتے ہوئے بجز اس صورت کے کہ کوئی بعض افعال سے اس کی نیت کرے جس کے لئے اس کو وضع نہیں کیا گیا۔ سا ہوا۔ تشریح پھر اول نماز سے آخر نماز تک خصوصاً ایک رکن سے دوسرے رکن کی طرف منتقل ہوتے وقت نہینہ کا استحضار ضروری ہے ماحصل یہ ہے کہ نیت عبادت کا ہر رکن میں استحضار ہونا ضروری ہے اور نقل و فرض دونوں کا اس سلسلہ میں ایک حکم ہے مگر نفل میں کچھ ہلکا پن اور سہولت ہے ظاہر ہے کہ عام آدمی اتنی لمی نیت نہیں کر پائے گا اس لئے معتمد مذہب یہی ہے کہ افعال والی عبادت کے شروع میں نیت کا ہونا کافی ہے ہر ہر فعل کے اندر نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ہاں جب کسی فعل سے موضوع لہ کے غیر کی نیت کرے تو پھر نیت کا اس کو کرتے وقت ہونالازم ہے۔ تنبيه: یہ بات ذہن میں مستحضر رہنی چاہئے کہ جو ہم نے یہ کہا کہ جو نیت کر لی جائے وہ آخر یک باقی رہتی ہے یہ مسئلہ تب ہے جبکہ وہ اس کے ارکان و لوازمات میں سے ہو ورنہ اگر اس کے ارکان ولوازمات میں سے نہ ہوتو پھر متفل نیت کرنا پڑے گی جیسے سجدہ سہو اسی لئے سجدہ تلاوت سے اعراض نہ ہوگا کیونکہ تلاوت نماز کے لوازمات میں ہے ؟ لہذا تلاوت کی نیت خود بخود ہوگئی۔ قَالُوا الطَّوَافَ طَالِباً لِغَرِيْمٍ لَا يُجْزِتُهُ، وَلَوْ وَقَفَ كَذَالِكَ بِعَرَفَاتٍ أَجْزَاهُ وَقَدَّمْنَاهُ وَالْفَرْقَ أَنَّ الطَّوَافَ عَهْدُ قُرْبَةٍ مُسْتَقِلَّةٍ، بِخِلَافِ الْوُقُوْفِ وَفَرَّقَ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ بَيْنَهُمَا بِفَرْقٍ آخَرَ، وَهُوَ أَنَّ النِّيَّةَ عِندَ الإِحْرَامِ تَضَمَّنَتْ جَمِيعَ مَا يُفْعَلُ فِي الْأَحْرَامِ، فَلَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى تَجْدِيدِ النِّيَّةِ، وَالطَّوَافُ يَقَعُ بَعْدَ التَّحَلَّلِ، وَفِي الْإِحْرَامِ مِنْ وَجْهِ، فَاشْتَرِطَ فِيْهِ أَصْلُ النِّيَّةِ لَا تَعْيِينُ الْجِهَةِ، إنتهى.
And among the strange (reports) is what is in al-Mujtaba: There must be intention of worship, which is utmost humility and lowliness, and intention of obedience, which is doing what Allah has required of him, and intention of seeking closeness, which is seeking reward through hardship in performing it, and he intends that he does it as a reform for his religion, so that he becomes closer to what is rationally obligatory in terms of action and fulfilling trust, and farther from what is forbidden to him of oppression and ingratitude for blessings. Translation: And in al-Mujtaba there is a rare case: that intention of worship is necessary, and it is the expression of complete humility and lowliness; intention of obedience is necessary, and it is to do what Allah has demanded of him; intention of closeness is necessary, and it is to seek reward for the hardship in performing it; also he should intend that he is doing this worship for the reform of his religion, and that he becomes very close to what is rationally obligatory for him, i.e., action and fulfillment of trust, and very far from what is forbidden to him, i.e., oppression and ingratitude for blessings. Explanation: Some people have mentioned a strange intention, transmitted in al-Mujtaba: it is necessary to intend worship, and worship is the ultimate degree of humility and lowliness. He should intend obedience, and the meaning of obedience is that he performs the action that Allah has desired from him. He should intend closeness, and its meaning is that he seeks reward for the hardship faced in performing it. And he should intend that he is performing this worship for religious benefit and advantage, and that rationally, he is performing the act that is closest to what is obligatory upon him, and he intends to stay away from oppression and ingratitude for blessings. Then these intentions from the beginning of prayer to its end, especially at the transition from one pillar to another: there must be intention of worship in every pillar, and supererogatory is like obligatory in this, except in one respect: that in supererogatory prayers he intends that they are a favor (lutf) for the obligatory prayers and a facilitation for them. End. The summary is that the relied-upon madhhab is that for worship consisting of multiple actions, one intention at its beginning is sufficient, and there is no need for it in every action, relying on its extension over them, except if he intends by some actions something other than what they are legislated for. Translation: Then these intentions remain from the beginning of prayer to the end, especially when moving from one pillar to another. It is learned that intention of worship is required in every pillar, and in this, supererogatory is like obligatory except in one case: that in supererogatory prayers he intends that they are for betterment and facilitation of the obligatory. Al-Hasil: The relied-upon madhhab is that for a worship consisting of actions, intention at its beginning is sufficient; there is no need for it in every action, relying on its extension over them, except when he intends by some actions something other than that for which it was prescribed. Explanation: Then from the beginning of prayer to the end, especially at transitions, the presence of intention is necessary. The gist is that the presence of intention of worship in every pillar is necessary, and supererogatory and obligatory have the same ruling in this regard, but in supererogatory there is some leniency and ease. It is obvious that ordinary people cannot have such a long intention. Therefore, the relied-upon madhhab is that for worship consisting of actions, having intention at its beginning is sufficient; there is no need for intention in every action. Yes, when he intends by some action something other than the purpose for which it was prescribed, then intention at that time is necessary. Caution: This should be kept in mind: that what we said, that once intention is made it remains until the end, this is when the action is among its pillars and essentials; otherwise, if it is not among its pillars and essentials, then he will have to make a separate intention, like the prostration of forgetfulness. For this reason, if he turns away from the prostration of recitation, it does not harm, because recitation is among the essentials of prayer, so the intention for recitation is automatically included. They said: If one performs tawaf seeking a debtor, it is not valid; but if he stands similarly at 'Arafat, it is valid. We have presented this. The difference is that tawaf is an independent act of worship, unlike standing (at 'Arafat). And al-Zayla'i distinguished between them with another difference: that the intention at ihram includes all that is done in the state of ihram, so there is no need to renew intention; but tawaf occurs after partial tahlul, and it is like ihram in some respect, so for it the basic intention is required, not specification of direction. End.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage presents a rare (gharib) view from al-Mujtaba that requires an elaborate intention for worship, including intention of humility, obedience, and seeking reward. It then states that these intentions must be maintained from the beginning to the end of prayer, specifically at each transition between pillars. However, the text then clarifies that the relied-upon madhhab (al-madhab al-mu'tamad) is that a single intention at the beginning of a multi-act worship is sufficient, and it extends to all subsequent acts except if one performs an action with a different intention. The passage concludes with a comparison between tawaf and wuquf at 'Arafat, explaining why tawaf requires a separate intention while wuquf does not, because tawaf is an independent act of worship after partial tahlul, whereas wuquf is included within the intention of ihram. This illustrates the principle that intention at the beginning of an act suffices for all its components, but a new worship requires a new intention.

Key Terms
عبادة (ibadah): Act of worship involving utmost humility and submission.
نیة (niyyah): Intention of worship, obedience, and seeking reward; also intention of performing the act as a means of religious reform and closeness to what is rationally obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when is a new intention required in a multi-act worship?
A) At the beginning of the worship
B) At every pillar (rukn)
C) Only when one intends a different act than what is prescribed
D) Never, intention is not required

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi rule is that a single intention at the start of a multi-act worship covers all subsequent acts, requiring renewal only if a contrary intention arises.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Intention Spreads Over All Actions in Worship
Defining the rule that initial intention covers all subsequent actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida of insihab al-niyya to determine when a single intention suffices for a multi-action act of worship and identify the istithna'at.

Core Idea
In multi-action worship, one intention at the start covers all actions unless a contrary intention arises.

This lesson examines a foundational legal maxim (qa'ida sughra) from the Hanafi tradition: that in acts of worship composed of multiple actions, the initial intention suffices for the whole act. The principle of 'insihab al-niyya' (the covering of intention) is a practical facilitation, especially for worshippers who may struggle to renew intention for every movement. Understanding this maxim is essential for a mufti when ruling on the validity of prayers or other rituals where the worshipper's focus may lapse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core qawida
Extract the exact wording of the maxim from the passage: intention at the beginning of a multi-action worship suffices and spreads over all actions.
The relied-upon madhhab (mu'tamad) is stated clearly.
2
Clarify the scope
Determine which acts of worship the rule applies to — primarily prayer, but also Hajj and other rituals with multiple actions.
The text mentions prayer specifically, but the rule is general.
3
Recognize the istithna' (exception)
Identify the condition that breaks the coverage: if the worshipper intends something other than the worship for a specific action, that action requires its own intention.
Mere distraction does not break coverage; only explicit contrary intention does.
4
Distinguish essential vs. non-essential actions
The rule applies only to actions that are pillars or essentials (arkan wa lawazim). For non-essential actions like sajda sahw, a separate intention is needed.
The text notes this in the tanbih (warning).
5
Apply to a fatwa scenario
Use the qawida to analyze a real case: a person starts fard prayer with intention, then during a rukn intends a nafl action. Apply the rule to see if the action counts.
Practice applying the istithna' correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ هذا النِّيَّاتُ مِنْ أَوَّلِ الصَّلَاةِ إلى آخِرِهَا خُصُوصًا عِندَ الانْتِقَالِ مِنْ رُكْنٍ إِلى رُكْنٍ، فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ نِيَّةِ الْعِبَادَةِ فِي كُلِّ رُكْنٍ وَالنَّفْلُ كَالْفَرْضِ فِيْهَا إِلَّا فِي وَجْهِ وَاحِدٍ، وَهُوَ أَنْ يُنْوِي فِي النَّوَافِلِ أَنَّهَا لُطْفٌ فِى الْفَرَائِضِ وَتَسْهِيْلٌ لَهَا، إِنْتَهَى وَالْحَاصِلُ أَنَّ الْمَذْهَبَ الْمُعْتَمَدَ أَنَّ الْعِبَادَةَ الَّتِي ذَاتَ أَفْعَالٍ يَكْتَفِي بِالنِّيَّةِ فِي أَوَّلِهَا، وَلَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَيْهَا فِي كُلِّ فِعْلِ إِكْتِفَاءً بِإِنْسِحَابِهَا عَلَيْهَا إِلَّا إِذَا نَوَى بِبَعْضِ الْأَفْعَالِ غَيْرَ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ.
ترجمه: پھر یہ نیتیں نماز کے شروع سے آخر تک بالخصوص ایک رکن سے دوسرے رکن کی طرف منتقل ہوتے وقت باقی رہیں معلوم ہوا کہ ہر رکن میں نیت عبادت ضروری ہے اور اس میں نفل فرض کے مانند ہے بجز ایک صورت کے اور وہ یہ کہ نوافل میں یہ نیت کرے کہ یہ فرائض میں عمدگی اور سہولت پیدا کرنے کے لئے [؟میں مجتبی کا کام عمل میلہ] الحاصل معتمد مذہب یہ ہے کہ وہ عبادت جو افعال پر مشتمل ہو اس کے شروع میں نیت کافی ہے ہر فعل میں اس کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس کے اس پر پھیل جانے پر اکتفا کرتے ہوئے بجز اس صورت کے کہ کوئی بعض افعال سے اس کی نیت کرے جس کے لئے اس کو وضع نہیں کیا گیا۔
تشریح پھر اول نماز سے آخر نماز تک خصوصاً ایک رکن سے دوسرے رکن کی طرف منتقل ہوتے وقت نہینہ کا استحضار ضروری ہے ماحصل یہ ہے کہ نیت عبادت کا ہر رکن میں استحضار ہونا ضروری ہے اور نقل و فرض دونوں کا اس سلسلہ میں ایک حکم ہے مگر نفل میں کچھ ہلکا پن اور سہولت ہے ظاہر ہے کہ عام آدمی اتنی لمی نیت نہیں کر پائے گا اس لئے معتمد مذہب یہی ہے کہ افعال والی عبادت کے شروع میں نیت کا ہونا کافی ہے ہر ہر فعل کے اندر نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ہاں جب کسی فعل سے موضوع لہ کے غیر کی نیت کرے تو پھر نیت کا اس کو کرتے وقت ہونالازم ہے۔
تنبيه: یہ بات ذہن میں مستحضر رہنی چاہئے کہ جو ہم نے یہ کہا کہ جو نیت کر لی جائے وہ آخر یک باقی رہتی ہے یہ مسئلہ تب ہے جبکہ وہ اس کے ارکان و لوازمات میں سے ہو ورنہ اگر اس کے ارکان ولوازمات میں سے نہ ہوتو پھر متفل نیت کرنا پڑے گی جیسے سجدہ سہو اسی لئے سجدہ تلاوت سے اعراض نہ ہوگا کیونکہ تلاوت نماز کے لوازمات میں ہے [؟] لہذا تلاوت کی نیت خود بخود ہوگئی۔
Then these intentions from the beginning of prayer to its end, especially at the transition from one pillar to another, so intention of worship is necessary in every pillar, and voluntary (nafl) is like obligatory (fard) in this except in one aspect: that one intends in voluntary prayers that they are a grace and facilitation for the obligatory prayers. End. The gist is that the relied-upon madhhab is that in a worship consisting of actions, intention at its beginning suffices and there is no need for it in every action, relying on its covering (insihab) over them, unless one intends with some actions something other than what they were placed for. Translation: Then these intentions from the beginning of prayer to its end, especially at transition from one pillar to another, remain; it is known that intention of worship is necessary in every pillar, and voluntary is like obligatory in this except in one case: that in voluntary prayers one intends that they are for perfection and facilitation of the obligatory. The summary: the relied-upon madhhab is that worship consisting of actions, intention at its beginning is sufficient, there is no need for it in every action, relying on its spreading over them, except when one intends with some actions something other than what it was placed for. Explanation: Then from the beginning of prayer to its end, especially at transition from one pillar to another, presence of intention is necessary. The gist: presence of intention of worship is necessary in every pillar, and voluntary and obligatory have the same ruling in this, but in voluntary there is some leniency and ease. It is obvious that a common person cannot make such a long intention, so the relied-upon madhhab is that in worship consisting of actions, intention at the beginning is sufficient; there is no need for intention in every action. Yes, when one intends with some action something other than what it was placed for, then intention at the time of that action is necessary. Note: It should be kept in mind that what we said, that intention once made remains until the end, this is when the action is among its pillars or essentials; otherwise, if it is not from its pillars or essentials, then a separate intention will be needed, like prostration of forgetfulness (sajda sahw). Similarly, turning away from prostration of recitation (sajda tilawat) does not invalidate because recitation is among the essentials of prayer [?]; therefore the intention for recitation is automatically made.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage defines a key rule about intention (niyya) in acts of worship that consist of multiple actions, such as prayer. The author begins by stating that in prayer, intention must be present from the start and especially when moving from one pillar to another. However, the relied-upon position of the Hanafi madhhab simplifies this: once the worshipper makes an intention at the beginning of the act, it spreads over all subsequent actions unless a contrary intention arises. For example, if during prayer one intentionally intends something else for a specific action, then that action requires a new intention. The text adds a nuance for voluntary prayers: they are considered a grace and facilitation for obligatory prayers, so the intention is slightly lighter. A note (tanbih) follows: the rule that intention covers all actions only applies if the actions are part of the worship's pillars or essentials. If an action is not an essential part (like sajda sahw), a separate intention is needed. The example of sajda tilawat shows that if it occurs during prayer, no separate intention is needed because recitation is an essential part of prayer.

Key Terms
نية (niyya): Intention that distinguishes acts of worship from habit, and differentiates between different types of worship.
انطباق النية (insihab al-niyya): The spreading or covering of the initial intention over all subsequent actions of the same worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi madhhab, for a multi-action worship like prayer, when is intention required?
A) At the beginning of each action
B) Only at the beginning, and it covers all actions unless a contrary intention occurs
C) Only at the end of the worship
D) Intention is not required in voluntary prayers

Key Takeaway
In multi-action worship, one intention at the start suffices for all essential actions unless a contrary intention for a specific action occurs.
